\section{PROJECT: TECT --- Master Contents for Continuation (Carrier Acceptance Stage)}

\section{Current Main Goal}

The current main goal is no longer to derive isolated support lemmas.
The actual frontier is now the \emph{full practical acceptance theorem} for the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{carrier acceptance (Gates 2--3)}
\quad+\quad
\text{mass protection (Gate 4)}.
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the immediate target is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{prove that the current microscopic branch is a viable massless Dirac carrier,}
}
\end{equation}
namely
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\end{equation}

This is now the nonredundant frontier.

\section{Working Microscopic Branch}

The strongest current explicit working microscopic branch remains

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi,P]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\end{equation}

This is still a \emph{working microscopic ansatz}, not yet claimed to be the unique final complete TECT microscopic action.

\section{Fixed Reduction Layer}

The exact light/heavy reduction skeleton is already fixed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\mathrm{eff}}=L-KH^{-1}K^\dagger.
}
\end{equation}

In the current Bloch/Class II realization:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k),
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k),
\qquad
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X.
}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X(k)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Shell Projection and Coefficient Extraction}

The shell-projected operator is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}\,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\,\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\end{equation}

The low-slot projector is spectrally defined by

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*=\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma (z-H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0))^{-1}\,dz.
}
\end{equation}

The projected transport matrices are

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_i
=
P_*
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}
P_*.
}
\end{equation}

In the adapted frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\),

\begin{equation}
M_\parallel=\hat n_iM_i,
\qquad
M_1=e_{1i}M_i,
\qquad
M_2=e_{2i}M_i.
\end{equation}

Under the locked Pauli selection rule,

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\qquad
M_1=\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2=\alpha\sigma_2-\beta\sigma_1.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the reduced coefficients are extracted by

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact Normalization Layer}

The exact overlap-normalization layer is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_\parallel g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O,
}
\end{equation}
where \(C_\parallel\) is the same longitudinal Bloch overlap normalization previously denoted by \(C_c\).

So

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_\parallel},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\end{equation}

The final microscopic calibration frontier is still the explicit evaluation of

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O).
}
\end{equation}

\section{Gate 1: Remote-Gap Support Theorem}

The support gate remains

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\end{equation}

The benchmark side is already reduced to explicit finite objects, including the same-shell non-enriched Hermitian eigenvalue problem.
The residual side is decomposed into transport, tail, and diagonal pieces.

Current honest status:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 is structurally closed and reduced to finite explicit verification.}
}
\end{equation}

It is no longer the main conceptual frontier.

\section{Gate 2: Longitudinal Survival}

\section{Gate 2A: Branch-Sensitive Longitudinal Structure}

The exact branch-sensitive longitudinal parameterization is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\end{equation}

In the solved lowest-order complete realization:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore Branch A is absent in the current solved local class, and the practical longitudinal route is forced to Branch B.

\section{Gate 2B: Primitive Longitudinal Source}

The primitive commutator-square seed is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the primitive longitudinal transport block is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel),\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\end{equation}

Projecting to the shell-localized low modes gives

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Gate 2C: OO-Candidate Interpretation}

Under the current blockwise working interpretation, the primitive longitudinal carrier is assigned to the \(OO\) candidate block:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the transport-level longitudinal problem is reduced to the single finite extraction

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0\ ?
}
\end{equation}

and then

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Gate 2D: Full Practical Verdict}

The strongest practical Gate-2 sufficient condition is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

Equivalent one-mediator Branch-B form:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{

=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3.
}
\end{equation}

Hence, practically,

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Gate 3: Transverse Survival}

\section{Gate 3A: Reduced Transverse Witness}

The reduced transverse coefficients are

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\end{equation}

So the transport-side transverse pass condition is exactly

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\end{equation}

\section{Gate 3B: Honest Microscopic Frontier}

The naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) shortcut fails because

\begin{equation}
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)
+
(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
=0.
\end{equation}

Therefore the honest microscopic frontier is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Gate 3C: Explicit Folded-Bragg Class II Compression}

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch,

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q'),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\end{equation}

In the minimal first-shell-dominant reduction this becomes

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

This is the strongest practical working-branch sufficient test.

After Bloch calibration,

\Longrightarrow

\section{Integrated Gate 2--3 Carrier Acceptance Theorem}

Combining the practical Gate-2 and Gate-3 verdicts, we obtain the strongest current carrier-level acceptance theorem before mass protection:

If both \eqref{carrier-long} and \eqref{carrier-trans} hold, then

\boxed{

\qquad

}
\end{equation}
so the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is accepted as a viable microscopic \emph{carrier} for an anisotropic massless Dirac block.

Equivalent compact one-mediator form:

assuming the nonzero overlap data

\section{Full Practical Accept/Reject Theorem for the Refined Locked \(+\) Class II Branch}

\section{Goal}

The current frontier is no longer the isolated carrier theorem or the isolated mass-protection theorem.
Both ingredients are already closed separately at the theorem/reduction level.
The correct next step is to attach Gate 4 to the integrated Gate 2--3 carrier theorem and state the full practical accept/reject theorem for the present refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch.

\section{Fixed carrier-side data}

The exact shell-reduced infrared symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:full_accept_A1}
\end{equation}
Hence the carrier-level nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:full_accept_nondeg}
\end{equation}

For the doubled shell block, the exact constant Dirac-mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
}
\label{eq:full_accept_mass_space}
\end{equation}

The exact mass-protection criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
}
\label{eq:full_accept_gate4}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4): U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}.
\label{eq:full_accept_Ares}
\end{equation}

\section{Gate 2--3 carrier block}

The practical Gate-2 longitudinal closure is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0,
\qquad
I_3\neq 0,
\qquad
C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:full_accept_gate2}
\end{equation}

The practical Gate-3 transverse closure is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0)
\Longrightarrow
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:full_accept_gate3}
\end{equation}

Combining \eqref{eq:full_accept_gate2} and \eqref{eq:full_accept_gate3}, one gets the carrier-level statement
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:full_accept_carrier_conclusion}
\end{equation}
so the present branch realizes a viable anisotropic massless Dirac \emph{carrier candidate}.

\section{Gate 4 mass-protection block}

Mass protection is independent of carrier existence.
Even after \eqref{eq:full_accept_carrier_conclusion}, a constant mass can still appear unless
\eqref{eq:full_accept_gate4} holds.

A sufficient mechanism is exact residual valley symmetry:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta=e^{i\theta Q_V/2}.
}
\label{eq:full_accept_QV}
\end{equation}

If exact residual \(U(1)_V\) survives on the isolated doubled shell block, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:full_accept_U1}
\end{equation}

The weaker remnant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
}
\label{eq:full_accept_Z2_generator}
\end{equation}
already suffices, since then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:full_accept_Z2}
\end{equation}

Thus either exact residual \(U(1)_V\), or already exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\), is sufficient for Gate 4.

\section{Full practical acceptance theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Full practical acceptance theorem for the refined locked \(+\) Class II branch]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the support gate passes:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho};
\label{eq:full_accept_assump1}
\end{equation}

\item the practical longitudinal Gate-2 conditions hold:
\begin{equation}
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0,
\qquad
I_3\neq 0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq 0;
\label{eq:full_accept_assump2}
\end{equation}

\item the practical transverse Gate-3 conditions hold:
\begin{equation}
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0);
\label{eq:full_accept_assump3}
\end{equation}

\item the corrected isolated doubled shell block passes Gate 4:
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\label{eq:full_accept_assump4}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Then the present refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is accepted as a
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{practically viable protected anisotropic massless Dirac branch.}
}
\label{eq:full_accept_main_claim}
\end{equation}

More explicitly, the isolated doubled shell block has the principal form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_D^{\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
v_\perp p_1' \Gamma^1
+
v_\perp p_2' \Gamma^2
+
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \Gamma^3,
}
\label{eq:full_accept_principal}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
v_\perp=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}>0,
\qquad
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4,
\label{eq:full_accept_clifford}
\end{equation}
and no symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Gate 2, assumptions \eqref{eq:full_accept_assump2} imply
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
By Gate 3, assumptions \eqref{eq:full_accept_assump3} imply
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
Hence
\[
v_\perp=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}>0,
\]
and therefore the shell-reduced symbol is a nondegenerate anisotropic massless Dirac carrier.

Independently, assumption \eqref{eq:full_accept_assump4} states that no symmetry-allowed constant Hermitian operator lies in the Dirac-mass space
\[
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
\]
Therefore no constant gap-opening Dirac mass is allowed.

Finally, assumption \eqref{eq:full_accept_assump1} guarantees spectral isolation of the relevant low slot from the remote sector, so the reduced carrier statement is actually supported as a low-energy isolated shell conclusion.

Thus the present branch is accepted as a practically viable protected anisotropic massless Dirac branch.
\end{proof}

\section{Equivalent sufficient symmetry version}

\begin{corollary}[Residual-valley sufficient form]
Under the same Gate-1, Gate-2, and Gate-3 assumptions, if in addition either

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{exact residual }U(1)_V\text{ survives on the corrected isolated doubled shell block},
}
\label{eq:full_accept_U1_assump}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{exact residual }\mathbb Z_2^V\text{ survives on the corrected isolated doubled shell block},
}
\label{eq:full_accept_Z2_assump}
\end{equation}
then the branch is accepted as a protected anisotropic massless Dirac branch.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Either assumption implies
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},

which is exactly Gate 4.
Then the theorem applies.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Practical reject theorem]

\end{theorem}

\section{Gate 4 Attachment to the Integrated Carrier Theorem}

\section{Carrier-side input already fixed}

The exact shell-reduced infrared symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)

H_D^{\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
v_\perp p_1' \Gamma^1
+

This is the exact Gate-4 pass/fail statement.

\section{Residual valley symmetry in the standard shell basis}

A sufficient protecting mechanism is exact residual valley symmetry.
In the standard doubled basis, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta=e^{i\theta Q_V/2}.

Then
\begin{equation}
[Q_V,H_D^{\mathrm{pr}}(p)]=0.
\label{eq:G4attach_QV_comm}

The two mass generators transform as a charged doublet:
\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\label{eq:G4attach_massrot1}

\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:G4attach_massrot2}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.

A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.

\label{eq:G4attach_Z2}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact \(Q_*\)-Invariant Constant-Sector Audit for Gate 4}

\section{Goal}

The remaining Gate-4 question is no longer the classification of possible Dirac masses.

\text{Does the full corrected constant sector preserve the same residual generator }
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3\ ?
}
\label{eq:Qaudit_goal}
\end{equation}

If yes, then no actual constant Dirac mass can appear.
If no, one must identify the explicit symmetry-breaking constant term and test whether it lies in the actual mass space.

\section{Actual principal block and actual mass space}

The actual projected massless shell block is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau_1\otimes s_2,
\label{eq:Qaudit_Hlin}
\end{equation}
with exact residual generator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:Qaudit_Qstar}
\end{equation}

The actual constant Dirac-mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{M_1,M_2\},
\qquad
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:Qaudit_Mactual}
\end{equation}

\section{Commutant of \(Q_*\)}

Let
\[
\tau_a\otimes s_b,
\qquad
a,b\in\{0,1,2,3\},
\]
be the real Hermitian operator basis, with \(\tau_0=s_0=\mathbf 1_2\).

Define the parity map
\[
\epsilon(0)=\epsilon(3)=+1,
\qquad
\epsilon(1)=\epsilon(2)=-1.
\]
Then
\[
\tau_3\tau_a=\epsilon(a)\tau_a\tau_3,
\qquad
s_3 s_b=\epsilon(b)s_b s_3.
\]
Hence
\begin{align}
[Q_*,\tau_a\otimes s_b]
&=
[\tau_3\otimes s_3,\tau_a\otimes s_b]
\\
&=
\tau_3\tau_a\otimes s_3 s_b
-
\tau_a\tau_3\otimes s_b s_3
\\
&=
\bigl(\epsilon(a)\epsilon(b)-1\bigr)\,
\tau_a\tau_3\otimes s_b s_3.
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
[Q_*,\tau_a\otimes s_b]=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\epsilon(a)\epsilon(b)=1.
\label{eq:Qaudit_comm_criterion}
\end{equation}

So the exact \(Q_*\)-commuting Hermitian constant algebra is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\mathbf 1_2\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_3\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\}.
}
\label{eq:Qaudit_CQ}
\end{equation}

\section{Mass exclusion by \(Q_*\)}

Now
\[
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\qquad\text{has}\qquad
\epsilon(2)\epsilon(0)=-1,
\]
and
\[
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3
\qquad\text{has}\qquad
\epsilon(1)\epsilon(3)=-1.
\]
Hence neither \(M_1\) nor \(M_2\) commutes with \(Q_*\).

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:Qaudit_intersection_zero}
\end{equation}

This proves the exact finite statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,K]=0
\Longrightarrow
K\notin \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
\quad\text{for every constant Hermitian }K.
}
\label{eq:Qaudit_no_mass_if_Q}
\end{equation}

So preservation of the same \(Q_*\) is already sufficient for actual constant mass protection.

\section{Source-by-source constant-sector decomposition}

Write the full corrected constant block as
\begin{equation}
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}

\Sigma(0,0).

\end{equation}
hence by \eqref{eq:Qaudit_no_mass_if_Q},

\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:Qaudit_total_no_mass}
\end{equation}

\section{What is already known for each source}

\subsection{Scalar identity-channel block}

The scalar identity-channel Bragg obstruction is a separate constant-sector issue and must already have been removed before the final massless Dirac conclusion is claimed.
So the scalar source is not a new conceptual frontier, but an explicit finite exclusion check.

\subsection{Class II sector}

The canonical minimal Class II correction renormalizes only the derivative shell tensor coefficients and does not, by construction, insert an independent constant \(4\times4\) mass operator.
Therefore Class II is compatible with mass protection, but is not by itself a proof of full microscopic protection.

\subsection{Remote Schur self-energy}

The only genuinely nontrivial remaining microscopic part is the remote-sector inheritance test.

\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.

\label{eq:Qaudit_Sigma_comm}

Then \(\Sigma(0,0)\) is automatically non-mass-generating.

\section{Conditional Gate-4 closure theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Actual \(Q_*\)-audit closure theorem]
Assume that the corrected isolated shell block and the remote-sector elimination preserve the same exact residual generator \(Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3\), i.e.

[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}]=0,

A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.

\text{no actual constant Dirac mass }M_1\text{ or }M_2\text{ can appear.}

\begin{proof}

every exact constant correction belongs to the \(Q_*\)-commuting algebra \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\).

\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.

Equivalently,

A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.

Combining the carrier conditions with the conditional Gate-4 closure, we obtain:

\section{Reject meaning}

\[
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}]\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad

\quad\text{or}\quad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]\neq 0,
\]
then Gate 4 is not closed.

This still does not immediately prove a mass appears.
It means only that symmetry no longer forbids it automatically.
At that point one must explicitly project the symmetry-breaking constant piece onto
\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The actual remaining Gate-4 problem is finite.

The actual residual generator is
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\]
and the actual constant mass space is
\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
\]

The exact \(Q_*\)-commuting constant algebra is
\[
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\mathbf 1_2\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_3\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\},
\]
and it satisfies
\[
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\]

Therefore preservation of the same exact residual generator \(Q_*\) is already sufficient for actual constant mass protection.

Writing the corrected constant sector as
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
+
\Sigma(0,0),
\]
the full microscopic Gate-4 audit is exactly
\[
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]

If these hold, then
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
\]
so the branch is mass-protected.

Hence the full practical acceptance criterion becomes
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}]=0.
}
\]

Equivalently, the only remaining microscopic frontier is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the full corrected microscopic block preserve the same exact }Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3\text{ symmetry?}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Schur-Complement Symmetry Inheritance Lemma for \texorpdfstring{$\Sigma(0,0)$}{Sigma(0,0)}}

\section{Purpose}

The remaining microscopic issue in Gate 4 is whether the remote-sector Schur self-energy preserves the same exact residual generator \(Q_*\) that is already identified on the projected \(4\times 4\) shell block.

The theorem-level statement already says that if the full microscopic theory preserves the residual valley symmetry, then the Schur-complement effective Hamiltonian inherits it, and hence \([Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0\). The present goal is to write this as a complete finite block-matrix proof in the actual shell-basis language.

\section{Full block structure}

Let the full microscopic Hamiltonian near the crossing be decomposed as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p,\omega)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_L(p) & W(p) \\
W(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:schur_full_block}
\end{equation}
where

\begin{itemize}
\item \(H_L(p)\) acts on the isolated low shell block,
\item \(H_R(p)\) acts on the remote sector,
\item \(W(p)\) couples the low block to the remote sector.
\end{itemize}

The Schur-complement effective low-energy Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(p,\omega)
=
H_L(p)
+
W(p)\bigl(\omega-H_R(p)\bigr)^{-1}W(p)^\dagger.
\label{eq:schur_heff}
\end{equation}
At zero momentum and zero frequency, define
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0)
:=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger.
\label{eq:schur_sigma00}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact residual symmetry on the full microscopic block}

Assume that the full microscopic theory preserves an exact residual symmetry generated on the low block by \(Q_*\), and on the remote sector by a Hermitian generator \(Q_R\). Equivalently, define
\begin{equation}
Q_{\mathrm{full}}
:=
Q_*\oplus Q_R
=
\begin{pmatrix}
Q_* & 0 \\
0 & Q_R
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:schur_qfull}
\end{equation}
and assume
\begin{equation}
[Q_{\mathrm{full}},H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)]=0.
\label{eq:schur_full_sym}
\end{equation}

Expanding \eqref{eq:schur_full_sym} blockwise gives
\begin{equation}
[Q_*,H_L(p)]=0,
\label{eq:schur_low_comm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
[Q_R,H_R(p)]=0,
\label{eq:schur_remote_comm}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
Q_*W(p)=W(p)Q_R,
\qquad
W(p)^\dagger Q_*=Q_R W(p)^\dagger.
\label{eq:schur_intertwiner}
\end{equation}

Thus \(W(p)\) is an intertwiner between the low and remote symmetry actions.

\section{Resolvent covariance}

From \eqref{eq:schur_remote_comm}, one has
\[
Q_R(\omega-H_R(p))=(\omega-H_R(p))Q_R.
\]
Whenever \(\omega-H_R(p)\) is invertible, this implies
\begin{equation}
Q_R(\omega-H_R(p))^{-1}=(\omega-H_R(p))^{-1}Q_R.
\label{eq:schur_resolvent_comm}
\end{equation}

Therefore the remote resolvent belongs to the commutant of \(Q_R\).

\section{Symmetry inheritance of the Schur self-energy}

Now compute
\begin{align}
Q_*\,\Sigma(0,0)
&=
Q_*\,W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
W(0)Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\qquad\text{by \eqref{eq:schur_intertwiner}}
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_R W(0)^\dagger
\qquad\text{by \eqref{eq:schur_resolvent_comm}}
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger Q_*
\qquad\text{by \eqref{eq:schur_intertwiner}}
\\
&=
\Sigma(0,0)\,Q_*.
\end{align}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:schur_sigma_qstar}
\end{equation}

This is the exact symmetry-inheritance lemma required for Gate 4.

\section{Equivalent operator-level statement}

The same computation at general \((p,\omega)\) gives
\begin{equation}
[Q_*,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(p,\omega)]=0
\label{eq:schur_heff_qstar}
\end{equation}
whenever the full block symmetry \eqref{eq:schur_full_sym} holds.

Thus the Schur complement preserves the exact residual generator \(Q_*\) automatically, provided the full microscopic block preserves the direct-sum generator \(Q_{\mathrm{full}}\).

\section{Consequences for the actual mass space}

The actual canonical shell basis carries
\begin{equation}
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\label{eq:schur_actual_qstar}
\end{equation}
and the actual constant Dirac-mass space is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{M_1,M_2\},
\qquad
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3.
\label{eq:schur_actual_mass}
\end{equation}

Now
\[
[Q_*,M_1]\neq 0,
\qquad
[Q_*,M_2]\neq 0.
\]
So every operator commuting with \(Q_*\) is automatically excluded from the actual mass space:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):[Q_*,K]=0\}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:schur_commutant_mass_zero}
\end{equation}

Combining \eqref{eq:schur_sigma_qstar} and \eqref{eq:schur_commutant_mass_zero}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:schur_sigma_no_mass}
\end{equation}

Therefore no Schur-generated constant Dirac mass can appear if the same exact residual symmetry survives remote elimination.

\section{Little-group scalar refinement}

If in addition the crossing-point constant sector is little-group scalar, then the \(Q_*\)-commuting constant algebra collapses further to the two-dimensional neutral sector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=\tilde a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+\tilde a_*\,Q_*.
}
\label{eq:schur_sigma_scalar_form}
\end{equation}
This is the actual-basis transport of the standard statement
\[
\Sigma(0,0)=a_0\mathbf 1_4+a_3(\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\]

Hence even at the refined scalar level, the Schur self-energy can produce at most an overall shift and a \(Q_*\)-neutral splitting term, but never a genuine constant Dirac mass.

\section{Conditional remote-sector closure theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Remote-sector symmetry inheritance in the actual basis]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the full microscopic Hamiltonian admits an exact direct-sum residual symmetry generator
\[
Q_{\mathrm{full}}=Q_*\oplus Q_R;
\]
\item the full block satisfies
\[
[Q_{\mathrm{full}},H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)]=0;
\]
\item the remote resolvent \((\omega-H_R(p))^{-1}\) exists at the point of interest.
\end{enumerate}
Then the Schur-complement effective shell Hamiltonian satisfies
\[
[Q_*,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(p,\omega)]=0,
\]
and in particular
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:schur_theorem_main}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:schur_theorem_nomass}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The blockwise consequences of \([Q_{\mathrm{full}},H_{\mathrm{full}}]=0\) are
\eqref{eq:schur_low_comm}, \eqref{eq:schur_remote_comm}, and \eqref{eq:schur_intertwiner}. These imply the resolvent covariance \eqref{eq:schur_resolvent_comm}. Substituting into the definition of the Schur self-energy yields \eqref{eq:schur_sigma_qstar}. Since every actual mass generator fails to commute with \(Q_*\), one gets \eqref{eq:schur_theorem_nomass}.
\end{proof}

\section{Integrated Gate 4 reduction}

Therefore Gate 4 reduces completely to the following finite microscopic yes/no test:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\,Q_R\ \text{such that}\ 
[Q_*\oplus Q_R,H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)]=0\ ?
}
\label{eq:schur_final_yesno}
\end{equation}

If yes, then remote elimination preserves \(Q_*\), so
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0
\]
and the remote self-energy cannot generate any element of \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\).

If no, then Gate 4 is not automatically closed, and one must explicitly project the symmetry-breaking constant remainder onto the basis
\[
\{M_1,M_2\}
=
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
\]

\section{Final operational form}

At this point the full constant-sector Gate-4 audit is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
\exists\,Q_R:\ [Q_*\oplus Q_R,H_{\mathrm{full}}]=0.
}
\label{eq:schur_operational_gate4}
\end{equation}

If these hold, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
}
\label{eq:schur_gate4_closed}
\end{equation}
so the current branch passes Gate 4.

\section{Final Summary}

The only genuinely nontrivial remaining part of Gate 4 is the remote-sector symmetry inheritance problem.

Let
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_L(p) & W(p)\\
W(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{full}}=Q_*\oplus Q_R.
\]
If
\[
[Q_{\mathrm{full}},H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)]=0,
\]
then blockwise one has
\[
[Q_*,H_L]=0,
\qquad
[Q_R,H_R]=0,
\qquad
Q_*W=WQ_R.
\]
Hence
\[
Q_R(\omega-H_R)^{-1}=(\omega-H_R)^{-1}Q_R,
\]
and therefore the Schur-complement self-energy
\[
\Sigma(0,0)=W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\]
satisfies
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\]

In the actual canonical shell basis,
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\qquad
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
\]
Since neither actual mass generator commutes with \(Q_*\), it follows that
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\]

Therefore the remote sector cannot generate a constant Dirac mass provided the same exact residual symmetry survives remote elimination.

So Gate 4 is now reduced to the finite microscopic question:
\[
\boxed{
\exists\,Q_R\ \text{such that}\ [Q_*\oplus Q_R,H_{\mathrm{full}}]=0\ ?
}
\]

If yes, then
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
\]
and the branch is mass-protected.
If no, one must explicitly project the symmetry-breaking constant remainder onto the basis
\[
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Remote Intertwiner Audit: Two-Route Closure of Gate 4}

\section{Purpose}

The remaining microscopic part of Gate 4 is not the classification of masses or the identification of the residual generator on the projected shell block.
Those are already closed.

The only remaining issue is the remote sector.
More precisely, one must determine whether the remote-sector contribution to the Schur self-energy can produce an actual constant Dirac mass on the corrected \(4\times4\) shell carrier.

The correct formulation is a two-route dichotomy:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Route I: strict shell-relevant mismatch } \Longrightarrow V(0)=0,
}
\label{eq:RT_route1}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Route II: exact residual intertwiner symmetry } \Longrightarrow [Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:RT_route2}
\end{equation}

Either route is sufficient for the remote sector to pass Gate 4.

\section{Low/remote block decomposition}

Let the corrected microscopic operator at the crossing be block-decomposed as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:RT_full_block}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R,
\qquad
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

The remote Schur self-energy at zero energy/momentum is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0)=V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger,
\label{eq:RT_sigma00}
\end{equation}
assuming the remote block is invertible at the crossing.

The actual residual generator on the projected shell carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
}
\label{eq:RT_Qstar}
\end{equation}
and the actual constant mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
}
\label{eq:RT_Mactual}
\end{equation}

Since neither actual mass generator commutes with \(Q_*\), every \(Q_*\)-commuting constant operator is automatically non-mass-generating.

\section{Route I: strict shell-relevant mismatch}

Let \(H_*\) denote the shell-relevant residual symmetry group at the crossing.
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the full microscopic operator is \(H_*\)-equivariant at \(p=0\);
\item \(\mathcal H_D\) and \(\mathcal H_R\) are \(H_*\)-invariant;
\item \(\mathcal H_D\) and \(\mathcal H_R\) share no common shell-relevant irreducible component.
\end{enumerate}

Then
\begin{equation}
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\label{eq:RT_intertwiner_space}
\end{equation}
But if there is no common irreducible component, Schur's lemma implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:RT_zero_mixing}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
}
\label{eq:RT_sigma_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore the remote sector contributes no constant term at all, and in particular no element of \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\) can be generated.

\subsection{Practical label version}

In the present TECT setting, the sufficient no-common-sector condition is checked by shell-relevant labels.
A remote sector \(K_a\subset \mathcal H_R\) is automatically excluded from mixing with \(\mathcal H_D\) if it differs from the Dirac carrier in at least one of:

\begin{equation}
\pm G_*,
\qquad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\qquad
\text{presence of enriched internal doublet},
\qquad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\qquad
\text{additional conserved microscopic labels}.
\label{eq:RT_labels}
\end{equation}

Thus Route I reduces to a finite mismatch table audit.

\section{Route II: exact residual intertwiner symmetry}

If a common shell-relevant sector does exist, then \(V(0)\) need not vanish.
In that case one must use the residual symmetry itself.

Assume there exists a Hermitian generator \(Q_R\) on \(\mathcal H_R\) such that
\begin{equation}
Q_{\mathrm{full}}:=Q_*\oplus Q_R
\label{eq:RT_Qfull}
\end{equation}
is an exact residual symmetry generator of the full microscopic block:
\begin{equation}
[Q_{\mathrm{full}},H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)]=0.
\label{eq:RT_full_sym}
\end{equation}

Blockwise this implies
\begin{equation}
[Q_*,H_D(0)]=0,
\qquad
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.
\label{eq:RT_blockwise}
\end{equation}

Since \([Q_R,H_R(0)]=0\), the inverse remote block also commutes with \(Q_R\):
\begin{equation}
Q_R\,H_R(0)^{-1}=H_R(0)^{-1}Q_R.
\label{eq:RT_resolvent}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{align}
Q_*\,\Sigma(0,0)
&=
Q_*V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
V(0)Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_RV(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger Q_*
\\
&=
\Sigma(0,0)\,Q_*.
\end{align}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:RT_sigma_comm}
\end{equation}

Because every actual constant mass fails to commute with \(Q_*\), one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:RT_sigma_nomass}
\end{equation}

So Route II also passes the remote-sector part of Gate 4.

\section{Charge-sector formulation of Route II}

The most practical way to realize Route II is to decompose the remote sector into \(Q_R\)-charge sectors:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_{q\in\mathcal Q}\mathcal H_R^{(q)},
\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(q)}}=q\,\mathbf 1.
\label{eq:RT_charge_decomp}
\end{equation}

Similarly the low shell carrier decomposes under \(Q_*\) into
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_D=\mathcal H_D^{(+)}\oplus \mathcal H_D^{(-)}.
\label{eq:RT_low_charge}
\end{equation}

Then the intertwiner condition
\[
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R
\]
is equivalent to the selection rule
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0):\mathcal H_R^{(q)}\longrightarrow \mathcal H_D^{(q)}
\quad\text{only.}
}
\label{eq:RT_charge_selection}
\end{equation}

Thus the practical audit becomes finite:

\begin{enumerate}
\item decompose \(\mathcal H_R\) into exact residual sectors;
\item assign the \(Q_R\)-charges;
\item check whether every nonzero block of \(V(0)\) preserves the charge;
\item if yes, then \([Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Remote-sector two-route closure theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Two-route remote-sector closure for Gate 4]
Assume the scalar identity-channel obstruction has already been removed and the Class II constant sector has passed its own audit.

Then the remote sector passes Gate 4 if either of the following holds:

\paragraph{Route I.}
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\paragraph{Route II.}
There exists a Hermitian generator \(Q_R\) on \(\mathcal H_R\) such that
\[
[Q_*\oplus Q_R,H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)]=0.
\]

Under Route I one gets
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
\]
Under Route II one gets
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\qquad
\Sigma(0,0)\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\]
Hence in either case the remote sector cannot generate an actual constant Dirac mass.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Route I follows from equivariance plus the vanishing of the intertwiner space.
Route II follows from blockwise symmetry inheritance through the Schur complement.
In both cases the resulting constant remote correction has zero projection onto \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\).
\end{proof}

\section{Integrated practical Gate-4 form}

At this stage, the full practical Gate-4 audit is reduced to:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}^{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
}
\label{eq:RT_gate4_scalar}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
}
\label{eq:RT_gate4_classII}
\end{equation}

and, for the remote sector, either
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
}
\label{eq:RT_gate4_remote1}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\,Q_R:\ [Q_*\oplus Q_R,H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:RT_gate4_remote2}
\end{equation}

Therefore Gate 4 is completely reduced to a finite yes/no audit.

\section{Strongest honest conclusion}

The shell-level mass-protection problem is already closed.
The only remaining microscopic open point is now sharply split:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{either prove strict shell-relevant remote mismatch,}
}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{construct }Q_R\text{ and verify exact remote intertwining.}
}
\end{equation}

No third conceptual mechanism is needed.

\section{Final Summary}

The remaining remote-sector part of Gate 4 has an exact two-route closure.

The actual shell carrier already has the residual generator
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\]
and the actual constant mass space is
\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
\]

Therefore the only remaining microscopic problem is the remote sector.

There are exactly two sufficient routes:

\paragraph{Route I: strict shell-relevant mismatch.}
If
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
then
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
\]
So the remote sector contributes no constant term at all.

\paragraph{Route II: exact residual intertwiner symmetry.}
If there exists a Hermitian generator \(Q_R\) on the remote sector such that
\[
[Q_*\oplus Q_R,H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)]=0,
\]
then
\[
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R,
\qquad
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\]
hence
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]
Since every actual mass generator fails to commute with \(Q_*\), it follows that
\[
\Sigma(0,0)\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\]

Thus the remote sector passes Gate 4 if either
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
or
\[
\exists\,Q_R:\ [Q_*\oplus Q_R,H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)]=0.
\]

So the full remaining microscopic frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the finite audit:
\[
\boxed{
\text{either prove strict remote mismatch, or explicitly construct }Q_R\text{ and verify the intertwiner condition.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Route I Closed in the Working Truncation}

\section{Goal}

We now stop treating Route I abstractly and write the actual sectorwise mismatch theorem for the present working truncation.

The local shell-relevant Dirac carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}
\otimes
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\label{eq:routeI_HD}
\end{equation}

At \(p=0\), the constant remote mixing block satisfies
\begin{equation}
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\label{eq:routeI_intertwiner}
\end{equation}
Hence it is enough to prove
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:routeI_goal}
\end{equation}

\section{Shell-relevant label set}

The shell-relevant labels used in the zero-mixing audit are:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\pm G_*,
\qquad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\qquad
\text{presence of enriched internal doublet},
}
\label{eq:routeI_labels1}
\end{equation}
together with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\qquad
\text{extra conserved microscopic labels}.
}
\label{eq:routeI_labels2}
\end{equation}

A remote sector is excluded from constant mixing as soon as it fails to match \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one of these labels.

\section{Minimal dangerous remote decomposition}

The canonical dangerous decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}.
\label{eq:routeI_HR_full}
\end{equation}

The four default sectors are excluded for the following shell-relevant reasons:

\begin{align}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
&:\quad
\text{volumetric mismatch},
\label{eq:routeI_vol}
\\
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
&:\quad
\text{different shell-orbit / shell-order mismatch},
\label{eq:routeI_high}
\\
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
&:\quad
\text{absence of the enriched internal doublet},
\label{eq:routeI_nonenr}
\\
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
&:\quad
\text{wrong internal representation}.
\label{eq:routeI_wrongint}
\end{align}

Thus these four sectors satisfy
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:routeI_four_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{Sectorwise mismatch table}

The finite audit may be displayed as follows:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{c|c|c|c|c|c}
Remote sector
& \(\pm G_*\)
& trans/non-vol
& enriched doublet
& grading/parity
& consequence \\ \hline
\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\)
& may match
& fails
& may match
& -- 
& excluded \\
\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\)
& fails
& may match
& may match
& --
& excluded \\
\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\)
& may match
& may match
& fails
& --
& excluded \\
\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\)
& may match
& may match
& fails
& possibly fails too
& excluded \\
\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\)
& case by case
& case by case
& case by case
& case by case
& requires explicit audit
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The logical point is not that every column must fail.
A single shell-relevant mismatch is sufficient to force the corresponding intertwiner space to vanish.

\section{Working truncation versus enlarged dangerous truncation}

There are now two precise versions.

\subsection{Version A: enlarged dangerous truncation}

For the enlarged decomposition \eqref{eq:routeI_HR_full}, the only unresolved possibility is
\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\).
Hence the whole Route-I frontier reduces to the single finite question:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does any }K\subset \mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}
\text{ match }\mathcal H_D
\text{ in all shell-relevant labels?}
}
\label{eq:routeI_extra_question}
\end{equation}

If the answer is no, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:routeI_enlarged_done}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Version B: present working truncation}

In the present working truncation, one keeps only
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
}
\label{eq:routeI_working_HR}
\end{equation}

Then all remote sectors are already covered by the default mismatch eliminations, so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:routeI_working_hom}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:routeI_working_V0}
\end{equation}

This closes Route I completely in the present working truncation.

\section{Consequence for the Schur self-energy}

Once
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0
\label{eq:routeI_V0}
\end{equation}
and the first nontrivial mixing is at most linear,
\begin{equation}
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\label{eq:routeI_Vlinear}
\end{equation}
the Schur self-energy satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(E,p)
=
V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right)
\label{eq:routeI_sigma}
\end{equation}
provided the remote block is gapped by \(\Delta>0\).

Thus the remote sector cannot generate any \(O(p^0)\) constant term in the working truncation.

\section{Route-I closure theorem in the working truncation}

\begin{theorem}[Working-truncation Route-I closure]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-relevant carrier is
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}};
\]
\item the remote sector in the working truncation is
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}};
\]
\item each of the four remote sectors differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:routeI_main_theorem}
\end{equation}
Consequently, in the presence of a remote gap \(\Delta>0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
}
\label{eq:routeI_sigma_bound}
\end{equation}
so the remote sector contributes no constant mass-generating term.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \(H_*\)-equivariance,
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Since the remote block is the direct sum of the four displayed sectors,
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\bigoplus_{a\in\{\mathrm{vol},\mathrm{high},\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}\}}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_a,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Each summand vanishes because the corresponding sector fails at least one shell-relevant matching condition.
Hence the full intertwiner space vanishes, which implies \(V(0)=0\).

The Schur bound then follows from \eqref{eq:routeI_Vlinear} and the remote gap bound.
\end{proof}

\section{Strongest honest conclusion}

The strongest honest conclusion is therefore split into two levels.

\paragraph{Working truncation.}
Route I is already closed:
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Enlarged dangerous truncation.}
Route I is reduced to a single finite residual question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{is } \mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}} \text{ empty or shell-relevantly mismatched?}
}
\]

So no new conceptual mechanism is needed.
Only a finite remote-sector classification remains.

\section{Final Summary}

The Route-I remote-sector audit is already closed in the present working truncation.

The shell-relevant local Dirac carrier is
\[
\mathcal H_D
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}
\otimes
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

The exact zero-mixing criterion is
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D),
\qquad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
\]

In the enlarged dangerous decomposition,
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}},
\]
the first four sectors are excluded immediately by shell-relevant mismatch:
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}:\ \text{volumetric mismatch},
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}:\ \text{different shell-orbit mismatch},
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}:\ \text{absence of enriched internal doublet},
\]
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}:\ \text{wrong internal representation}.
\]

Therefore the only unresolved enlarged-truncation question is whether
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}
\]
contains any sector matching \(\mathcal H_D\) in all shell-relevant labels.

In the present working truncation, however, one keeps only
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
so every remote sector is already eliminated and hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
V(0)=0.
}
\]

Consequently, if the remote block is gapped by \(\Delta>0\) and the first nontrivial mixing is at most linear in momentum, then
\[
\Sigma(E,p)
=
V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\]

So, in the present working truncation, the remote sector cannot generate any constant \(O(p^0)\) term.
The next independent frontier is therefore no longer zero constant mixing, but the remote spectral gap.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Step IV: Finite Remote-Gap Inequality on the Actual Working Truncation Matrix}

\section{Goal}

We now stop speaking about the remote gap in abstract operator language only.
The task is to write the remote-gap condition
\[
\Delta>0
\]
as an explicit finite inequality for the actual working truncation matrix.

The shell-relevant working decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\label{eq:stepIV_Hfull_tr}
\end{equation}
and the full truncated block Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V_{DR}(p)\\
V_{DR}(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:stepIV_full_block}
\end{equation}

The present step is to prove a positive lower bound for the remote block
\[
H_R(p).
\]

\section{Actual working truncation remote block}

In the ordered remote basis
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
write the remote block as
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\label{eq:stepIV_DR_RR}
\end{equation}
where the benchmark block is the sector-center diagonal operator
\begin{equation}
D_R(p)
=
\operatorname{diag}\!\Bigl(
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),
\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)
\Bigr),
\label{eq:stepIV_DR_diag}
\end{equation}
and \(R_R(p)\) collects all residual remote--remote off-diagonal mixing terms.

Define the pointwise benchmark distance and the residual norm budget by
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p)
:=
\min\Bigl\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\Bigr\},
\label{eq:stepIV_delta0_point}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\eta_R(p):=\|R_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:stepIV_eta_point}
\end{equation}

On the low-momentum neighborhood
\[
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\]
define the uniform quantities
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\label{eq:stepIV_uniform_defs}
\end{equation}

\section{Uniform finite spectral inequality}

\begin{theorem}[Working-truncation remote-gap criterion]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\label{eq:stepIV_main_ineq}
\end{equation}
then the remote sector has a uniform positive spectral gap:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho),
}
\label{eq:stepIV_gap_claim}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho:=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_gap_value}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix \(|p|\le \rho\).
Since
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\]
for every \(\psi\in\mathcal H_R\),
\begin{align}
\|H_R(p)\psi\|
&\ge
\|D_R(p)\psi\|-\|R_R(p)\psi\|
\\
&\ge
\delta_0(p)\|\psi\|-\eta_R(p)\|\psi\|
\\
&=
(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p))\|\psi\|.
\end{align}
Taking the infimum over \(|p|\le \rho\) gives
\[
\|H_R(p)\psi\|
\ge
(\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho})\|\psi\|
=
\Delta_\rho\|\psi\|.
\]
If \(\Delta_\rho>0\), then zero lies at uniform distance at least \(\Delta_\rho\) from
\(\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\) for all \(|p|\le \rho\).
This proves \eqref{eq:stepIV_gap_claim} and \eqref{eq:stepIV_gap_value}.
\end{proof}

\section{Sectorwise benchmark lower bounds}

The actual usefulness of \eqref{eq:stepIV_main_ineq} depends on explicit lower bounds
for the four benchmark entries in \eqref{eq:stepIV_DR_diag}.

\subsection{Higher-shell benchmark}

For the current BCC normalization, the higher-shell sector admits the explicit lower bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)} \ge 4K-|r_*|.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_high_bench}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Volumetric benchmark}

The heavy volumetric sector contributes the benchmark
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_vol_bench}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Wrong-internal benchmark}

The wrong-internal sector has the explicit benchmark
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
\ge
|E_L-E_*|.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_wrongint_bench}
\end{equation}
Under bounded internal perturbation \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}\), this remains positive provided
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}<|E_L-E_*|,
}
\label{eq:stepIV_wrongint_stability}
\end{equation}
in which case
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}
\ge
|E_L-E_*|-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}>0.
\label{eq:stepIV_wrongint_perturbed}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Non-enriched benchmark}

The same-shell but non-enriched sector is the genuinely non-automatic part.
Its benchmark is represented by the finite truncated lower bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_nonenr_bench}
\end{equation}

\section{Master benchmark matrix inequality}

Collecting the four sectorwise lower bounds, define the working benchmark
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_master_bench}
\end{equation}

Then the full working-truncation remote-gap condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_final_working_ineq}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:stepIV_final_working_ineq} holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}
>
0.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_final_gap}
\end{equation}

Thus the remote-gap problem in the actual working truncation is reduced to one explicit finite matrix inequality.

\section{Gershgorin alternative}

If the remote block is sparse in the chosen sector basis, one may use the Gershgorin lower bound instead of the operator norm estimate.
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min_a
\left(
|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|
-
\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|
\right).
}
\label{eq:stepIV_gershgorin}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0,
}
\label{eq:stepIV_gershgorin_positive}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_{G,\rho},\Delta_{G,\rho})=\varnothing
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho).
\label{eq:stepIV_gershgorin_gap}
\end{equation}

This is often sharper than the crude block-norm budget when the remote matrix is nearly diagonal.

\section{Schur-complement consequence}

Assume in addition that Step III has already been closed, so that
\[
V_{DR}(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|.
\]
Then for any \(|E|<\Delta_\rho/2\),
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta_\rho},
\label{eq:stepIV_resolvent}
\end{equation}
and the Schur self-energy satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(E,p)
=
V_{DR}(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V_{DR}(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
\label{eq:stepIV_schur}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
}
\label{eq:stepIV_effective}
\end{equation}

So, once \eqref{eq:stepIV_final_working_ineq} is proved, the remote sector cannot spoil the principal linear Dirac block.

\section{Honest status}

What is now fully fixed is the exact finite form of Step IV for the actual working truncation.

What is still not inserted is the explicit numerical or analytic evaluation of:
\begin{equation}
4K-|r_*|,
\qquad
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}.
\label{eq:stepIV_notinserted}
\end{equation}

Therefore the honest final wording is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Step IV is closed at the exact finite-inequality level,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual working-branch numbers still need to be inserted.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

In the actual working truncation, the remote block is
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
and
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\]
with
\[
D_R(p)
=
\operatorname{diag}\!\Bigl(
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),
\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)
\Bigr).
\]

Define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min\Bigl\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\Bigr\},
\]
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]
Then the exact finite remote-gap criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

For the current working branch, the practical benchmark is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\]

Therefore the Step-IV master inequality is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]
If this holds, then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

An alternative sufficient route is the Gershgorin lower bound
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min_a
\left(
|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|
\right)>0.
\]

Finally, if
\[
V_{DR}(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
then for \(|E|<\Delta_\rho/2\),
\[
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta_\rho},
\qquad
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
\]
So the remote sector cannot destroy the principal linear Dirac block.

Thus Step IV is now closed at the exact finite-inequality level.
What remains is only the explicit insertion of the working-branch benchmark numbers.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Sectorwise Block-Norm Budget for \texorpdfstring{$\eta_{R,\rho}$}{etaR,rho} in the Working Truncation}

\section{Goal}

The remaining Step-IV input is not the benchmark side anymore.
It is the residual remote mixing budget
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]
The purpose of this section is to replace this abstract norm by a finite sectorwise block budget which can actually be inserted in the working truncation.

\section{Working truncated remote decomposition}

The actual working truncated remote sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
}
\label{eq:eta_working_remote_space}
\end{equation}

Let
\[
Q_{\mathrm{vol}},\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{high}},\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{non}},\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
\]
be the corresponding orthogonal projectors.

Write the remote block as
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\label{eq:eta_HR_split}
\end{equation}
where \(D_R(p)\) is the benchmark block-diagonal part and \(R_R(p)\) is the residual remainder.

At the truncated level, separate
\begin{equation}
R_R(p)=R_R^{\mathrm{off}}(p)+R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)+R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p),
\label{eq:eta_R_split}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(R_R^{\mathrm{off}}(p)\) is the finite remote--remote off-diagonal block;
\item \(R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\) is the tail / omitted-sector coupling;
\item \(R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)\) is the bounded correction to the benchmark diagonal block.
\end{enumerate}

Accordingly define
\begin{equation}
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{off}}(p)\|,
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\|,
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)\|.
\label{eq:eta_three_budgets}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:eta_total_split}
\end{equation}

\section{Pairwise off-diagonal blocks}

For \(a\neq b\) in the label set
\[
\mathcal I=\{\mathrm{vol},\mathrm{high},\mathrm{non},\mathrm{wrong}\},
\]
define
\begin{equation}
R_{ab}(p):=Q_a\,H_R(p)\,Q_b,
\qquad
\eta_{ab,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\label{eq:eta_ab_def}
\end{equation}

Since \(D_R\) already contains the block-diagonal benchmark, the truncated off-diagonal remainder is
\begin{equation}
R_R^{\mathrm{off}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & R_{\mathrm{vol,high}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,non}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{high,vol}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{high,non}} & R_{\mathrm{high,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{non,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{non,high}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{non,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{wrong,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,high}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,non}} & 0
\end{pmatrix}(p).
\label{eq:eta_off_matrix}
\end{equation}

By self-adjointness,
\[
R_{ba}(p)=R_{ab}(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
\eta_{ba,\rho}=\eta_{ab,\rho}.
\]
So there are only six independent pair budgets:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho},\;
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho},\;
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho},\;
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho},\;
\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho},\;
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:eta_six_pairs}
\end{equation}

\section{Sharp finite budget matrix}

Define the symmetric \(4\times 4\) nonnegative budget matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\rho=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}\\
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho} & 0 & \eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}\\
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho} & 0 & \eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}\\
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho} & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:eta_budget_matrix}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Budget-matrix bound]
For the truncated off-diagonal remote remainder,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\|E_\rho\|_2.
}
\label{eq:eta_spectral_budget}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\max_{a\in\mathcal I}\sum_{b\neq a}\eta_{ab,\rho}
\le
\sum_{a<b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:eta_row_sum_budget}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Take any vector
\[
\Psi=(\Psi_{\mathrm{vol}},\Psi_{\mathrm{high}},\Psi_{\mathrm{non}},\Psi_{\mathrm{wrong}})
\in
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}},
\]
and define the nonnegative coordinate vector
\[
x=
\begin{pmatrix}
\|\Psi_{\mathrm{vol}}\|\\
\|\Psi_{\mathrm{high}}\|\\
\|\Psi_{\mathrm{non}}\|\\
\|\Psi_{\mathrm{wrong}}\|
\end{pmatrix}
\in \mathbb R_{\ge 0}^4.
\]
Then for each sector \(a\),
\[
\|(R_R^{\mathrm{off}}(p)\Psi)_a\|
=
\left\|
\sum_{b\neq a}R_{ab}(p)\Psi_b
\right\|
\le
\sum_{b\neq a}\|R_{ab}(p)\|\,\|\Psi_b\|
\le
\sum_{b\neq a}\eta_{ab,\rho}\,x_b
=
(E_\rho x)_a.
\]
Therefore
\[
\|R_R^{\mathrm{off}}(p)\Psi\|^2
=
\sum_a \|(R_R^{\mathrm{off}}(p)\Psi)_a\|^2
\le
\sum_a (E_\rho x)_a^2
=
\|E_\rho x\|_{\ell^2}^2.
\]
But
\[
\|x\|_{\ell^2}^2
=
\sum_a \|\Psi_a\|^2
=
\|\Psi\|^2.
\]
Hence
\[
\|R_R^{\mathrm{off}}(p)\Psi\|
\le
\|E_\rho\|_2\,\|\Psi\|.
\]
Taking the supremum over \(|p|\le \rho\) and over unit vectors \(\Psi\) proves
\eqref{eq:eta_spectral_budget}.

Since \(E_\rho\) is symmetric and entrywise nonnegative,
\[
\|E_\rho\|_2
\le
\|E_\rho\|_\infty
=
\max_a\sum_{b\neq a}\eta_{ab,\rho},
\]
and trivially
\[
\max_a\sum_{b\neq a}\eta_{ab,\rho}
\le
\sum_{a<b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:eta_row_sum_budget}.
\end{proof}

\section{Explicit six-pair row sums}

In the present four-sector truncation, the row-sum bound is
\begin{align}
S_{\mathrm{vol}}
&=
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho},
\\
S_{\mathrm{high}}
&=
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho},
\\
S_{\mathrm{non}}
&=
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho},
\\
S_{\mathrm{wrong}}
&=
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}.
\end{align}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\max\{S_{\mathrm{vol}},S_{\mathrm{high}},S_{\mathrm{non}},S_{\mathrm{wrong}}\}.
}
\label{eq:eta_explicit_rowsum}
\end{equation}

This is already sharper than the crude total-sum bound.

\section{Tail and diagonal budgets}

The previously established tail theorem gives the power-counting bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
}
\label{eq:eta_tail_bound}
\end{equation}
The diagonal correction budget is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)\|.
}
\label{eq:eta_diag_bound}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full residual remote budget obeys
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\|E_\rho\|_2
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:eta_full_sharp}
\end{equation}
and in particular
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\max\{S_{\mathrm{vol}},S_{\mathrm{high}},S_{\mathrm{non}},S_{\mathrm{wrong}}\}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:eta_full_rowsum}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Step-IV insertion theorem}

Recall the benchmark side
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:eta_master_bench_recall}
\end{equation}

Then a sufficient explicit Step-IV condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\|E_\rho\|_2
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:eta_final_sharp_gate}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, one may use the more elementary but weaker form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\max\{S_{\mathrm{vol}},S_{\mathrm{high}},S_{\mathrm{non}},S_{\mathrm{wrong}}\}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:eta_final_rowsum_gate}
\end{equation}

Under either condition,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
-
\eta_{R,\rho}
>
0.
}
\label{eq:eta_gap_final}
\end{equation}

\section{What is now genuinely left}

After this reduction, the only unresolved inputs are finite and explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the same-shell non-enriched benchmark
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)};
\]
\item the six pair budgets
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho},
\;
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho},
\;
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho},
\;
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho},
\;
\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho},
\;
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho};
\]
\item the tail constants in \eqref{eq:eta_tail_bound};
\item the diagonal correction budget \(\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

So Step IV is no longer conceptually open.
It is reduced entirely to a finite benchmark computation plus a finite residual-budget computation.

\section{Final Summary}

The residual remote mixing norm in the working truncation is now reduced to explicit finite data.

The truncated remote sector is
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]

For the pairwise off-diagonal blocks
\[
R_{ab}(p)=Q_aH_R(p)Q_b,
\qquad
\eta_{ab,\rho}=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|,
\]
define the symmetric budget matrix
\[
E_\rho=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}\\
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho} & 0 & \eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}\\
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho} & 0 & \eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}\\
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho} & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\|E_\rho\|_2
\le
\max_a\sum_{b\neq a}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
\]

Together with the tail and diagonal budgets,
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\|E_\rho\|_2+\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}+\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]

Therefore the sharp explicit Step-IV gate is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\|E_\rho\|_2+\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}+\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

This is stronger than the crude total-sum bound and is the most natural form for actual insertion in the working truncation.

\section{Final Summary}

The Step-IV remote-gap problem is now reduced to explicit finite data on the working truncation.

The truncated remote sector is
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]

For the pairwise off-diagonal blocks
\[
R_{ab}(p)=Q_aH_R(p)Q_b,
\qquad
\eta_{ab,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|,
\]
define the symmetric budget matrix
\[
E_\rho=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}\\
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho} & 0 & \eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}\\
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho} & 0 & \eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}\\
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho} & \eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho} & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then the truncated remote budget obeys
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\|E_\rho\|_2
\le
\max_a\sum_{b\neq a}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
\]

Including the tail and diagonal budgets,
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\|E_\rho\|_2+\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}+\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]

Therefore the sharp explicit Step-IV condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\|E_\rho\|_2+\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}+\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

This implies
\[
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0,
\]
so the remote sector is uniformly gapped and the Schur self-energy is suppressed as
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
\]

Hence Step IV is now reduced to the explicit computation of:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\]
the six pairwise budgets \(\eta_{ab,\rho}\),
the tail constants,
and the diagonal correction budget.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Dominant-Pair Reduction of the Six-Pair Remote Budget}

\section{Goal}

The remaining Step-IV problem is to sharpen the six-pair residual norm budget
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\]
into a form adapted to the actual working branch.

The exact six-pair decomposition is already fixed:
\[
(\mathrm{vol,high}),\ 
(\mathrm{vol,non}),\ 
(\mathrm{vol,wrong}),\ 
(\mathrm{high,non}),\ 
(\mathrm{high,wrong}),\ 
(\mathrm{non,wrong}).
\]
For each pair,
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}
\le
\mathcal D_{ab,\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{KK}.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
2\sum_{(ab)\in\mathfrak P_6}
\left[
\mathcal D_{ab,\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{KK}
\right].
\label{eq:dompair_start}
\end{equation}

The purpose of the present section is to reduce \eqref{eq:dompair_start} to the dominant pairs
\[
(\mathrm{high,non}),
\qquad
(\mathrm{non,wrong}),
\]
plus a subleading remainder.

\section{Exact-zero lemma versus suppression lemma}

Before reducing the six-pair budget, we separate two logically different mechanisms.

\begin{lemma}[Exact vanishing from an exact conserved label]
Let \(Q_a,Q_b\) be sector projectors and let \(X\) be an operator source contributing to
\(R_{ab}\).
If there exists an exact projector-valued conserved label \(L\) such that
\[
[L,X]=0,
\]
and the two sectors lie in disjoint \(L\)-eigenspaces, then
\[
Q_a X Q_b=0.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If \(L=\sum_\ell \ell P_\ell\) and \(Q_a\le P_{\ell_a}\), \(Q_b\le P_{\ell_b}\) with \(\ell_a\neq \ell_b\), then
\[
Q_a X Q_b
=
Q_a P_{\ell_a} X P_{\ell_b} Q_b
=
Q_a P_{\ell_a}P_{\ell_b} X Q_b
=0,
\]
because \([L,X]=0\) implies \(X\) preserves each \(L\)-eigenspace.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Honest implication.}
This lemma yields exact zeros only when the corresponding label is an exact symmetry of the relevant pairwise source.
In the present notes, this exact-symmetry status is not yet established for all six pairwise source terms.
Therefore the current working theorem must be formulated in terms of \emph{dominance and suppression}, not by declaring all non-dominant pairs identically zero.

\section{Structural suppression classes}

The current working notes already identify three suppression mechanisms for non-dominant pairs:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{volumetric suppression:}
every pair involving the heavy volumetric sector is suppressed by the positive heavy-locking scale \(M_\sigma\);

\item \textbf{shell-mismatch suppression:}
pairs involving a higher-shell channel inherit the shell mismatch scale
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|;
\]

\item \textbf{double suppression:}
if a pair simultaneously feels shell mismatch and an additional internal or heavy-sector mismatch, then its contribution is subleading relative to the dominant same-shell route.
\end{enumerate}

This is exactly why the current structural notes isolate
\[
(\mathrm{high,non}),
\qquad
(\mathrm{non,wrong})
\]
as the dominant truncated pairs.

\section{Dominant-pair reduced budget theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Dominant-pair reduction]
Under the current structural assumptions of the refined locked \(+\) Class II working truncation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
2\Bigl(
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\Bigr)
+
\Xi_{\mathrm{sub}}(\rho),
}
\label{eq:dompair_main}
\end{equation}
where the subleading remainder \(\Xi_{\mathrm{sub}}(\rho)\) collects the four non-dominant pairs
\[
(\mathrm{vol,high}),\ 
(\mathrm{vol,non}),\ 
(\mathrm{vol,wrong}),\ 
(\mathrm{high,wrong}),
\]
