and is parametrically suppressed by volumetric gap, shell mismatch, or double suppression.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Start from the exact six-pair bound \eqref{eq:dompair_start}.
By the current structural sector audit, the pairs
\[
(\mathrm{high,non}),
\qquad
(\mathrm{non,wrong})
\]
are the only pairs not assigned to one of the three suppression classes above.
Therefore all remaining pair budgets are grouped into
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{sub}}(\rho)
:=
2\Bigl(
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}
\Bigr).
\]
Substituting this into the symmetric six-pair estimate gives \eqref{eq:dompair_main}.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Important honesty clause.}
The theorem above does \emph{not} claim that \(\Xi_{\mathrm{sub}}(\rho)=0\) exactly.
It only states that, in the present working structural regime, it is subleading compared with the dominant pair sector.

\section{Explicit non--wrong bound}

Among the dominant pairs, the non--wrong block is already explicitly reduced.

The direct part is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{dir}}^{\mathrm{non,wrong}}
=
Q_{\mathrm{non}} V^\mu_\perp \partial_\mu Q_{\mathrm{wrong}},
}
\label{eq:dompair_dir_nonwrong}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_\perp
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
C_E E^\mu_a\Sigma_a
+
C_O J^\mu_a\Sigma_a
\right].
\label{eq:dompair_Vperp}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{dir}}^{\mathrm{non,wrong}}
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
C_E\,Q_{\mathrm{non}}(E^\mu_a\Sigma_a)Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
+
C_O\,Q_{\mathrm{non}}(J^\mu_a\Sigma_a)Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
\right]\partial_\mu.
}
\label{eq:dompair_nonwrong_direct}
\end{equation}

The heavy-mediated part is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_{\mathrm{non}}\Delta_XQ_{\mathrm{wrong}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
Q_{\mathrm{non}}
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)^\dagger
Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}.
}
\label{eq:dompair_nonwrong_med}
\end{equation}
Expanding,
\begin{align}
Q_{\mathrm{non}}\Delta_XQ_{\mathrm{wrong}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\Bigl[
&\alpha_X^2\,Q_{\mathrm{non}}\mathcal J\mathcal J^\dagger Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
\nonumber\\
&+
\alpha_X\beta_X\,Q_{\mathrm{non}}
(\mathcal J\mathcal K^\dagger+\mathcal K\mathcal J^\dagger)
Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
\nonumber\\
&+
\beta_X^2\,Q_{\mathrm{non}}\mathcal K\mathcal K^\dagger Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
\Bigr].
\label{eq:dompair_nonwrong_med_expand}
\end{align}

Combining the direct and mediated pieces gives the explicit working bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\le
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right).
}
\label{eq:dompair_nonwrong_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Practical reduction of the high--non contribution}

The pair \((\mathrm{high,non})\) is still one of the two dominant pairs at the theorem-reduction level.
However, the current working notes also state that, at leading order in the small-\(\rho\) regime, the non--wrong pair dominates.
So one may write
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
=
O(\rho)
+
\Xi_{\mathrm{high,non}}^{\mathrm{sub}}(\rho),
\label{eq:dompair_highnon_smallrho}
\end{equation}
and absorb this into the general small-\(\rho\) remainder.

This gives the practical leading-order estimate
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
+
O(\rho).
}
\label{eq:dompair_practical_tr}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Step-IV gate after dominant-pair reduction}

Recall the exact benchmark side
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:dompair_bench}
\end{equation}

Using
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
\]
the exact dominant-pair sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\Bigl(
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\Bigr)
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:dompair_exact_gate}
\end{equation}

At the current practical leading-order level, this reduces further to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
+
O(\rho)
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:dompair_practical_gate}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:dompair_nonwrong_final}, one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
O(\rho)
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:dompair_fully_practical}
\end{equation}

\section{What is actually proved here}

What is rigorously proved at the present level is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the six-pair truncated residual budget is exactly reduced to pairwise source terms;
\item under the current structural assumptions, the dominant pair sector is
\[
(\mathrm{high,non}),\qquad(\mathrm{non,wrong});
\]
\item the pair \((\mathrm{non,wrong})\) already has a fully explicit working upper bound;
\item therefore the Step-IV sufficient condition is practically reduced to a benchmark comparison against a single leading pair plus controlled remainders.
\end{enumerate}

What is \emph{not} yet proved is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{that every non-dominant pair vanishes exactly.}
}
\label{eq:dompair_notproved}
\end{equation}
That stronger statement would require additional exact label-preservation theorems for the corresponding direct and mediated source operators.

\section{Final Summary}

The truncated remote budget has an exact six-pair decomposition:
\[
(\mathrm{vol,high}),\ 
(\mathrm{vol,non}),\ 
(\mathrm{vol,wrong}),\ 
(\mathrm{high,non}),\ 
(\mathrm{high,wrong}),\ 
(\mathrm{non,wrong}).
\]

For each pair,
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}
\le
\mathcal D_{ab,\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{KK}.
\]

Under the current structural assumptions, the dominant truncated residual budget is carried by
\[
(\mathrm{high,non}),
\qquad
(\mathrm{non,wrong}),
\]
while all other pairs are subleading due to volumetric mass gap, shell mismatch, or double suppression.

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
2\Bigl(
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\Bigr)
+
\Xi_{\mathrm{sub}}(\rho).
}
\]

The non--wrong pair already has the explicit working bound
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\le
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right).
}
\]

Therefore the exact dominant-pair Step-IV sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\Bigl(
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\Bigr)
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

At the current practical leading-order level, this reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
+
O(\rho)
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

What is rigorously proved is dominant-pair reduction, not exact vanishing of every non-dominant pair.
Any stronger exact-zero theorem would require additional exact label-preservation results for the corresponding source operators.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit \(O(\rho)\) Bound for the \texorpdfstring{\((\mathrm{high,non})\)}{(high,non)} Pair}

\section{Goal}

The current dominant-pair reduction leaves two potentially leading truncated remote pairs:
\[
(\mathrm{high,non}),
\qquad
(\mathrm{non,wrong}).
\]
The non--wrong block already has an explicit working bound.
So the next nonredundant step is to prove that the high--non block is at most \(O(\rho)\) on the low-momentum window
\[
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\}.
\]

This is enough to justify the practical reduction
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}+O(\rho)
\]
used in the current Step-IV gate.

\section{Remote pair decomposition}

Let
\[
Q_{\mathrm{high}},
\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{non}}
\]
denote the orthogonal projectors onto the higher-shell and same-shell non-enriched sectors inside the truncated remote space.
The pairwise block is
\[
R_{\mathrm{high,non}}(p)
=
Q_{\mathrm{high}}\,H_R(p)\,Q_{\mathrm{non}}.
\]

As usual, split the remote block into direct and mediated pieces:
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{high,non}}(p)
=
Q_{\mathrm{high}}H_{\mathrm{dir}}(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}}
+
Q_{\mathrm{high}}\Delta_X(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}},
\label{eq:hn_split}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\Delta_X(p)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}S(p)S(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
S(p):=\alpha_X\mathcal J(p)+\beta_X\mathcal K(p).
\label{eq:hn_DeltaX}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact constant-shell selection assumption}

The correct theorem here is not an unconditional exact-zero theorem.
We assume only the shell-order selection that is already structurally natural in the current working branch:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_{\mathrm{high}}H_{\mathrm{dir}}(0)Q_{\mathrm{non}}=0.
}
\label{eq:hn_A1}
\end{equation}

This means that the direct high--non coupling vanishes at the shell point.
Equivalently, the first nontrivial direct contribution begins at derivative order.

For the mediated piece, we assume the one-leg shell-mismatch selection:
for every sector projector \(Q_c\) appearing in the truncated completion of identity,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_{\mathrm{high}}\mathcal J(0)Q_c=0,
\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{high}}\mathcal K(0)Q_c=0.
}
\label{eq:hn_A2}
\end{equation}

This is weaker than demanding all pairwise source blocks vanish identically.
It only says that the \emph{high-shell leg} cannot be hit at zeroth order by the source operators.
That is exactly the shell-mismatch mechanism relevant to the higher-shell sector.

\section{Finite derivative bounds}

Assume the following finite operator bounds on \(N_\rho\).

\paragraph{Direct block.}
There exists \(L_{\mathrm{dir}}^{\mathrm{hn}}<\infty\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|Q_{\mathrm{high}}H_{\mathrm{dir}}(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}}\|
\le
L_{\mathrm{dir}}^{\mathrm{hn}}\,|p|.
}
\label{eq:hn_A3}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Source operators on the high leg.}
For every sector \(c\), there exist constants
\[
L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{J},\qquad L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{K}
\]
such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|Q_{\mathrm{high}}\mathcal J(p)Q_c\|
\le
L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{J}\,|p|,
\qquad
\|Q_{\mathrm{high}}\mathcal K(p)Q_c\|
\le
L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{K}\,|p|.
}
\label{eq:hn_A4}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Bounded complementary leg.}
For every sector \(c\), there exist constants
\[
B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{J},\qquad B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{K}
\]
such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|Q_{\mathrm{non}}\mathcal J(p)Q_c\|
\le
B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{J},
\qquad
\|Q_{\mathrm{non}}\mathcal K(p)Q_c\|
\le
B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{K}.
}
\label{eq:hn_A5}
\end{equation}

These are finite because the working truncation is finite-dimensional.

\section{Direct contribution}

By \eqref{eq:hn_A3},
\begin{equation}
\|Q_{\mathrm{high}}H_{\mathrm{dir}}(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}}\|
\le
L_{\mathrm{dir}}^{\mathrm{hn}}\,|p|.
\label{eq:hn_direct_bound}
\end{equation}

So the direct high--non block is already \(O(\rho)\).

\section{Mediated contribution}

Using \eqref{eq:hn_DeltaX},
\[
Q_{\mathrm{high}}\Delta_X(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
Q_{\mathrm{high}}S(p)S(p)^\dagger Q_{\mathrm{non}}.
\]
Insert the remote-shell resolution of identity
\[
\mathbf 1=\sum_c Q_c.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
Q_{\mathrm{high}}\Delta_X(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_c
\bigl(Q_{\mathrm{high}}S(p)Q_c\bigr)
\bigl(Q_{\mathrm{non}}S(p)Q_c\bigr)^\dagger.
\label{eq:hn_med_sum}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{align}
\|Q_{\mathrm{high}}\Delta_X(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}}\|
&\le
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_c
\|Q_{\mathrm{high}}S(p)Q_c\|\,
\|Q_{\mathrm{non}}S(p)Q_c\|.
\label{eq:hn_med_norm_start}
\end{align}

Now
\[
Q_{\mathrm{high}}S(p)Q_c
=
\alpha_X\,Q_{\mathrm{high}}\mathcal J(p)Q_c
+
\beta_X\,Q_{\mathrm{high}}\mathcal K(p)Q_c,
\]
so by \eqref{eq:hn_A4},
\begin{equation}
\|Q_{\mathrm{high}}S(p)Q_c\|
\le
\bigl(
|\alpha_X|L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{J}
+
|\beta_X|L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{K}
\bigr)|p|.
\label{eq:hn_high_leg}
\end{equation}

Similarly, by \eqref{eq:hn_A5},
\begin{equation}
\|Q_{\mathrm{non}}S(p)Q_c\|
\le
|\alpha_X|B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{J}
+
|\beta_X|B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{K}.
\label{eq:hn_non_leg}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:hn_high_leg} and \eqref{eq:hn_non_leg} into \eqref{eq:hn_med_norm_start} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|Q_{\mathrm{high}}\Delta_X(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}}\|
\le
\frac{|p|}{M_X^2}
\sum_c
\bigl(
|\alpha_X|L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{J}
+
|\beta_X|L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{K}
\bigr)
\bigl(
|\alpha_X|B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{J}
+
|\beta_X|B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{K}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:hn_med_final}
\end{equation}

So the mediated high--non block is also \(O(\rho)\).

\section{Explicit \texorpdfstring{\((\mathrm{high,non})\)}{(high,non)} bound}

Combining \eqref{eq:hn_direct_bound} and \eqref{eq:hn_med_final}, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\mathrm{high,non}}
:=
L_{\mathrm{dir}}^{\mathrm{hn}}
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_c
\bigl(
|\alpha_X|L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{J}
+
|\beta_X|L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{K}
\bigr)
\bigl(
|\alpha_X|B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{J}
+
|\beta_X|B_{\mathrm{non},c}^{K}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:hn_Cdef}
\end{equation}

Then for all \(|p|\le \rho\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|R_{\mathrm{high,non}}(p)\|
\le
C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\,|p|,
}
\label{eq:hn_pointwise}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{high,non}}(p)\|
\le
C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\,\rho.
}
\label{eq:hn_rho_bound}
\end{equation}

This is the desired explicit \(O(\rho)\) bound.

\section{Quadratic improvement}

If the non-leg also vanishes linearly, i.e. if for every \(c\),
\begin{equation}
\|Q_{\mathrm{non}}\mathcal J(p)Q_c\|
\le
\widetilde L_{\mathrm{non},c}^{J}\,|p|,
\qquad
\|Q_{\mathrm{non}}\mathcal K(p)Q_c\|
\le
\widetilde L_{\mathrm{non},c}^{K}\,|p|,
\label{eq:hn_quad_assump}
\end{equation}
then the mediated block improves to
\begin{equation}
\|Q_{\mathrm{high}}\Delta_X(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}}\|
\le
\frac{|p|^2}{M_X^2}
\sum_c
\bigl(
|\alpha_X|L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{J}
+
|\beta_X|L_{\mathrm{high},c}^{K}
\bigr)
\bigl(
|\alpha_X|\widetilde L_{\mathrm{non},c}^{J}
+
|\beta_X|\widetilde L_{\mathrm{non},c}^{K}
\bigr).
\label{eq:hn_quad_med}
\end{equation}
So in this stronger case,
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
=
O(\rho)+O(\rho^2/M_X^2),
\]
and the direct block still dominates the high--non contribution.

\section{Insertion into the dominant-pair gate}

The dominant-pair Step-IV inequality was previously reduced to
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\Bigl(
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\Bigr)
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\label{eq:hn_gate_start}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:hn_rho_bound}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
+
2\,C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:hn_gate_final}
\end{equation}

Hence the high--non pair is now absorbed into an explicit \(O(\rho)\) remainder, exactly as required by the practical small-\(\rho\) program.

\section{What is actually proved}

The present theorem proves:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the high--non pair does not need to be declared identically zero;
\item under the shell-order selection on the high leg and finite derivative bounds, it is rigorously \(O(\rho)\);
\item therefore the leading Step-IV residual budget is carried by the non--wrong pair, while the high--non pair is an explicit linear remainder.
\end{enumerate}

What is not proved here is an unconditional exact-zero theorem for the high--non pair.
That stronger statement would require exact label-preservation of all relevant direct and mediated source operators at all orders.

\section{Final Summary}

Under the shell-order selection on the higher-shell leg and finite derivative bounds on the direct and mediated source operators, the high--non pair obeys the explicit linear bound
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}\le C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho.
}
\]

Therefore the dominant-pair Step-IV gate becomes
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
+
2\,C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

This proves that the high--non pair is not leading in the small-\(\rho\) regime.
The genuine leading residual pair is non--wrong, while high--non is absorbed into an explicit \(O(\rho)\) remainder.

What remains is not the structure of the theorem, but the explicit insertion of:
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho},\qquad
C_{\mathrm{high,non}},\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho},\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
\]
together with the same-shell non-enriched benchmark inside
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Full Inserted Step-IV Gate: Adding Tail and Diagonal Budgets}

\section{Goal}

The remaining Step-IV structure after the dominant-pair reduction is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
+
2\,C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\label{eq:stepIV_pre_tail_goal}
\end{equation}

The purpose of this section is to insert the explicit tail theorem and obtain the full practical Step-IV inequality in fully expanded finite form.

\section{Tail-sector decomposition}

Let the full remote space decompose as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}.
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_fullspace}
\end{equation}

Write the tail remainder as the sum over active tail sectors:
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)
=
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} R_a(p)
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}} R_a^{\mathrm{ind}}(p).
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_split}
\end{equation}

Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}\) denotes active local tail sectors;
\item \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}\) denotes active heavy-induced tail sectors.
\end{itemize}

\section{Local active tail estimate}

Assume that for every active local tail sector \(a\in \mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}\),
\begin{equation}
R_a(0)=0
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_local_zero}
\end{equation}
and the first nonzero Taylor term has order \(r_a\ge 1\).
Then there exists a finite constant \(K_a\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|R_a(p)\|\le K_a |p|^{r_a}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_local_bound}
\end{equation}

Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_a(p)\|
\le
K_a \rho^{r_a}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_local_uniform}
\end{equation}

\section{Heavy-induced tail estimate}

Let \(a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}\) be a heavy-induced tail sector generated through a heavy auxiliary block of gap \(M_a\), with induced form
\begin{equation}
R_a^{\mathrm{ind}}(p,E)
=
X_a(p)\bigl(H_a^{(H)}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}Y_a(p).
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_heavy_form}
\end{equation}

Assume
\begin{equation}
\|X_a(p)\|\le A_a |p|^{m_a},
\qquad
\|Y_a(p)\|\le B_a |p|^{n_a},
\qquad
m_a+n_a=r_a\ge 1,
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_heavy_assump}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
|E|<\frac{M_a}{2}.
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_heavy_energy}
\end{equation}
Then the heavy resolvent obeys
\begin{equation}
\|(H_a^{(H)}(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2}{M_a},
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_heavy_resolvent}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|R_a^{\mathrm{ind}}(p,E)\|
\le
\frac{2A_aB_a}{M_a}|p|^{r_a}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_heavy_bound}
\end{equation}

Therefore there exist constants \(\widetilde K_a\) and integers \(\sigma_a\ge 1\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_a^{\mathrm{ind}}(p,E)\|
\le
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_heavy_uniform}
\end{equation}

\section{Uniform tail budget}

Summing \eqref{eq:stepIV_tail_local_uniform} and \eqref{eq:stepIV_tail_heavy_uniform} over all active sectors gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_tail_master}
\end{equation}

This is the exact tail insertion required in Step IV.

\section{Diagonal correction budget}

If the benchmark diagonal block \(D_R(p)\) receives additional bounded corrections, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{diag\ corr}}(p)\|.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_diag_def}
\end{equation}

No further structure is required here beyond finiteness.
It enters the gate additively.

\section{Inserted dominant-pair inequality}

Recall the explicit non--wrong bound
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\le
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right),
\label{eq:stepIV_nonwrong_recall}
\end{equation}
and the explicit high--non bound
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
\le
C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho.
\label{eq:stepIV_highnon_recall}
\end{equation}

Therefore the dominant-pair residual budget satisfies
\begin{align}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
&\le
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
+
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
\\
&\le
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\label{eq:stepIV_rem_inserted}
\end{align}

Substituting \eqref{eq:stepIV_tail_master}, we obtain the fully inserted residual bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_full_residual_inserted}
\end{equation}

\section{Full inserted Step-IV theorem}

Recall the benchmark side
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:stepIV_bench_recall_full}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Fully inserted Step-IV gate]
If
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
}
\nonumber\\
\boxed{
\qquad\qquad
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
}
\label{eq:stepIV_final_inserted_gate}
\end{align}
then the remote sector has a uniform positive gap on \(N_\rho\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_final_inserted_gap}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The residual side is bounded by \eqref{eq:stepIV_full_residual_inserted}.
Therefore condition \eqref{eq:stepIV_final_inserted_gate} implies
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
By the uniform Bloch-spectral lower-bound theorem for the remote block, this yields
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}>0.
\]
This proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\section{Schur-complement consequence}

Assume in addition that Step III has already been closed:
\begin{equation}
V_{DR}(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|.
\label{eq:stepIV_final_VDR}
\end{equation}
Then for
\[
|E|<\frac{\Delta_\rho}{2},
\]
the remote resolvent exists and satisfies
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2}{\Delta_\rho}.
\label{eq:stepIV_final_resolvent}
\end{equation}
Hence the Schur self-energy obeys
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta_\rho}|p|^2,
}
\label{eq:stepIV_final_sigma}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
}
\label{eq:stepIV_final_Heff}
\end{equation}

Thus, once the fully inserted gate \eqref{eq:stepIV_final_inserted_gate} is verified,
the remote sector cannot destroy the principal linear Dirac block.

\section{What remains after this theorem}

After the present theorem, the Step-IV frontier is no longer structural.
The only remaining inputs are finite coefficient insertions:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the same-shell non-enriched benchmark
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)};
\]
\item the explicit constant \(C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\);
\item the tail coefficients \(K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,\sigma_a\);
\item the diagonal correction budget \(\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

So Step IV is now fully reduced to a finite inserted inequality problem.

\section{Final Summary}

The Step-IV residual side is now fully inserted.

The dominant truncated remote pairs satisfy
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\le
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right),
\]
and
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}\le C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho.
\]

The tail contribution satisfies
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\]
while the diagonal correction is
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{diag\ corr}}(p)\|.
\]

Therefore the fully inserted Step-IV sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

If this holds, then
\[
\Delta_\rho>0,
\qquad
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta_\rho},
\qquad
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right),
\]
so the remote sector cannot destroy the principal massless Dirac block.

What remains is no longer structural.
Only the finite insertion of
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\quad
C_{\mathrm{high,non}},
\quad
K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,\sigma_a,
\quad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
\]
is still needed.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Closure of the Same-Shell Non-Enriched Benchmark}

\section{Goal}

The only unresolved benchmark-side slot in Step IV is the same-shell non-enriched sector.
We now close it by reducing the exact benchmark to a finite Hermitian eigenvalue problem plus a truncation error.

\section{Exact same-shell non-enriched operator}

Let
\begin{equation}
Q_{\mathrm{non}}
\label{eq:non_qnon}
\end{equation}
denote the orthogonal projector onto the same-shell complementary sector which excludes the enriched doublet.

Define the exact same-shell non-enriched operator by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)
:=
Q_{\mathrm{non}}\,H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\,Q_{\mathrm{non}},
\qquad |p|\le \rho.
}
\label{eq:non_exact_operator}
\end{equation}

Its exact benchmark gap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non}}(p))\bigr).
}
\label{eq:non_exact_gap}
\end{equation}

This is the exact object which must enter the master benchmark.

\section{Finite truncation}

Choose an \(N\)-dimensional trial space
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}\subset \operatorname{Ran}(Q_{\mathrm{non}})
\]
with isometric embedding
\[
\iota_N:\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}\hookrightarrow \operatorname{Ran}(Q_{\mathrm{non}}).
\]

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)
:=
\iota_N^*\,H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)\,\iota_N.
}
\label{eq:non_truncated_operator}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, if one first truncates the shell block, one may write
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)
=
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}.
\label{eq:non_truncated_shell_form}
\end{equation}

Since \(H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)\) is finite-dimensional and Hermitian for each \(p\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p))
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:non_finite_gap}
\end{equation}

\section{Truncation error budget}

Define the uniform truncation error by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)
-
\iota_N H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)\iota_N^*
\right\|.
}
\label{eq:non_trunc_error}
\end{equation}

This is the exact error quantity controlling the upgrade from the finite truncation to the exact operator.

\section{Spectral perturbation lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Distance to zero under bounded Hermitian perturbation]
Let \(A\) and \(B\) be self-adjoint operators on the same Hilbert space such that
\[
\|A-B\|\le \varepsilon.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(A)\bigr)
\ge
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(B)\bigr)-\varepsilon.
}
\label{eq:non_perturb_lemma}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For self-adjoint \(B\), one has
\[
\|(B-\lambda)\psi\|
\ge
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(\lambda,\operatorname{spec}(B)\bigr)\|\psi\|.
\]
At \(\lambda=0\),
\[
\|B\psi\|
\ge
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(B)\bigr)\|\psi\|.
\]
Hence
\[
\|A\psi\|
\ge
\|B\psi\|-\|(A-B)\psi\|
\ge
\Bigl(
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(B)\bigr)-\varepsilon
\Bigr)\|\psi\|.
\]
Taking the infimum over unit vectors \(\psi\) gives \eqref{eq:non_perturb_lemma}.
\end{proof}

\section{Truncation-to-exact upgrade theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Same-shell non-enriched finite-to-exact upgrade]
For the exact same-shell non-enriched benchmark \eqref{eq:non_exact_gap}, the finite truncation gap \eqref{eq:non_finite_gap}, and the truncation error \eqref{eq:non_trunc_error}, one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\label{eq:non_upgrade_main}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
}
\label{eq:non_upgrade_positive_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:non_upgrade_positive}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix \(|p|\le \rho\). Apply the perturbation lemma with
\[
A=H_{\mathrm{non}}(p),
\qquad
B=\iota_N H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)\iota_N^*.
\]
Then
\[
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non}}(p))\bigr)
\ge
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p))
\bigr)
-
\left\|
H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)-\iota_N H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)\iota_N^*
\right\|.
\]
Now take the infimum over \(|p|\le \rho\) on the left-hand side and the corresponding uniform lower/upper bounds on the right-hand side.
This gives exactly
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]
If \eqref{eq:non_upgrade_positive_cond} holds, then the right-hand side is strictly positive, so \eqref{eq:non_upgrade_positive} follows.
\end{proof}

\section{Usable benchmark entry}

Therefore the correct usable benchmark entry for the same-shell non-enriched sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\label{eq:non_usable_entry}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the quantity that must be inserted into the master benchmark.

\section{Computable finite realization}

The actual finite computation is now reduced to the following explicit steps:

\begin{enumerate}
\item choose a truncated same-shell non-enriched basis
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)};
\]

\item compute the finite Hermitian matrix
\[
\mathbf H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p);
\]

\item compute
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_j |\lambda_j^{(N)}(p)|,
}
\label{eq:non_finite_realization}
\end{equation}
where \(\lambda_j^{(N)}(p)\) are the eigenvalues of \(\mathbf H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)\);

\item compute or bound
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)};
\]

\item form the exact usable quantity
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{Optional Gershgorin lower bound}

If one wants an inexpensive sufficient lower bound before diagonalizing the matrix, one may use Gershgorin.
Write
\[
\mathbf H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)=\bigl(h_{ij}(p)\bigr)_{i,j=1}^N.
\]
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(G,N)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min_i
\left(
|h_{ii}(p)|-\sum_{j\neq i}|h_{ij}(p)|
\right).
}
\label{eq:non_gershgorin}
\end{equation}
If
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(G,N)}>0,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(G,N)}.
\label{eq:non_gershgorin_lower}
\end{equation}
Hence one may replace the exact finite eigenvalue computation by a purely entrywise sufficient bound whenever useful.

\section{Insertion into the master benchmark}

Recall the working master benchmark
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:non_master_bench}
\end{equation}

Therefore the benchmark side of Step IV is now completely reduced to finite explicit data.

\section{Consequence for the full Step-IV gate}

Combining \eqref{eq:non_master_bench} with the previously derived fully inserted residual budget, the final Step-IV sufficient condition is
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
}
\nonumber\\
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:non_final_stepIV_gate}
\end{align}

If this holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\label{eq:non_final_gap}
\end{equation}

\section{What is now actually left}

After the present theorem, the benchmark side is no longer conceptually open.
Its only remaining task is computational:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }
\mathbf H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p),
\quad
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\quad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\label{eq:non_final_left}
\end{equation}

Thus the same-shell non-enriched slot is fully reduced to one finite Hermitian matrix computation plus one truncation-error estimate.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Inserted Remote-Gap Theorem for the Current Working Branch}

\section{Goal}

We now combine the benchmark side and the fully inserted residual side into one final Step-IV theorem.

The purpose is to obtain a single practical sufficient condition implying:

\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right),
\]
so that the remote sector cannot destroy the principal massless Dirac block.

\section{Benchmark side}

Recall the fully reduced working benchmark
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_benchmark}
\end{equation}

Here the same-shell non-enriched term is obtained from the exact lower bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_nonenr}
\end{equation}

\section{Residual side}

The full residual remote budget is decomposed as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_residual_split}
\end{equation}

After the dominant-pair reduction and the explicit tail insertion, the residual side satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_residual}
\end{equation}

\section{Final inserted Step-IV theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Final inserted remote-gap theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-level enriched carrier block has already been isolated;

\item Step III holds:
\begin{equation}
V_{DR}(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho);
\label{eq:final_inserted_stepIII}
\end{equation}

\item the benchmark side is given by \eqref{eq:final_inserted_benchmark};

\item the residual side satisfies \eqref{eq:final_inserted_residual}.
\end{enumerate}

If
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
}
\nonumber\\
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}
>
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
}
\nonumber\\
\boxed{
\qquad\qquad
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_gate}
\end{align}
then the remote block has a uniform positive spectral gap:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho),
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_gap_spec}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_gap_value}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:final_inserted_nonenr}, the same-shell non-enriched benchmark is bounded below by
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]
Therefore every benchmark contribution entering \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}\) is an explicit lower bound for the corresponding remote sector.

On the residual side, \eqref{eq:final_inserted_residual_split} and \eqref{eq:final_inserted_residual} provide an explicit upper bound for the full remote remainder norm \(\eta_{R,\rho}\).

Hence condition \eqref{eq:final_inserted_gate} implies
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]
By the uniform remote-gap criterion for the block decomposition
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\]
this yields
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:final_inserted_gap_spec} and \eqref{eq:final_inserted_gap_value}.
\end{proof}

\section{Schur-complement corollary}

\begin{corollary}[Remote sector is subleading in the effective shell theory]
Under the assumptions of the theorem, and for
\[
|E|<\frac{\Delta_\rho}{2},
\]
the remote resolvent exists and obeys
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta_\rho}.
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_resolvent}
\end{equation}
Therefore the Schur self-energy
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=V_{DR}(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V_{DR}(p)^\dagger
\]
satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta_\rho}|p|^2,
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_sigma}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_Heff}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The resolvent estimate follows from the spectral gap \eqref{eq:final_inserted_gap_spec}.
Then Step III gives
\[
\|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
so
\[
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\|V_{DR}(p)\|^2\,\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
c^2|p|^2\cdot \frac{2}{\Delta_\rho}.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:final_inserted_sigma}, and \eqref{eq:final_inserted_Heff} follows immediately.
\end{proof}

\section{What this theorem actually closes}

The theorem closes Step IV at the theorem-reduction level completely.

What remains is no longer structural.
Only the explicit insertion of the finite constants remains:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\quad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\quad
C_{\mathrm{high,non}},
\quad
K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,\sigma_a,
\quad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]

Thus the current working branch now satisfies the following honest statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Step IV is fully closed as a single inserted finite inequality.}
}
\label{eq:final_inserted_closed}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The benchmark side and the residual side of Step IV are now fully unified.

The benchmark side is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\]

The residual side is bounded by
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]

Therefore the final inserted Step-IV sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]
In explicit fully inserted form, this is exactly equation \eqref{eq:final_inserted_gate} above.

If it holds, then the remote block has a uniform positive gap
\[
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0,
\]
and, together with
\[
V_{DR}(0)=0,\qquad \|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
the Schur self-energy satisfies
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
\]
Hence
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right),
\]
so the remote sector cannot destroy the principal massless Dirac block.

Thus Step IV is now fully closed at the theorem-reduction level.
What remains is only the explicit insertion of the finite constants
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\quad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\quad
C_{\mathrm{high,non}},
\quad
K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,\sigma_a,
\quad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]

\section{Full Practical Acceptance Theorem for the Current Refined Locked + Class II Branch}

\section{Purpose}

We now combine:

\[
\text{Gate 2: longitudinal survival},

\qquad
\text{Step III: zero constant mixing},
\]
\[
\text{Step IV: positive remote gap},
\qquad

into one final practical accept/reject theorem for the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch.

\section{Carrier-side hypotheses}

Assume the practical longitudinal block:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0,
\qquad

\section{Remote-sector hypotheses}

Assume Step III:

V_{DR}(0)=0,

\qquad
(|p|\le \rho).

\label{eq:full_accept_stepIII}

Assume the fully inserted Step-IV inequality:
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|

\nonumber\\

-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}

>

+

\left(

\right)
\right]
}
\nonumber\\
\boxed{
\qquad\qquad
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:full_accept_stepIV}
\end{align}

Then the remote block has a uniform positive gap:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.

\end{equation}

Moreover, for \(|E|<\Delta_\rho/2\),

\boxed{
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta_\rho}|p|^2,
\qquad
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
}
\label{eq:full_accept_schur}
\end{equation}

Let the exact constant Dirac-mass space be

\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.

U(1)_V
\quad\text{or already}\quad

\end{equation}

\section{Final practical accept theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Full practical acceptance theorem]
If \eqref{eq:full_accept_long}, \eqref{eq:full_accept_trans}, \eqref{eq:full_accept_stepIII}, \eqref{eq:full_accept_stepIV}, and \eqref{eq:full_accept_gate4} all hold, then the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is accepted as a
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{practically viable, spectrally isolated, mass-protected anisotropic massless Dirac branch.}
}
\label{eq:full_accept_main}
\end{equation}

More explicitly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell carrier is nondegenerate:
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0);
\]

\item the remote sector is uniformly gapped:
\[
\Delta_\rho>0;
\]

\item the remote Schur correction is subleading:
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right);
\]

\item no symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass survives:
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the effective low-energy shell theory has the protected principal form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right),

where \(H_D(p)\) is an anisotropic massless Dirac block with
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}>0.

\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:full_accept_long} and \eqref{eq:full_accept_trans}, Gate 2 and Gate 3 pass, hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).

So the isolated shell block defines a nondegenerate anisotropic massless Dirac carrier.

By \eqref{eq:full_accept_stepIII} and \eqref{eq:full_accept_stepIV}, the remote-gap theorem applies. Therefore
\[
\Delta_\rho>0,
\]
and the remote Schur contribution satisfies
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
\]
Hence the remote sector cannot alter the principal linear Dirac symbol.

Finally, \eqref{eq:full_accept_gate4} excludes every symmetry-allowed constant operator in the exact mass space \(\mathcal M_D\). Therefore no constant gap-opening Dirac mass is permitted.

Combining the three conclusions yields \eqref{eq:full_accept_main} and \eqref{eq:full_accept_principal}.
\end{proof}

\section{Reject theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Practical reject theorem]
The current branch must be rejected at the corresponding level if any one of the following fails:

\item if Gate 3 fails, then \((\alpha,\beta)=(0,0)\), so the transverse carrier channel is absent;

\item if Gate 4 fails, i.e.
\[

\]
then the branch may still define a carrier, but it is not accepted as a protected massless Dirac branch.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\section{Honest status statement}

The theorem above is the strongest honest \emph{working-branch practical theorem} presently available.

What is closed:

\item the exact mass-space classification;

What is still not inserted:

\end{enumerate}

Therefore the correct final wording is:
\begin{equation}

\text{the full practical acceptance theorem is closed,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{its actual branch verification still requires finite explicit insertions.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is accepted at the practical level if and only if the following three layers all pass:

\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,

What remains is no longer structural.

\section{Actual Corrected-Block Residual-Symmetry Audit for Gate 4}

\section{Goal}

The mass-space classification is already closed.
The remaining problem is not to identify possible masses, but to prove that the \emph{actual corrected constant block} cannot contain any element of the actual mass space.

In the actual canonical shell basis, the remaining audit is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_audit_goal}
\end{equation}

If all three hold, then Gate 4 passes.

\section{Actual canonical basis and actual mass space}

The actual projected shell block is brought to the canonical massless form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau_1\otimes s_2.
\label{eq:G4_actual_Hcore}
\end{equation}

Its exact residual generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_Qstar}
\end{equation}
and the transported actual mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{M_1,M_2\},
\qquad
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_Mactual}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact \texorpdfstring{$Q_*$}{Q*}-commutant}

Let
\[
\mathcal B=\{\tau_a\otimes s_b:\ a,b\in\{0,1,2,3\}\}
\]
be the Hermitian operator basis, with \(\tau_0=s_0=\mathbf 1_2\).

Define
\[
\epsilon(0)=\epsilon(3)=+1,
\qquad
\epsilon(1)=\epsilon(2)=-1.
\]
Then
\[
\tau_3\tau_a=\epsilon(a)\tau_a\tau_3,
\qquad
s_3s_b=\epsilon(b)s_bs_3.
\]
Hence
\begin{align}
[Q_*,\tau_a\otimes s_b]
&=
[\tau_3\otimes s_3,\tau_a\otimes s_b]
\\
&=
\bigl(\epsilon(a)\epsilon(b)-1\bigr)\,
\tau_a\tau_3\otimes s_bs_3.
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
[Q_*,\tau_a\otimes s_b]=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\epsilon(a)\epsilon(b)=1.
\label{eq:G4_actual_comm_criterion}
\end{equation}

So the exact \(Q_*\)-commuting Hermitian constant algebra is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\mathbf 1_2\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_3\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_CQ}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact exclusion of the actual mass space}

Now
\[
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
\epsilon(2)\epsilon(0)=-1,
\]
and
\[
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
\epsilon(1)\epsilon(3)=-1.
\]
Hence neither \(M_1\) nor \(M_2\) commutes with \(Q_*\).

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_intersection_zero}
\end{equation}

This is the decisive algebraic fact:
every exact constant correction preserving \(Q_*\) is automatically non-mass-generating.

\section{Source I: scalar constant sector}

At this stage one must separate the scalar identity-channel problem from the Dirac mass problem.

The scalar identity-channel Bragg obstruction is a distinct constant-sector issue and must already have been removed before the final protected Dirac conclusion is claimed.
So, after scalar cancellation, the remaining scalar constant block is assumed to be \(Q_*\)-neutral:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_scalar_neutral}
\end{equation}

This is not a new mass-classification problem.
It is exactly the assumption that the dangerous scalar identity channel has been removed while preserving the derivative shell symbol.

\section{Source II: Class II constant sector}

For the canonical minimal Class II correction, the shell-level coefficients are only renormalized:
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J.
\]
So the corrected shell block remains of the same derivative Dirac form and does not insert an independent constant shell-level mass operator.

Transported to the actual canonical basis, this means that the Class II constant contribution is either zero or \(Q_*\)-neutral, and in particular
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_classII_neutral}
\end{equation}

\section{Source III: remote self-energy}

The genuinely nontrivial microscopic issue is remote-sector inheritance.

If the full microscopic theory preserves the same residual symmetry and the remote elimination preserves it as well, then the Schur-complement self-energy inherits the same generator:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_sigma_neutral}
\end{equation}

Under transported little-group scalarity, this further restricts the zero-momentum self-energy to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=\tilde a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+\tilde a_*\,Q_*.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_sigma_form}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\label{eq:G4_actual_sigma_nomass}
\end{equation}

\section{Combined actual audit theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Actual corrected-block Gate-4 closure]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the projected shell block has been reduced to the actual canonical form \eqref{eq:G4_actual_Hcore};

\item the dangerous scalar identity-channel block has been removed, so that
\[
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0;
\]

\item the corrected Class II constant block preserves the same \(Q_*\), i.e.
\[
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0;
\]

\item remote elimination preserves the same exact residual generator, so that
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then the full corrected constant sector
\begin{equation}
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\Sigma(0,0)
\label{eq:G4_actual_dHconst}
\end{equation}
belongs to the \(Q_*\)-commutant:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*}.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_dH_in_CQ}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_no_mass}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, Gate 4 passes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_gate4_pass}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By assumptions (2)–(4), each exact constant source commutes with \(Q_*\).
Hence their sum \(\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\) also commutes with \(Q_*\), so
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*}.
\]
But by \eqref{eq:G4_actual_intersection_zero},
\[
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\]
Therefore \(\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\) cannot contain any component along the actual mass generators \(M_1\) or \(M_2\).
This proves
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\]
Hence no exact constant Dirac mass can appear in the corrected projected shell block.
\end{proof}

\section{Transport back to the standard doubled basis}

Let \(U_{\mathrm{can}}\) be the unitary basis change transporting the standard doubled basis to the actual canonical basis.
Then
\[
Q_*=U_{\mathrm{can}}Q_VU_{\mathrm{can}}^{-1},
\qquad
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=U_{\mathrm{can}}\mathcal M_DU_{\mathrm{can}}^{-1}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\label{eq:G4_actual_transport_back}
\end{equation}

So the actual-basis audit is exactly the transported version of the original Gate-4 criterion.

\section{What is actually proved and what remains open}

What is proved here is complete algebraic closure of the actual corrected-block audit:
if the same exact residual generator \(Q_*\) survives all constant corrections and remote elimination, then no constant actual mass can appear.

What remains open is not the classification of masses or the form of the audit.
The only remaining microscopic question is:

\text{does the final complete corrected microscopic realization preserve the same exact }Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3\text{ symmetry?}
}
\label{eq:G4_actual_last_open}
\end{equation}

Thus Gate 4 is no longer conceptually open.
It is a finite source-by-source symmetry-preservation audit on the actual corrected block.

\section{Final Summary}

In the actual canonical shell basis, the residual generator and the actual mass space are
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\qquad
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
\]

The exact \(Q_*\)-commuting constant algebra is

\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=

\mathbf 1_4,\,

\tau_3\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\},
\]
and it satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\]

Therefore any exact constant correction preserving the same \(Q_*\) is automatically non-mass-generating.

If the scalar identity-channel obstruction has been removed, the corrected Class II constant block preserves \(Q_*\), and remote elimination also preserves \(Q_*\), then
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\Sigma(0,0)
\in \mathcal C_{Q_*},
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
}
\]
so Gate 4 passes on the actual corrected block.

Thus the remaining Gate-4 frontier is no longer algebraic.
It is the finite microscopic check of whether the final complete corrected realization preserves the same exact residual generator
\[
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}

\section{The True Final Frontier: Exact Remote-Symmetry Inheritance}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At this stage, the only logically independent remaining microscopic issue is whether the full corrected microscopic realization preserves the same exact residual generator \(Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3\) through remote-sector elimination.

Everything else has already been reduced:
the carrier-side theorem is closed,
the remote-gap theorem is closed as a finite inserted inequality,
and the actual mass-space classification is closed.

So the only remaining frontier is the exact symmetry-inheritance problem
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]

\section{Precise formulation of the frontier}

Let the full corrected microscopic block at the crossing be written as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_L(p) & W(p)\\
W(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:frontier_full_block}
\end{equation}
where \(H_L\) acts on the actual shell carrier block and \(H_R\) acts on the remote sector.

The Schur-complement self-energy is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0):=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger.
\label{eq:frontier_sigma00}
\end{equation}

The actual residual generator on the shell carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:frontier_Qstar}
\end{equation}

The true final frontier is exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0\ ? 
}
\label{eq:frontier_true_question}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact sufficient criterion}

The correct sufficient criterion is not mysterious.
It is the existence of a remote-sector generator \(Q_R\) such that the full microscopic corrected block preserves the direct-sum symmetry
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_{\mathrm{full}}:=Q_*\oplus Q_R,
\qquad
[Q_{\mathrm{full}},H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)]=0.
}
\label{eq:frontier_Qfull}
\end{equation}

Expanding \eqref{eq:frontier_Qfull} blockwise gives
\begin{equation}
[Q_*,H_L(p)]=0,
\label{eq:frontier_low_comm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
[Q_R,H_R(p)]=0,
\label{eq:frontier_remote_comm}
\end{equation}
and the intertwiner condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*W(p)=W(p)Q_R.
}
\label{eq:frontier_intertwiner}
\end{equation}

Since \([Q_R,H_R(p)]=0\), one has
\begin{equation}
Q_R(\omega-H_R(p))^{-1}=(\omega-H_R(p))^{-1}Q_R.
\label{eq:frontier_resolvent}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{align}
Q_*\Sigma(0,0)
&=
Q_*W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
W(0)Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_R W(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger Q_*
\\
&=
\Sigma(0,0)Q_*.
\end{align}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:frontier_sigma_comm}
\end{equation}

\section{Why this solves Gate 4}

In the actual canonical shell basis, the actual mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
}
\label{eq:frontier_Mactual}
\end{equation}

But the exact \(Q_*\)-commutant satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:frontier_commutant_zero}
\end{equation}

So once
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\]
the remote self-energy is automatically excluded from the actual mass space.
Therefore the remote source passes the mass audit.

\section{The last executable theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Final executable Gate-4 frontier]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the dangerous scalar identity-channel constant block has been removed;
\item the Class II constant correction preserves the actual shell generator \(Q_*\);
\item there exists a Hermitian remote-sector generator \(Q_R\) such that
\[
[Q_*\oplus Q_R,\ H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)]=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:frontier_final_gate4}
\end{equation}
So Gate 4 passes.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The scalar and Class II constant sectors are \(Q_*\)-neutral by assumption.
The third assumption implies the blockwise intertwiner condition and the remote resolvent covariance, so \([Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0\).
Since every \(Q_*\)-commuting constant operator lies in the commutant \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\), and \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}\), no actual constant Dirac mass can be generated.
\end{proof}

\section{What is genuinely left}

Thus the final microscopic problem is not to classify masses.
That is already done.

It is also not to guess the symmetry.
The actual symmetry generator is already explicit:
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
\]

The only remaining task is the finite execution problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{construct }Q_R\text{ and verify }Q_*W=WQ_R,\ [Q_R,H_R]=0
\text{ on the full corrected microscopic realization.}
}
\label{eq:frontier_last_execution}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The true final frontier is exactly the remote-symmetry inheritance condition
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\qquad
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\]

A sufficient and executable microscopic criterion is the existence of a Hermitian remote-sector generator \(Q_R\) such that
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*\oplus Q_R,\ H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)]=0.
}
\]
Blockwise, this is equivalent to
\[
[Q_*,H_L]=0,
\qquad
[Q_R,H_R]=0,
\qquad
Q_*W=WQ_R.
\]

Under this condition, the Schur self-energy satisfies
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\]

Since the actual mass space
\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_1\otimes s_3\}
\]
has trivial intersection with the exact \(Q_*\)-commutant,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
}
\]
the remote self-energy cannot generate an actual constant Dirac mass.

Therefore the final Gate-4 frontier is no longer algebraic.
It is the finite microscopic execution problem:
\[
\boxed{
\text{construct }Q_R\text{ and verify }Q_*W=WQ_R,\ [Q_R,H_R]=0.
}
\]
