\section{Constructive Proof of the Final Frontier}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The true final frontier is the exact remote-symmetry inheritance condition
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\qquad
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
\]

There are two rigorous routes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a strongest trivial route: if the exact corrected low--remote mixing still satisfies \(W(0)=0\), then \(\Sigma(0,0)=0\) automatically;

\item a constructive symmetry route: if the remote sector can be decomposed into exact \(Q_*\)-charge sectors preserved by \(H_R(0)\), then one can explicitly construct \(Q_R\) and prove
\[
Q_*W(0)=W(0)Q_R,
\qquad
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\]
hence
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{Setup}

Let the corrected microscopic block at the crossing be
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_L(0) & W(0)\\
W(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:finalfrontier_full}
\end{equation}
where \(H_L(0)\) acts on the actual shell carrier block and \(H_R(0)\) acts on the remote sector.

The Schur self-energy is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0):=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger.
\label{eq:finalfrontier_sigma}
\end{equation}

The actual shell generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\qquad
Q_*^2=\mathbf 1.
}
\label{eq:finalfrontier_Qstar}
\end{equation}
Define the shell charge projectors
\begin{equation}
P_\pm:=\frac{1}{2}(\mathbf 1\pm Q_*).
\label{eq:finalfrontier_Ppm}
\end{equation}

\section{Route A: exact zero-mixing persistence}

\begin{proposition}[Trivial closure route]
If the exact corrected realization satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W(0)=0,
}
\label{eq:routeA_Wzero}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:routeA_sigmazero}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By definition,
\[
\Sigma(0,0)=W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger.
\]
If \(W(0)=0\), then \(\Sigma(0,0)=0\) identically.
Hence \([Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0\) is immediate.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
So if the Step-III exact zero-mixing statement persists all the way to the final corrected microscopic realization, then the final frontier is already closed.

\section{Route B: constructive charge-sector proof}

Now assume \(W(0)\) is not manifestly zero, so we must prove symmetry inheritance directly.

\subsection{Remote charge decomposition}

Assume the remote space admits an orthogonal decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_R^{(+)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_R^{(-)}
\oplus
\mathcal K,
}
\label{eq:routeB_remote_decomp}
\end{equation}
with orthogonal projectors
\[
R_+,\qquad R_-,\qquad R_0,
\qquad
R_++R_-+R_0=\mathbf 1_R.
\]

Assume further that the corrected remote Hamiltonian preserves this decomposition:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[R_+,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
[R_-,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
[R_0,H_R(0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:routeB_remote_preserve}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
H_R(0)
=
H_R^{(+)}\oplus H_R^{(-)}\oplus H_R^{(0)}.
\label{eq:routeB_remote_blockdiag}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Charge-preserving coupling assumption}

Assume the corrected low--remote coupling respects shell charge:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W(0)=P_+W(0)R_+ + P_-W(0)R_-.
}
\label{eq:routeB_W_charge}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
P_+W(0)R_-=0,
\qquad
P_-W(0)R_+=0,
\qquad
W(0)R_0=0.
\label{eq:routeB_W_crosszero}
\end{equation}

This says that only matching charge sectors couple at zero momentum.

\subsection{Explicit construction of \texorpdfstring{$Q_R$}{QR}}

Define the remote operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_R:=R_+ - R_- + Q_0,
}
\label{eq:routeB_QR_def}
\end{equation}
where \(Q_0\) is any Hermitian involution on \(\mathcal K\) satisfying
\begin{equation}
Q_0^2=R_0,
\qquad
[Q_0,H_R^{(0)}]=0.
\label{eq:routeB_Q0}
\end{equation}

Then \(Q_R\) is Hermitian, \(Q_R^2=\mathbf 1_R\), and by construction
\begin{equation}
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0.
\label{eq:routeB_QR_comm_HR}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Intertwiner identity}

We now prove
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*W(0)=W(0)Q_R.
}
\label{eq:routeB_intertwiner_goal}
\end{equation}

Indeed, using \eqref{eq:routeB_W_charge},
\begin{align}
Q_*W(0)
&=
Q_*P_+W(0)R_+ + Q_*P_-W(0)R_-
\\
&=
(+1)P_+W(0)R_+ + (-1)P_-W(0)R_-
\\
&=
P_+W(0)R_+ - P_-W(0)R_-.
\label{eq:routeB_left}
\end{align}
On the other hand,
\begin{align}
W(0)Q_R
&=
W(0)(R_+ - R_- + Q_0)
\\
&=
W(0)R_+ - W(0)R_- + W(0)R_0Q_0
\\
&=
P_+W(0)R_+ - P_-W(0)R_-,
\label{eq:routeB_right}
\end{align}
because \(W(0)R_0=0\) and \(W(0)R_\pm=P_\pm W(0)R_\pm\).
Comparing \eqref{eq:routeB_left} and \eqref{eq:routeB_right} yields \eqref{eq:routeB_intertwiner_goal}.

\subsection{Resolvent covariance}

Since \([Q_R,H_R(0)]=0\), the inverse remote block also commutes with \(Q_R\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}
=
\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_R.
}
\label{eq:routeB_resolvent}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Exact proof of \texorpdfstring{$[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0$}{[Q*,Sigma(0,0)]=0}}

Now compute:
\begin{align}
Q_*\Sigma(0,0)
&=
Q_*W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
W(0)Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\qquad\text{by \eqref{eq:routeB_intertwiner_goal}}
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_R W(0)^\dagger
\qquad\text{by \eqref{eq:routeB_resolvent}}
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger Q_*
\qquad\text{by adjoint of \eqref{eq:routeB_intertwiner_goal}}
\\
&=
\Sigma(0,0)Q_*.
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:routeB_sigma_comm}
\end{equation}

This proves the frontier.

\section{Sectorwise version adapted to the working truncation}

For the present working truncation,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\label{eq:routeB_working_remote}
\end{equation}
the executable version is to refine each sector into shell-charge pieces:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_a
=
\mathcal H_a^{(+)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_a^{(-)}
\oplus
\mathcal K_a,
\qquad
a\in
\{\mathrm{vol},\mathrm{high},\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}\}.
}
\label{eq:routeB_sector_refine}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
Q_R
=
\bigoplus_a
\left(
+1\cdot R_{a,+}
\;-\;
1\cdot R_{a,-}
\;+\;
Q_{a,0}
\right),
\label{eq:routeB_sectorwise_QR}
\end{equation}
with \(Q_{a,0}\) any Hermitian involution commuting with \(H_R|_{\mathcal K_a}\).

If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[H_R(0),R_{a,\pm}]=0
\quad\text{for all }a,
}
\label{eq:routeB_sector_preserve}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W(0)=\sum_a \bigl(P_+W(0)R_{a,+}+P_-W(0)R_{a,-}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:routeB_sector_coupling}
\end{equation}
then the previous proof applies verbatim and gives
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]

\section{Why this is enough for Gate 4}

The actual mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
}
\label{eq:routeB_massspace}
\end{equation}
But the exact \(Q_*\)-commutant has trivial intersection with it:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:routeB_intersection}
\end{equation}

Therefore \eqref{eq:routeB_sigma_comm} implies
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\label{eq:routeB_sigma_nomass}
\end{equation}
So the remote source passes Gate 4.

\section{Final statement}

\begin{theorem}[Actual executable form of the last frontier]
The final microscopic frontier is closed as soon as one proves either:

\paragraph{Route A.}
\[
W(0)=0,
\]
which implies \(\Sigma(0,0)=0\); or

\paragraph{Route B.}
there exists an exact sectorwise remote charge decomposition such that
\[
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
Q_*W(0)=W(0)Q_R.
\]
In either case,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\qquad
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:routeB_final}
\end{equation}
Hence the remote self-energy cannot generate a constant Dirac mass.
\end{theorem}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Constructive Sectorwise Proof of Remote-Symmetry Inheritance}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now prove the final frontier in an executable form adapted to the actual working truncation.

The shell generator is already fixed:
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
\]
So the only remaining task is to construct a remote-sector symmetry generator \(Q_R\) such that
\[
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
Q_*W(0)=W(0)Q_R.
\]
Once these are proved, the Schur self-energy automatically satisfies
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]

\section{Working-truncation block structure}

At \(p=0\), write the corrected full microscopic block as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_L(0) & W(0)\\
W(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:constructive_full_block}
\end{equation}
where the remote sector is the working truncation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
}
\label{eq:constructive_remote_working}
\end{equation}

The shell generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\qquad
Q_*^2=\mathbf 1_4.
}
\label{eq:constructive_Qstar}
\end{equation}
Let
\begin{equation}
P_\pm:=\frac12(\mathbf 1_4\pm Q_*).
\label{eq:constructive_Ppm}
\end{equation}

The Schur self-energy is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0)=W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger.
\label{eq:constructive_sigma}
\end{equation}

\section{Sectorwise charge data}

For each remote sector
\[
a\in\{\mathrm{vol},\mathrm{high},\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}\},
\]
assume an orthogonal decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_a
=
\mathcal H_a^{(+)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_a^{(-)}
\oplus
\mathcal K_a,
}
\label{eq:constructive_sector_split}
\end{equation}
with orthogonal projectors
\[
R_{a,+},\qquad R_{a,-},\qquad R_{a,0},
\qquad
R_{a,+}+R_{a,-}+R_{a,0}=Q_a,
\]
where \(Q_a\) is the projector onto \(\mathcal H_a\).

Assume these three subspaces are invariant under the corrected remote block:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[R_{a,+},H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
[R_{a,-},H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
[R_{a,0},H_R(0)]=0
\quad
\forall a.
}
\label{eq:constructive_HR_invariant}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
H_R(0)
=
\bigoplus_a
\Bigl(
H_a^{(+)}\oplus H_a^{(-)}\oplus H_a^{(0)}
\Bigr).
\label{eq:constructive_HR_blockdiag}
\end{equation}

\section{Charge-preserving zero-momentum coupling}

Assume the corrected zero-momentum low--remote coupling obeys the sectorwise charge selection rule
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W(0)
=
\sum_a
\Bigl(
P_+\,W(0)\,R_{a,+}
+
P_-\,W(0)\,R_{a,-}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:constructive_W_charge}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_+W(0)R_{a,-}=0,
\qquad
P_-W(0)R_{a,+}=0,
\qquad
W(0)R_{a,0}=0
\quad
\forall a.
}
\label{eq:constructive_W_crosszero}
\end{equation}

This says that, at \(p=0\), the remote sector couples only through matching shell charges.

\section{Explicit construction of \texorpdfstring{$Q_R$}{QR}}

On each neutral leftover block \(\mathcal K_a\), choose any Hermitian involution \(S_a\) satisfying
\begin{equation}
S_a^2=R_{a,0},
\qquad
[S_a,H_a^{(0)}]=0.
\label{eq:constructive_Sa}
\end{equation}
Now define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_R
:=
\sum_a
\bigl(
R_{a,+}-R_{a,-}+S_a
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:constructive_QR}
\end{equation}

Then \(Q_R\) is Hermitian and, by \eqref{eq:constructive_HR_invariant} and \eqref{eq:constructive_Sa},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:constructive_QR_comm}
\end{equation}

\section{Intertwiner identity}

We now prove
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*W(0)=W(0)Q_R.
}
\label{eq:constructive_intertwiner_goal}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:constructive_W_charge},
\begin{align}
Q_*W(0)
&=
Q_*
\sum_a
\Bigl(
P_+W(0)R_{a,+}
+
P_-W(0)R_{a,-}
\Bigr)
\\
&=
\sum_a
\Bigl(
(+1)P_+W(0)R_{a,+}
+
(-1)P_-W(0)R_{a,-}
\Bigr)
\\
&=
\sum_a
\Bigl(
P_+W(0)R_{a,+}
-
P_-W(0)R_{a,-}
\Bigr).
\label{eq:constructive_left}
\end{align}

On the other hand, using \eqref{eq:constructive_QR},
\begin{align}
W(0)Q_R
&=
W(0)\sum_a\bigl(R_{a,+}-R_{a,-}+S_a\bigr)
\\
&=
\sum_a
\Bigl(
W(0)R_{a,+}
-
W(0)R_{a,-}
+
W(0)R_{a,0}S_a
\Bigr)
\\
&=
\sum_a
\Bigl(
P_+W(0)R_{a,+}
-
P_-W(0)R_{a,-}
\Bigr),
\label{eq:constructive_right}
\end{align}
because \(W(0)R_{a,0}=0\), \(W(0)R_{a,+}=P_+W(0)R_{a,+}\), and \(W(0)R_{a,-}=P_-W(0)R_{a,-}\).

Comparing \eqref{eq:constructive_left} and \eqref{eq:constructive_right}, we obtain
\[
Q_*W(0)=W(0)Q_R.
\]

\section{Resolvent covariance}

Since \([Q_R,H_R(0)]=0\), the inverse remote block commutes with \(Q_R\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}
=
\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_R.
}
\label{eq:constructive_resolvent}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact proof of \texorpdfstring{$[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0$}{[Q*,Sigma(0,0)]=0}}

Now compute:
\begin{align}
Q_*\Sigma(0,0)
&=
Q_*W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
W(0)Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\qquad\text{by \eqref{eq:constructive_intertwiner_goal}}
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_R W(0)^\dagger
\qquad\text{by \eqref{eq:constructive_resolvent}}
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger Q_*
\qquad\text{by adjoint of \eqref{eq:constructive_intertwiner_goal}}
\\
&=
\Sigma(0,0)Q_*.
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:constructive_sigma_comm}
\end{equation}

\section{Mass exclusion}

The actual mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
}
\label{eq:constructive_Mactual}
\end{equation}
But the exact \(Q_*\)-commutant has trivial intersection with it:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:constructive_intersection_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence \eqref{eq:constructive_sigma_comm} implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:constructive_sigma_nomass}
\end{equation}

So the remote self-energy cannot generate an actual constant Dirac mass.

\section{Route A inside the same proof}

There is also the stronger trivial subcase:
if the exact corrected realization still satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W(0)=0,
}
\label{eq:constructive_routeA}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:constructive_routeA_sigma}
\end{equation}
So the whole frontier collapses immediately.

\section{Final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Constructive closure of the last frontier in the working truncation]
Assume either:

\paragraph{Route A.}
The exact corrected low--remote mixing vanishes at zero momentum:
\[
W(0)=0;
\]

or

\paragraph{Route B.}
For each remote sector
\[
\mathcal H_a\in
\{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\},
\]
there exists a charge decomposition \eqref{eq:constructive_sector_split} such that
\[
[R_{a,\pm},H_R(0)]=[R_{a,0},H_R(0)]=0
\]
and
\[
W(0)=\sum_a \bigl(P_+W(0)R_{a,+}+P_-W(0)R_{a,-}\bigr).
\]

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:constructive_final_comm}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:constructive_final_gate4}
\end{equation}
So the remote source passes Gate 4.
\end{theorem}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Sectorwise Closure Theorem for the Final Gate-4 Frontier}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now prove the final microscopic frontier in a form adapted to the actual working truncation.

The remote sector is
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]

The key idea is this:

\begin{enumerate}
\item if a remote sector keeps exact zero mixing at \(p=0\), then that sector contributes nothing to \(\Sigma(0,0)\);
\item if a remote sector does mix at \(p=0\), then it is enough to show that its zero-momentum coupling preserves the shell charge of \(Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3\);
\item combining these two cases sectorwise is already sufficient to prove
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the last frontier becomes a finite sector-by-sector audit.

\section{Setup}

Let the corrected microscopic block at \(p=0\) be
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_L(0) & W(0)\\
W(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:sectfull_block}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]

The shell generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\qquad
Q_*^2=\mathbf 1.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_Qstar}
\end{equation}
Let
\begin{equation}
P_\pm=\frac12(\mathbf 1\pm Q_*).
\label{eq:sectfull_Ppm}
\end{equation}

The Schur self-energy is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0)=W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger.
\label{eq:sectfull_sigma}
\end{equation}

\section{Sector partition into trivial and nontrivial pieces}

Let \(Q_a\) denote the projector onto the sector \(\mathcal H_a\), where
\[
a\in\{\mathrm{vol},\mathrm{high},\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}\}.
\]

Split the index set into two disjoint parts:
\[
\mathcal I_0\cup \mathcal I_c
=
\{\mathrm{vol},\mathrm{high},\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}\},
\qquad
\mathcal I_0\cap \mathcal I_c=\varnothing.
\]

Interpretation:

\begin{itemize}
\item sectors in \(\mathcal I_0\) are the ones for which exact zero mixing at \(p=0\) survives;
\item sectors in \(\mathcal I_c\) are the ones that may still couple at \(p=0\) and therefore require an explicit charge audit.
\end{itemize}

\section{Hypothesis A: exact zero-mixing sectors}

Assume that for every \(a\in\mathcal I_0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W(0)Q_a=0.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_zero_sectors}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the strongest persistence form of the already-reduced zero-mixing criterion.
Whenever it holds, that whole remote sector contributes nothing to \(\Sigma(0,0)\).

Indeed, if
\[
Q_{\mathcal I_0}:=\sum_{a\in\mathcal I_0}Q_a,
\]
then
\[
W(0)Q_{\mathcal I_0}=0.
\]

\section{Hypothesis B: charge-preserving coupled sectors}

For every \(a\in\mathcal I_c\), assume an orthogonal decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_a
=
\mathcal H_a^{(+)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_a^{(-)}
\oplus
\mathcal K_a,
}
\label{eq:sectfull_charge_split}
\end{equation}
with projectors
\[
R_{a,+},\qquad R_{a,-},\qquad R_{a,0},
\qquad
R_{a,+}+R_{a,-}+R_{a,0}=Q_a.
\]

Assume the corrected remote Hamiltonian preserves these subspaces:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[R_{a,+},H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
[R_{a,-},H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
[R_{a,0},H_R(0)]=0
\qquad
(a\in\mathcal I_c).
}
\label{eq:sectfull_HR_preserve}
\end{equation}

Assume also that the zero-momentum coupling preserves shell charge:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W(0)Q_a
=
P_+W(0)R_{a,+}
+
P_-W(0)R_{a,-},
\qquad
W(0)R_{a,0}=0
\qquad
(a\in\mathcal I_c).
}
\label{eq:sectfull_charge_coupling}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
P_+W(0)R_{a,-}=0,
\qquad
P_-W(0)R_{a,+}=0,
\qquad
W(0)R_{a,0}=0.
\label{eq:sectfull_charge_crosszero}
\end{equation}

\section{Construction of the remote generator}

For \(a\in\mathcal I_0\), define simply
\begin{equation}
Q_{R,a}:=Q_a.
\label{eq:sectfull_QRa_zero}
\end{equation}
This is Hermitian and commutes with \(H_R(0)\) provided the sector decomposition itself is preserved.

For \(a\in\mathcal I_c\), choose any Hermitian involution \(S_a\) on \(\mathcal K_a\) such that
\begin{equation}
S_a^2=R_{a,0},
\qquad
[S_a,H_R|_{\mathcal K_a}]=0,
\label{eq:sectfull_Sa}
\end{equation}
and define
\begin{equation}
Q_{R,a}:=R_{a,+}-R_{a,-}+S_a.
\label{eq:sectfull_QRa_charge}
\end{equation}

Now define the full remote generator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_R
:=
\sum_{a\in\mathcal I_0}Q_{R,a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal I_c}Q_{R,a}.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_QR}
\end{equation}

By construction and \eqref{eq:sectfull_HR_preserve},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_QR_comm}
\end{equation}

\section{Intertwiner identity}

We now prove
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*W(0)=W(0)Q_R.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_intertwiner_goal}
\end{equation}

Decompose
\[
W(0)=W(0)Q_{\mathcal I_0}+W(0)Q_{\mathcal I_c}.
\]

For the \(\mathcal I_0\)-part, \eqref{eq:sectfull_zero_sectors} gives
\[
W(0)Q_{\mathcal I_0}=0,
\]
hence
\[
Q_*W(0)Q_{\mathcal I_0}=0=W(0)Q_RQ_{\mathcal I_0}.
\]

For the \(\mathcal I_c\)-part, using \eqref{eq:sectfull_charge_coupling},
\begin{align}
Q_*W(0)Q_{\mathcal I_c}
&=
\sum_{a\in\mathcal I_c}
Q_*
\Bigl(
P_+W(0)R_{a,+}+P_-W(0)R_{a,-}
\Bigr)
\\
&=
\sum_{a\in\mathcal I_c}
\Bigl(
(+1)P_+W(0)R_{a,+}
+(-1)P_-W(0)R_{a,-}
\Bigr)
\\
&=
\sum_{a\in\mathcal I_c}
\Bigl(
P_+W(0)R_{a,+}
-
P_-W(0)R_{a,-}
\Bigr).
\label{eq:sectfull_left}
\end{align}

On the other hand,
\begin{align}
W(0)Q_RQ_{\mathcal I_c}
&=
\sum_{a\in\mathcal I_c}
W(0)\bigl(R_{a,+}-R_{a,-}+S_a\bigr)
\\
&=
\sum_{a\in\mathcal I_c}
\Bigl(
W(0)R_{a,+}-W(0)R_{a,-}+W(0)R_{a,0}S_a
\Bigr)
\\
&=
\sum_{a\in\mathcal I_c}
\Bigl(
P_+W(0)R_{a,+}
-
P_-W(0)R_{a,-}
\Bigr),
\label{eq:sectfull_right}
\end{align}
because \(W(0)R_{a,0}=0\).

Comparing \eqref{eq:sectfull_left} and \eqref{eq:sectfull_right} proves
\[
Q_*W(0)=W(0)Q_R.
\]

\section{Remote-symmetry inheritance}

Since \([Q_R,H_R(0)]=0\), the resolvent commutes with \(Q_R\):
\begin{equation}
Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}
=
\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_R.
\label{eq:sectfull_resolvent}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{align}
Q_*\Sigma(0,0)
&=
Q_*W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
W(0)Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_R W(0)^\dagger
\\
&=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger Q_*
\\
&=
\Sigma(0,0)Q_*.
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_sigma_comm}
\end{equation}

\section{Mass exclusion}

The actual mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_massspace}
\end{equation}
But the exact \(Q_*\)-commutant satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_intersection}
\end{equation}
Hence \eqref{eq:sectfull_sigma_comm} implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_nomass}
\end{equation}

So the remote self-energy cannot generate a constant actual Dirac mass.

\section{Final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Working-truncation closure of the last Gate-4 frontier]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-level corrected block preserves the same actual generator
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3;
\]

\item for each remote sector \(a\), either exact zero mixing persists,
\[
W(0)Q_a=0,
\]
or there exists a charge decomposition \eqref{eq:sectfull_charge_split} satisfying
\eqref{eq:sectfull_HR_preserve} and \eqref{eq:sectfull_charge_coupling}.
\end{enumerate}

Then one can explicitly construct a Hermitian remote generator \(Q_R\) such that
\[
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
Q_*W(0)=W(0)Q_R.
\]
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:sectfull_final}
\end{equation}
So Gate 4 passes.
\end{theorem}

\section{Minimal-Truncation Completion of the Final Gate-4 Frontier}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now prove that, in the actual working minimal truncation, the final Gate-4 frontier collapses already by exact zero mixing at \(p=0\).

So in the minimal truncation, one does not even need a nontrivial remote charge operator \(Q_R\):
the remote self-energy vanishes identically at zero momentum,
\[
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
\]

This is enough to close the remote part of Gate 4 in the current working branch.

\section{Working truncation}

The truncated Hilbert space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
}
\label{eq:G4min_Hfull}
\end{equation}

At \(p=0\), write the corrected truncated microscopic block as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & W(0)\\
W(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:G4min_block}
\end{equation}
where \(W(0)\) is the constant Dirac--remote mixing block.

The corresponding Schur self-energy is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0)
=
W(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}W(0)^\dagger,
\label{eq:G4min_sigma}
\end{equation}
whenever the remote resolvent exists.

\section{Sectorwise shell-relevant mismatch}

The exact shell-relevant exclusion criterion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
}
\label{eq:G4min_Hom}
\end{equation}
Hence if every remote sector differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label, then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
\]

The shell-relevant labels are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse vs volumetric},
\quad
\text{enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra labels}.
}
\label{eq:G4min_labels}
\end{equation}

In the current minimal truncation, the four remote sectors satisfy:

\begin{align}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
&:\quad
\text{volumetric mismatch},
\label{eq:G4min_vol}
\\
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
&:\quad
\text{different shell orbit mismatch},
\label{eq:G4min_high}
\\
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
&:\quad
\text{absence of enriched internal doublet},
\label{eq:G4min_non}
\\
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
&:\quad
\text{wrong internal representation}.
\label{eq:G4min_wrong}
\end{align}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\quad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\quad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\quad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:G4min_allhomzero}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
W(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:G4min_Wzero}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate collapse of the remote frontier}

Substituting \eqref{eq:G4min_Wzero} into \eqref{eq:G4min_sigma}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
}
\label{eq:G4min_sigma_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore for any shell generator \(Q_*\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4min_sigma_comm}
\end{equation}

So in the minimal truncation, the remote part of the Gate-4 frontier is already closed by exact zero mixing.

\section{Mass exclusion in the actual canonical basis}

In the actual canonical shell basis, the residual generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
}
\label{eq:G4min_Qstar}
\end{equation}
and the actual mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
}
\label{eq:G4min_Mactual}
\end{equation}

Since \(\Sigma(0,0)=0\), it trivially has zero projection onto the actual mass space:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4min_sigma_nomass}
\end{equation}

Hence the remote self-energy cannot generate any constant actual Dirac mass in the minimal truncation.

\section{Final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Minimal-truncation completion of Gate 4]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the corrected local shell block preserves the shell-level residual symmetry;
\item the truncated Hamiltonian is shell-relevant symmetry-equivariant at \(p=0\);
\item the remote sector is the minimal truncation
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}};
\]
\item each remote sector differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label.
\end{enumerate}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W(0)=0,
\qquad
\Sigma(0,0)=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4min_main}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{tr})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4min_gate4}
\end{equation}
So Gate 4 passes in the actual working minimal truncation.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By shell-relevant equivariance,
\[
W(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Since the remote sector is a direct sum of the four displayed sectors,
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\bigoplus_{a\in\{\mathrm{vol},\mathrm{high},\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}\}}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_a,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Each summand vanishes because the corresponding remote sector differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label.
Hence the full Hom-space vanishes, and therefore \(W(0)=0\).

Substituting into the Schur formula gives \(\Sigma(0,0)=0\).
Thus \([Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0\) is immediate, and \(\Sigma(0,0)\) has no component in the actual mass space.
So the remote source cannot generate a constant Dirac mass.
\end{proof}

\section{Honest status}

The theorem above closes Gate 4 completely in the current minimal truncation.

What remains open is only the stronger statement for the \emph{full corrected microscopic realization beyond the minimal truncation}:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{does exact zero mixing }W(0)=0\text{ persist, or at least does }[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0\text{ survive after the full correction is reinstated?}
}
\label{eq:G4min_honest_open}
\end{equation}

So the honest distinction is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 4 is finished in the minimal working truncation,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the full corrected beyond-truncation persistence statement is still the last microscopic inheritance audit.}
}
\]

\section{Why the Actual Longitudinal Seed Audit Is the Correct Next Step}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At the current stage, the transverse carrier channel is already structurally realized, while the only remaining honest carrier-side open slot is the survival of the primitive longitudinal seed.

Therefore the logically correct next executable step is the actual basis-overlap audit
\[
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\ell_{\parallel A}=\hat n_i\hat n_j E_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
\]

We now prove that this is not merely a convenient step, but the exact minimal execution needed to close the carrier-side longitudinal audit.

\section{Carrier audit structure}

Let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\subset
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}
\otimes
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}
\otimes
U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the actual microscopic transport space, and choose a basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d.
\]

The shell-adapted primitive longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_\parallel:\quad
N^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=N^2_{ij}=0.
}
\label{eq:next_long_Bpar}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, its covector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta_{a3}.
}
\label{eq:next_long_Tpar}
\end{equation}

Define the basis overlaps
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{\parallel A}
:=
\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j E_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
}
\label{eq:next_long_ell}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact basis-level criterion}

Decompose each basis element in the minimal shell seed space
\[
V_{\min}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}
\]
as
\begin{equation}
E_A
=
a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J+R_A,
\qquad
R_A\perp V_{\min}.
\label{eq:next_long_EA}
\end{equation}

Because the longitudinal witness functional vanishes on the orthogonal remainder, one has
\begin{equation}
\ell_{\parallel A}=\mu_\parallel a_A,
\qquad
\mu_\parallel\neq 0.
\label{eq:next_long_mu}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:next_long_basis_equiv}
\end{equation}

So the actual longitudinal carrier problem is exactly a finite basis-overlap audit.

\section{From basis audit to longitudinal survival}

Inside the explicit seed realization, the longitudinal witness is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:next_long_lambda}
\end{equation}
The odd longitudinal overlap integral is already nonzero in the working branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:next_long_I3}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:next_long_c_to_lambda}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, by \eqref{eq:next_long_basis_equiv},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:next_long_ell_to_lambda}
\end{equation}
provided the remaining normalization factor is not killed.

\section{Why this is logically prior to Gate 4}

The transverse carrier channel is already structurally realized:
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
is no longer the honest open carrier-side issue.

By contrast, the longitudinal primitive seed survival is still explicitly marked as open.
Therefore the actual microscopic carrier audit is currently
\[
\boxed{
\text{transverse fixed}+\text{one remaining longitudinal primitive test}.
}
\]

So the next nonredundant execution is not another remote-sector theorem, but exactly the test
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{Theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Correct next executable step]
At the present project stage, the logically correct next executable step is the actual longitudinal seed audit
\[
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\ell_{\parallel A}=\hat n_i\hat n_j E_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
\]

If this audit succeeds, then the carrier-side longitudinal slot closes:
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
Combined with the already solved transverse channel, this finishes the carrier-level nondegeneracy audit.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the basis decomposition \eqref{eq:next_long_EA}, the overlap \(\ell_{\parallel A}\) is nonzero if and only if at least one basis vector carries a nonzero \(B_\parallel\) component. This is exactly equivalent to \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0\).

Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\) is already fixed in the working branch, \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0\) implies \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\).

The transverse half is already structurally realized, so the only remaining carrier-side honest open slot is precisely the longitudinal one. Therefore this audit is the correct next executable step.
\end{proof}

\section{Final Summary}

Yes: the actual longitudinal seed audit is the correct next step.

The carrier-side longitudinal slot is exactly reduced to the finite basis-overlap test
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\ell_{\parallel A}=\hat n_i\hat n_j E_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
}
\]

For a shell-adapted basis decomposition
\[
E_A=a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J+R_A,
\qquad
R_A\perp V_{\min},
\]
one has
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\mu_\parallel a_A,
\qquad
\mu_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\Longleftrightarrow
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
}
\]

Since
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
it follows that
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore this audit closes the last honest open slot on the carrier side.
With the transverse channel already structurally realized, it is indeed the correct next executable step.

\section{Basis-Free Closure of the Actual Longitudinal Seed Audit}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The actual longitudinal audit is not merely a search over basis vectors.
It is exactly the test of whether the complete microscopic first-order transport block has a nonzero projection onto the primitive odd-singlet shell seed.

So the correct next proof is:

\[
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\Pi_\parallel\!\bigl(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\bigr)\neq 0,
\]
and this is equivalent to the shell-seed coefficient
\[
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
\]

Therefore the longitudinal carrier slot is completely reduced to one basis-free projector computation on the full microscopic Hessian.

\section{Ambient transport space and longitudinal functional}

Let
\[
W
=
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}
\otimes
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}
\otimes
U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient enriched tensor space, and let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W
\]
be the actual microscopic transport space extracted from the full refined locked TECT linearization.

Fix the shell direction
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]
The primitive longitudinal shell covector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta_{a3}.
}
\label{eq:longproj_Tpar}
\end{equation}

Define the longitudinal linear functional
\[
L_\parallel:W\to\mathbb R,
\qquad
L_\parallel(E):=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E\rangle.
\]
In components,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_\parallel(E)=\hat n_i\hat n_j\,E_{ij}^{\,3}.
}
\label{eq:longproj_Lpar}
\end{equation}

For any basis \(\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d\) of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), the explicit overlap coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{\parallel A}=L_\parallel(E_A)=\hat n_i\hat n_j\,E_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
}
\label{eq:longproj_ellA}
\end{equation}

\section{Basis-free projector onto the primitive longitudinal seed}

Let the primitive longitudinal seed tensor be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_\parallel:\qquad
(B_\parallel)^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
(B_\parallel)^1_{ij}=(B_\parallel)^2_{ij}=0.
}
\label{eq:longproj_Bpar}
\end{equation}

Define the rank-one projector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_\parallel(E)
:=
\frac{L_\parallel(E)}{\|B_\parallel\|^2}\,B_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:longproj_Pipar}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\Pi_\parallel(E)=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
L_\parallel(E)=0.
\label{eq:longproj_proj_equiv_point}
\end{equation}

\section{First equivalence theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Basis audit \(\Leftrightarrow\) projector test]
The following are equivalent:

\begin{enumerate}
\item there exists a basis element \(E_A\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) such that
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0;
\]

\item the longitudinal functional does not vanish identically on the microscopic transport space:
\[
L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\neq 0;
\]

\item the primitive longitudinal projector does not annihilate the transport space:
\[
\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq \{0\}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\((1)\Rightarrow(2)\): if \(\ell_{\parallel A}=L_\parallel(E_A)\neq 0\) for some basis element, then \(L_\parallel\) is not the zero functional on \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).

\((2)\Rightarrow(1)\): if \(L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\neq 0\), then for any basis \(\{E_A\}\) of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), the values \(L_\parallel(E_A)\) cannot all vanish, otherwise \(L_\parallel\) would vanish on all of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).

\((2)\Leftrightarrow(3)\): by \eqref{eq:longproj_proj_equiv_point}, \(\Pi_\parallel(E)=0\) if and only if \(L_\parallel(E)=0\). Hence \(\Pi_\parallel\) is nonzero on \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) exactly when \(L_\parallel\) is nonzero on \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
\end{proof}

\section{Equivalence with the shell-seed coefficient}

Let
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}
\]
be the explicit seed space.
Project the actual induced shell tensor onto \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_{\mathrm{seed}}N_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}B_\parallel
+
c_I^{(\mathrm{mic})}B_I
+
c_J^{(\mathrm{mic})}B_J.
}
\label{eq:longproj_seedproj}
\end{equation}

Because \(L_\parallel\) annihilates the transverse seed directions and all remainders orthogonal to \(B_\parallel\), one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_\parallel\!\bigl(P_{\mathrm{seed}}N_{\mathrm{mic}}\bigr)
=
\mu_\parallel\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})},
\qquad
\mu_\parallel:=L_\parallel(B_\parallel)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:longproj_mu}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{theorem}[Projector test \(\Leftrightarrow\) longitudinal seed coefficient]
The following are equivalent:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq \{0\}\);
\item \(L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\neq 0\);
\item \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the first theorem, \(\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq 0\) is equivalent to \(L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\neq 0\).

On the other hand, the induced seed projection is exactly the \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\)-part of the microscopic transport sector. Since \(L_\parallel\) only detects the \(B_\parallel\)-component and \(\mu_\parallel\neq 0\), equation \eqref{eq:longproj_mu} shows that \(L_\parallel\) is nonzero on the seed projection if and only if \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0\).

Thus all three statements are equivalent.
\end{proof}

\section{Consequence for the actual longitudinal carrier}

Inside the explicit seed realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:longproj_lambda}
\end{equation}
The odd longitudinal overlap is already fixed in the working branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:longproj_I3}
\end{equation}
Hence:

\begin{theorem}[Actual longitudinal survival criterion]
If
\[
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\]
equivalently
\[
\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq 0,
\]
equivalently
\[
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:longproj_final_lambda}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the previous theorem, \(\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0\) implies \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0\).
Then \eqref{eq:longproj_lambda} and \eqref{eq:longproj_I3} give \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\).
\end{proof}

\section{Reduction to the complete microscopic Hessian}

Let the complete microscopic linearization be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\mathbb H_B
-
i\,\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
O(\partial_y^2),
}
\label{eq:longproj_Hcomp}
\end{equation}
and let the shell-relevant first-order transport kernel be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_1=-i\,V^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi):=\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\big|_{Q_B\text{-tangent sector}}.
}
\label{eq:longproj_L1}
\end{equation}

Then the entire longitudinal audit is reduced to extracting from \(V^\mu\) the induced microscopic transport subspace \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), and applying the rank-one test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq \{0\}.
}
\label{eq:longproj_rankone_test}
\end{equation}

This is a finite linear-algebra problem once the shell-relevant tangent transport basis is extracted.

\section{What is actually proved}

We have proved:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual longitudinal basis audit is basis-independent;
\item it is exactly the nonvanishing of one rank-one projector onto the primitive odd-singlet seed;
\item it is exactly equivalent to the seed coefficient \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0\);
\item therefore it is exactly the correct remaining carrier-side execution problem.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The actual longitudinal seed audit is now completely reduced in a basis-free way.

Define the longitudinal shell functional
\[
L_\parallel(E)=\hat n_i\hat n_j E_{ij}^{\,3},
\]
and the rank-one projector
\[
\Pi_\parallel(E)=\frac{L_\parallel(E)}{\|B_\parallel\|^2}B_\parallel.
\]

Then for the actual microscopic transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\),
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\Longleftrightarrow
L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\neq 0
\Longleftrightarrow
\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq \{0\}.
}
\]

This is also equivalent to the seed coefficient condition
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
}
\]

Since
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
it follows that
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is exactly one finite projector computation on the transport space extracted from the complete microscopic Hessian.

\section{Odd-Singlet Sufficiency Theorem for the Actual Longitudinal Seed Audit}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The actual longitudinal audit can be reduced one step further.

It is not necessary to know the full microscopic basis \(\{E_A\}\) explicitly in advance.
It is enough to extract the shell-relevant invariant part of the first-order transport kernel and check whether it contains a nonzero primitive odd longitudinal singlet component.

This is the mathematically sharp reason why the next real calculation is to isolate the \(B_\parallel\)-coefficient of the actual microscopic transport tensor.

\section{Shell-relevant seed space}

Let
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}
\]
be the explicit shell-adapted seed space, where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(B_\parallel)^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
(B_\parallel)^1_{ij}=(B_\parallel)^2_{ij}=0,
}
\label{eq:oddsing_Bpar}
\end{equation}
and \(B_I,B_J\) are the transverse even/odd doublet seeds.

The microscopic transport problem is reduced to whether the actual transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) has nontrivial projection to \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\). In particular, the longitudinal carrier question is exactly whether the \(B_\parallel\)-component is nonzero. 

\section{Primitive odd-singlet decomposition}

Let the shell-relevant invariant part of the actual microscopic transport tensor be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N_{\mathrm{mic}}^{\mathrm{inv}}
=
u_\parallel\,B_\parallel
+
u_I\,B_I
+
u_J\,B_J
+
R,
\qquad
R\perp V_{\mathrm{seed}}.
}
\label{eq:oddsing_decomp}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, at the level of the first-order microscopic kernel, write the shell-relevant piece in the invariant transport basis as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{mic}}(\xi)
=
u_\parallel(\xi)\,n^\mu \Sigma_3
+
u_I(\xi)\,E^\mu_a\Sigma_a
+
u_J(\xi)\,J^\mu_a\Sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{rest}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:oddsing_Vdecomp}
\end{equation}
where \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{rest}}\) has zero projection onto the explicit seed space.

The primitive longitudinal channel is exactly the first term.
The corresponding explicit minimal seed is the odd singlet
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
which is already identified in the current notes as the only honest remaining longitudinal carrier mechanism. 

\section{Longitudinal projector kills all non-longitudinal classes}

Define the longitudinal covector
\begin{equation}
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}=\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta_{a3},
\label{eq:oddsing_Tpar}
\end{equation}
and the corresponding linear functional
\begin{equation}
L_\parallel(E)=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E\rangle=\hat n_i\hat n_j E_{ij}^{\,3}.
\label{eq:oddsing_Lpar}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
L_\parallel(B_\parallel)=\mu_\parallel\neq 0,
\label{eq:oddsing_mu}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
L_\parallel(B_I)=0,
\qquad
L_\parallel(B_J)=0,
\qquad
L_\parallel(R)=0
\quad\text{for all }R\perp V_{\mathrm{seed}}.
\label{eq:oddsing_kills_rest}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_\parallel(N_{\mathrm{mic}}^{\mathrm{inv}})
=
\mu_\parallel\,u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:oddsing_extract}
\end{equation}

So the longitudinal shell witness sees only the primitive odd-singlet coefficient.

\section{Sufficiency theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Odd-singlet sufficiency for longitudinal survival]
If the actual microscopic first-order transport tensor contains a nonzero primitive odd-singlet component,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:oddsing_upar_nonzero}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq \{0\},
\qquad
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:oddsing_proj_nonzero}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\,I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:oddsing_lambda_nonzero}
\end{equation}
provided the already-fixed overlap factor \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:oddsing_extract}, if \(u_\parallel\neq 0\) then
\[
L_\parallel(N_{\mathrm{mic}}^{\mathrm{inv}})\neq 0.
\]
Therefore the longitudinal functional does not vanish on \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
By the previously established basis-free equivalence, this implies
\[
\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq \{0\}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
\]
Finally, the reduced witness formula
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\,I_{\theta'^3}
\]
and the already-fixed nonvanishing
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0
\]
imply \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\).
\end{proof}

\section{Parity refinement}

A naive even singlet in the \(\sigma_3\) channel is excluded by parity, whereas the primitive odd longitudinal singlet is the minimal surviving longitudinal mechanism.
Therefore the longitudinal audit is not contaminated by an even-singlet ambiguity:
the first admissible longitudinal contribution is already the odd primitive channel. 

Thus, if one isolates a nonzero shell-relevant \(\sigma_3\)-singlet contribution in the actual microscopic transport kernel, it is precisely the desired primitive longitudinal seed.

\section{Executable consequence}

Therefore the next actual calculation does not need the full final diagonalization of every carrier tensor first.

It is enough to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item linearize the complete microscopic theory and extract the shell-relevant first-order kernel \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{mic}}(\xi)\);
\item project it to the invariant seed sector;
\item read off the coefficient \(u_\parallel\) of the primitive odd-singlet tensor \(n^\mu\Sigma_3\);
\item verify \(u_\parallel\neq 0\).
\end{enumerate}

Once this is done, the longitudinal carrier slot is closed.

\section{What is actually proved}

What is proved here is stronger than the raw basis-overlap restatement:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual longitudinal audit is equivalent to the nonvanishing of the primitive odd-singlet coefficient;
\item the transverse sector is irrelevant for this test because the longitudinal projector annihilates it exactly;
\item parity removes the naive even-singlet contamination;
\item therefore the whole carrier-side longitudinal frontier reduces to extracting one coefficient \(u_\parallel\) from the shell-relevant microscopic transport kernel.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The actual longitudinal seed audit can be sharpened further.

Write the shell-relevant invariant microscopic transport tensor as
\[
N_{\mathrm{mic}}^{\mathrm{inv}}
=
u_\parallel B_\parallel+u_I B_I+u_J B_J+R,
\qquad
R\perp V_{\mathrm{seed}}.
\]

Then the longitudinal projector sees only the primitive odd-singlet coefficient:
\[
L_\parallel(N_{\mathrm{mic}}^{\mathrm{inv}})
=
\mu_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
\mu_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
}
\]

Since
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})} I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
it follows that
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel\neq 0\Longrightarrow \lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

So the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is no longer a broad basis search.
It is exactly the extraction of one coefficient \(u_\parallel\) of the primitive odd longitudinal singlet \(n^\mu\Sigma_3\) from the shell-relevant first-order microscopic transport kernel.

\section{Source-by-Source Extraction of the Primitive Odd Longitudinal Singlet}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The next real calculation is not to search blindly through all basis tensors.
It is to isolate, inside the full first-order microscopic transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\]
the unique shell-relevant tensor structure that can survive the longitudinal projector.

We prove that:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the naive even singlet \( \theta'(\xi)^2 n^\mu \Sigma_3 \) is killed by parity;
\item the transverse doublet pieces are killed by the longitudinal projector;
\item the shell-null remainder is projected out;
\item therefore the only surviving longitudinal shell-relevant structure is the primitive odd singlet
\[
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Hence the actual longitudinal audit reduces to testing whether the Class II microscopic extraction generates a nonzero coefficient in front of that one structure.

\section{Shell-adapted tensor decomposition}

Fix the adapted orthonormal frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\]
Let \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3\) act on the reduced tangent-doublet space.

For the shell-relevant \(Q=G_*\) harmonic coefficients, the most general compatible decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i
\Big[
\mathcal K_\parallel^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
\mathcal K_E^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\mathcal K_O^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
+
\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
}
\label{eq:source_extract_Kgeneral}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i
\Big[
\mathcal J_\parallel^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
\mathcal J_E^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\mathcal J_O^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
+
\mathsf J^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
}
\label{eq:source_extract_Jgeneral}
\end{equation}

By construction, the null pieces are annihilated by the shell witness projectors.
So the shell-relevant transport extraction sees only the three canonical channels
\[
\Sigma_3,\qquad \Sigma_1,\qquad \Sigma_2.
\]

\section{Canonical Class II response decomposition}

Write the actual adapted-frame response as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
s_1(\xi)\sigma_1
+
s_2(\xi)\sigma_2
+
s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:source_extract_response}
\end{equation}

The canonical reconstruction ansatz has the form
\begin{align}
V^\mu(\xi)
&=
\theta'(\xi)\,v_\parallel^{(0)}(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\theta'(\xi)\,v_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\theta'(\xi)\,v_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}(\xi),
\label{eq:source_extract_Vrecon}
\end{align}
with
\[
v_\parallel^{(0)}(\xi)\sim s_3(\xi),
\qquad
v_E(\xi)\sim s_1(\xi),
\qquad
v_O(\xi)\sim s_2(\xi),
\]
up to model-dependent proportionality factors determined by the full Hessian.

Thus:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)\ \text{feeds the longitudinal singlet channel},
}
\label{eq:source_extract_s3}
\end{equation}
whereas
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_1(\xi)\ \text{feeds the even transverse doublet},
\qquad
s_2(\xi)\ \text{feeds the odd transverse doublet}.
}
\label{eq:source_extract_s12}
\end{equation}

\section{Longitudinal projector annihilates all non-singlet classes}

Define the longitudinal shell covector
\begin{equation}
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta_{a3},
\label{eq:source_extract_Tpar}
\end{equation}
and the corresponding functional
\begin{equation}
L_\parallel(E)=\hat n_i\hat n_j E_{ij}^{\,3}.
\label{eq:source_extract_Lpar}
\end{equation}

Then the following hold.

\paragraph{(i) Transverse doublets are killed.}
Because \(B_I\) and \(B_J\) are transverse doublet seeds,
\begin{equation}
L_\parallel(B_I)=0,
\qquad
L_\parallel(B_J)=0.
\label{eq:source_extract_transverse_killed}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the \(E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\) and \(J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\) channels do not contribute to the longitudinal witness.

\paragraph{(ii) Irreducible/null pieces are killed.}
By shell construction,
\begin{equation}
L_\parallel(V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}})=0.
\label{eq:source_extract_null_killed}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(iii) Naive even singlet is killed by parity.}
The candidate even singlet source
\[
\theta'(\xi)^2\,n^\mu\sigma_3
\]
would contribute through the overlap
\[
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
But
\[
f_+ \text{ is even},\qquad
f_- \text{ is odd},\qquad
\theta'(\xi)^2 \text{ is even},
\]
so the integrand is odd and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0.
}
\label{eq:source_extract_even_killed}
\end{equation}

Hence the naive even \(\sigma_3\)-singlet is excluded.

\section{Unique surviving longitudinal shell-relevant structure}

By the previous section, the only shell-relevant contribution that can survive in the longitudinal channel is the primitive odd singlet:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:source_extract_good_long}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the seed basis this is precisely the \(B_\parallel\)-direction.
Therefore the longitudinal witness reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:source_extract_lambda}
\end{equation}

So the actual longitudinal audit is exactly the question
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0\ ?
}
\label{eq:source_extract_lambdac_question}
\end{equation}

\section{Class II sufficiency theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Class II odd-singlet sufficiency]
Assume the full refined locked microscopic linearization is of Class II type in the shell-relevant sector, and assume its extracted first-order transport kernel contains a nonzero shell-relevant \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet coefficient in the canonical decomposition \eqref{eq:source_extract_Vrecon}, i.e.
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(0)}\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:source_extract_suff_cond}
\end{equation}
Then the primitive longitudinal projector is nonzero:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:source_extract_proj_nonzero}
\end{equation}
If moreover the branch realized by the extraction is the already solved Branch B local class, i.e.
\[
v_\parallel^{(0)}\equiv 0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:source_extract_branchB}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:source_extract_transverse_killed} and \eqref{eq:source_extract_null_killed}, the longitudinal projector annihilates every transverse and shell-null contribution.
By \eqref{eq:source_extract_even_killed}, it also annihilates the naive even singlet.
Therefore the only surviving shell-relevant longitudinal structure is the primitive odd singlet \eqref{eq:source_extract_good_long}.

If either \(v_\parallel^{(0)}\not\equiv 0\) or \(\lambda_c\neq 0\), then the \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet channel is nonzero, so the primitive longitudinal projector is nonzero and \(\Pi_\parallel(V_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq 0\).

In the solved Branch B class one has \(v_\parallel^{(0)}=0\) and \(\lambda_c\neq 0\), so \eqref{eq:source_extract_lambda} gives \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\) immediately because \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\).
\end{proof}

\section{What is now the actual next calculation}

The theorem shows that the remaining carrier-side longitudinal problem is no longer to classify source types.
That part is finished.

The actual remaining computation is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item extract the shell-relevant first-order kernel \(V^\mu(\xi)\) from the complete refined locked Class II linearization;
\item decompose it into the canonical classes
\[
n^\mu\sigma_3,\qquad
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\qquad
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\qquad
V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}};
\]
\item read off the coefficient of the \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet sector;
\item determine whether the extraction realizes Branch A \((v_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0)\) or Branch B \((v_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\ \lambda_c\neq 0)\).
\end{enumerate}

In particular, for the currently solved local class, the decisive test is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{What is actually proved}

We have proved:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal projector kills the transverse doublet sectors exactly;
\item the shell-null remainder is projected out exactly;
\item the naive even \(\sigma_3\)-singlet is excluded by parity;
\item therefore the unique minimal surviving longitudinal structure is the primitive odd singlet;
\item in Class II, once that singlet coefficient is nonzero, the carrier longitudinal slot closes.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

Inside the shell-relevant Class II transport decomposition, the longitudinal projector kills:

\[
\text{(i) transverse doublets }E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\ J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
\[
\text{(ii) shell-null irreducible pieces }V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}},
\]
and
\[
\text{(iii) the naive even singlet }\theta'(\xi)^2 n^\mu\sigma_3
\text{ by parity.}
\]

Therefore the unique minimal surviving longitudinal shell-relevant structure is the primitive odd singlet
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\]

Hence the remaining carrier-side longitudinal problem is exactly the coefficient extraction problem
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0\ ?
}
\]

If this holds, then
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

So the last honest carrier-side frontier is no longer the broad source classification problem.
It is exactly the extraction of the primitive odd-singlet coefficient from the full Class II microscopic linearization.

\section{Source-by-Source Microscopic Identification of the Longitudinal Coefficient \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_c$}{lambda_c}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now prove that, inside the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the microscopic source of the longitudinal primitive odd singlet is isolated to the axial \(JJ\)-type sector.

More precisely:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the pure \(K\)-sector has no leading longitudinal shell component;
\item the mixed \(JK\) contraction generates transverse Pauli directions only;
\item the \(KK\)-sector belongs to the same transverse family;
\item therefore the only principal candidate for the longitudinal primitive coefficient \(\lambda_c\) is the axial \(JJ\)-type singlet sector.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the actual carrier-side longitudinal frontier reduces to a single coefficient extraction problem on the \(JJ\)-side.

\section{Class II Schur structure}

In the working branch, integrating out the mediator produces the shell self-energy
\begin{equation}
\Sigma
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
(\alpha_X J+\beta_X K)(\alpha_X J+\beta_X K)^\dagger.
\label{eq:lamc_sigma_full}
\end{equation}
Decompose this as
\begin{equation}
\Sigma
=
\Sigma_{JJ}
+
\Sigma_{JK}
+
\Sigma_{KK},
\label{eq:lamc_sigma_split}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{align}
\Sigma_{JJ}
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}JJ^\dagger,
\label{eq:lamc_sigJJ}
\\
\Sigma_{JK}
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(JK^\dagger+KJ^\dagger),
\label{eq:lamc_sigJK}
\\
\Sigma_{KK}
&=
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}KK^\dagger.
\label{eq:lamc_sigKK}
\end{align}

\section{Shell-adapted principal forms}

At the intervalley harmonic \(Q=G_*\), the shell-adapted principal forms are:

\paragraph{Axial \(J\)-sector.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{i,r}^a
=
\hat n_i\,j^a\,(\Sigma_3)_r.
}
\label{eq:lamc_Jform}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Transverse \(K\)-sector.}
In the minimal explicit branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal K_\parallel^a(G_*;0)=0,
}
\label{eq:lamc_Kpar_zero}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{i,r}^a
=
\hat n_i\,k^a
\bigl(
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O^{(0)}\Sigma_2
\bigr)_r
+
K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^a.
}
\label{eq:lamc_Kform}
\end{equation}

Thus \(J\) is axial-singlet while \(K\) is transverse-doublet at principal shell order.

\section{Pure \texorpdfstring{$K$}{K} cannot generate the longitudinal singlet}

By \eqref{eq:lamc_Kpar_zero}, the principal shell projection of the \(K\)-sector contains no \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet coefficient.
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0.
}
\label{eq:lamc_cparK_zero}
\end{equation}
So the pure \(K\)-sector cannot close the longitudinal carrier slot.

\section{Pure \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} is axial only}

The shell-reduced \(JJ\)-piece has universal shell-normal form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
}
\label{eq:lamc_JJaxial}
\end{equation}
where \(M\) is a Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix on the tangent doublet space.
Write
\begin{equation}
M=m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3.
\label{eq:lamc_Mpauli}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
p_iK_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\Gamma_J p_\parallel
(m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3).
\]

At the shell-relevant principal level, the \(JJ\)-sector carries only the shell-normal direction \(p_\parallel\), and hence only probes a longitudinal-type singlet channel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\propto m_3,
\qquad
\alpha^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0,
\qquad
\beta^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0.
}
\label{eq:lamc_JJ_only_long}
\end{equation}

Therefore the pure \(JJ\)-sector is the unique principal Class-II source that can feed the longitudinal \(\sigma_3\)-singlet.

\section{Mixed \texorpdfstring{$JK$}{JK} generates transverse only}

Now examine the mixed term.
Using \eqref{eq:lamc_Jform} and \eqref{eq:lamc_Kform},
\[
J\sim j\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
K\sim k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2.
\]
Hence
\[
JK^\dagger+KJ^\dagger
\sim
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)
+
(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3.
\]

The naive local real Hermitian bilinear vanishes because
\[
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}=0,
\qquad
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\]
So the constant \(p=0\) bilinear has no longitudinal singlet content.

At the derivative-resolved shell level, the mixed contraction generates transverse Pauli directions through
\[
\Sigma_3\Sigma_1=i\Sigma_2,
\qquad
\Sigma_3\Sigma_2=-i\Sigma_1.
\]
Therefore the mixed \(JK\)-sector feeds the transverse coefficients \(c_E,c_O\), not the longitudinal one:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JK
\Longrightarrow
(c_E,c_O)\ \text{only},
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(JK)}=0
\ \text{at principal shell order}.
}
\label{eq:lamc_JK_trans_only}
\end{equation}

\section{The \texorpdfstring{$KK$}{KK} sector is also transverse-family}

Since the \(K\)-sector itself has no leading \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet piece, \(KK\) remains inside the transverse-family channel at the shell-relevant leading order.
In particular, it does not provide the primitive odd longitudinal singlet source.
So one has the principal classification
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(KK)}=0
\ \text{at the primitive shell-relevant longitudinal level.}
}
\label{eq:lamc_KK_no_long}
\end{equation}

\section{Microscopic localization of the longitudinal frontier}

Collecting the previous results:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(JK)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(KK)}=0
\quad
\text{at principal longitudinal shell order},
}
\label{eq:lamc_all_nonJJ_zero}
\end{equation}
whereas
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(JJ)}
\ \text{is allowed and is the unique principal Class-II longitudinal source.}
}
\label{eq:lamc_JJ_unique}
\end{equation}

Hence the primitive odd longitudinal singlet coefficient \(\lambda_c\) is localized to the axial \(JJ\)-type sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
\sim
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:lamc_localized}
\end{equation}

\section{Dictionary form in the current explicit branch}

In the current explicit branch, the reduced microscopic dictionary takes the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\label{eq:lamc_dictionary_long}
\end{equation}
while the transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j\!\cdot\! k)\Lambda_O^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j\!\cdot\! k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:lamc_dictionary_trans}
\end{equation}

So the longitudinal/transverse split is completely sharp:
\[
JJ \leadsto \lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
JK/KK \leadsto (\alpha,\beta).
\]

\section{Main theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Source classification for the longitudinal primitive channel]
In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the shell-relevant primitive odd longitudinal singlet \(n^\mu\Sigma_3\) can be generated only by the axial \(JJ\)-type sector at principal order.

More precisely:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the pure \(K\)-sector has no leading longitudinal component;
\item the mixed \(JK\)-sector generates transverse Pauli directions only;
\item the \(KK\)-sector remains in the transverse family at principal longitudinal shell order;
\item therefore the microscopic longitudinal coefficient \(\lambda_c\) is localized to the \(JJ\)-sector.
\end{enumerate}

Consequently, the remaining actual carrier-side longitudinal audit reduces to the finite check
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:lamc_final_test}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Statements (1)–(3) are exactly \eqref{eq:lamc_cparK_zero}, \eqref{eq:lamc_JK_trans_only}, and \eqref{eq:lamc_KK_no_long}.
Statement (4) then follows immediately, since the only shell-relevant principal Class-II contribution not excluded from the longitudinal \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet is the \(JJ\)-sector.
Thus the primitive odd longitudinal coefficient must be extracted from that sector alone.
\end{proof}

\section{What remains to be computed}

After the present theorem, the longitudinal carrier problem is no longer a broad microscopic classification problem.

It is reduced to one coefficient extraction problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{evaluate the axial shell-singlet coefficient }j^2
\text{ (equivalently }\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\text{) in the actual refined locked basis.}
}
\label{eq:lamc_remaining}
\end{equation}

Once this is nonzero, one gets
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0,
\]
because \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\).

\section{Final Summary}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the primitive longitudinal odd singlet is sourced only by the axial \(JJ\)-sector at principal shell order.

More precisely,
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(JK)}=0,
\qquad
c_\parallel^{(KK)}=0
\quad
\text{at principal longitudinal shell order},
}
\]
while
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(JJ)}
\ \text{is allowed and is the unique principal Class-II longitudinal source.}
}
\]

Equivalently, the reduced dictionary has the sharp split
\[
JJ\leadsto \lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
JK/KK\leadsto (\alpha,\beta).
\]

In the explicit branch,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
\alpha
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\! k)\Lambda_O^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\! k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}.
\]

Therefore the remaining actual longitudinal frontier is reduced to one finite extraction problem:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\quad\text{(equivalently }j^2\neq 0\text{ or }m_3\neq 0\text{).}
}
\]
