\section{Finite Matrix-Element Theorem for the Longitudinal \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} Coefficient}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The last carrier-side longitudinal question is no longer a source-classification problem.
It is a concrete \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrix computation.

The pure \(JJ\)-sector produces an axial shell-normal block
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
\]
and the longitudinal witness is exactly the \(\sigma_3\)-component of \(M\).

Therefore the actual longitudinal frontier is reduced to checking whether the two tangent-doublet basis states couple unequally to the axial \(JJ\)-source.

\section{Axial shell-normal form of the \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} block}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the pure \(JJ\)-piece of the shell-reduced first-order kernel has the universal form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
}
\label{eq:jjM_axial_form}
\end{equation}
where \(M\) is a Hermitian \(2\times2\) operator on the reduced tangent-doublet space.  :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Write its Pauli decomposition as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M=m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:jjM_pauli}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
p_iK_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\Gamma_J p_\parallel
(m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3).
\]
Since the pure \(JJ\)-sector is axial only, it can probe only the longitudinal shell-normal singlet channel, and the witness is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\propto m_3.
}
\label{eq:jjM_lambda_m3}
\end{equation}
The transverse witnesses vanish in this sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0,
\qquad
\beta^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0.
}
\label{eq:jjM_no_trans}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the axial-only statement for the pure \(JJ\)-piece.  

\section{Actual matrix-element formula}

Choose an orthonormal tangent-doublet basis
\[
\{u_1,u_2\}
\]
for the shell-localized reduced subspace \(\mathcal H_*\).
Then
\begin{equation}
M_{\alpha\beta}
=
\langle u_\alpha,\,M\,u_\beta\rangle,
\qquad
\alpha,\beta\in\{1,2\}.
\label{eq:jjM_entries}
\end{equation}
Since \(M\) is Hermitian,
\[
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
M_{11} & M_{12}\\
\overline{M_{12}} & M_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Comparing with \eqref{eq:jjM_pauli}, one gets the exact identities
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_0=\frac12(M_{11}+M_{22}),
\qquad
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}),
}
\label{eq:jjM_m0m3}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_1=\Re M_{12},
\qquad
m_2=-\Im M_{12}.
}
\label{eq:jjM_m1m2}
\end{equation}

Therefore the longitudinal witness coefficient is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\propto \frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}).
}
\label{eq:jjM_lambda_diagdiff}
\end{equation}

\section{Interpretation in terms of tangent-doublet asymmetry}

Equation \eqref{eq:jjM_lambda_diagdiff} shows that the longitudinal \(JJ\)-coefficient is nonzero exactly when the two tangent-doublet basis states couple unequally to the axial \(JJ\)-source:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
}
\label{eq:jjM_criterion}
\end{equation}

Thus the longitudinal audit is not a mysterious nonlinear problem.
It is the finite check of whether the axial \(JJ\)-sector distinguishes the two tangent-doublet channels.

\section{Generic nonvanishing theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Generic nonvanishing of the axial singlet coefficient]
Let \(M\) be the Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix extracted from the pure \(JJ\)-sector as in \eqref{eq:jjM_axial_form}. Suppose there is no exact microscopic symmetry forcing the tangent-doublet exchange
\[
u_1\longleftrightarrow u_2
\]
to be a symmetry of the \(JJ\)-source at the selected shell pair.

Then the condition
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
is a codimension-one fine-tuning relation, and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\quad\text{generically.}
}
\label{eq:jjM_generic}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:jjM_m0m3}, the equality \(m_3=0\) is exactly the single real equation
\[
M_{11}-M_{22}=0.
\]
In the space of Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrices
\[
\mathrm{Herm}(2)\cong \mathbb R^4,
\]
this cuts out a codimension-one affine hyperplane.
Hence, unless an exact symmetry forces the matrix to lie on that hyperplane, the generic value is off the hyperplane, i.e.
\[
M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
\]
Therefore \(m_3\neq 0\) generically.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Honest meaning.}
This does \emph{not} prove that the actual current branch already satisfies \(m_3\neq 0\).
It proves that the only way the longitudinal \(JJ\)-coefficient can vanish is through an exact symmetry or a fine-tuned equality of the two diagonal shell couplings.

\section{Exact symmetry obstruction theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Exact obstruction to \(m_3\)]
Suppose there exists a Hermitian involution \(S\) on the tangent-doublet space such that
\begin{equation}
Su_1=u_2,
\qquad
Su_2=u_1,
\label{eq:jjM_swap}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
[S,M]=0.
\label{eq:jjM_swap_comm}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{11}=M_{22},
\qquad
m_3=0.
}
\label{eq:jjM_swap_zero}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(S\) swaps \(u_1\) and \(u_2\),
\[
M_{11}
=
\langle u_1,Mu_1\rangle
=
\langle Su_1,SMu_1\rangle
=
\langle u_2,MSu_1\rangle
=
\langle u_2,Mu_2\rangle
=
M_{22},
\]
where we used \(S^\dagger=S\), \(S^2=\mathbf1\), and \([S,M]=0\).
Then \eqref{eq:jjM_m0m3} gives \(m_3=0\).
\end{proof}

\section{Practical audit theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Practical longitudinal \(JJ\)-audit]
The remaining actual carrier-side longitudinal frontier in the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is reduced to the following finite matrix audit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item extract the pure \(JJ\)-shell block and its axial matrix \(M\);
\item compute the two diagonal matrix elements
\[
M_{11}=\langle u_1,Mu_1\rangle,
\qquad
M_{22}=\langle u_2,Mu_2\rangle;
\]
\item test whether
\[
M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{11}\neq M_{22},
}
\label{eq:jjM_practical_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:jjM_practical_conclusion}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The first implication is exactly \eqref{eq:jjM_criterion}.
The second is the source-classification statement that the primitive longitudinal Class-II coefficient is localized to the \(JJ\)-sector.
The third follows from the already established longitudinal witness formula
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,\lambda_c\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
\end{proof}

\section{Equivalent projector form}

Equivalently, if \(\Pi_\pm\) denote the one-dimensional projectors onto the two tangent-doublet basis states, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\bigl((\Pi_1-\Pi_2)M\bigr).
}
\label{eq:jjM_projector_form}
\end{equation}
So the audit may be phrased basis-freely as:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{Tr}\bigl((\Pi_1-\Pi_2)M\bigr)\neq 0\ ?
}
\label{eq:jjM_basisfree_audit}
\end{equation}

\section{What is actually left}

After the present theorem, the longitudinal carrier problem is reduced to one explicit finite extraction:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the actual pure-}JJ\text{ axial shell matrix }M
\text{ and test }M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
}
\label{eq:jjM_last_task}
\end{equation}

Everything before this point is already closed structurally.

\section{Final Summary}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the pure \(JJ\)-sector has axial shell-normal form
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
\]
with \(M\in \mathrm{Herm}(2)\).

Writing
\[
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
M_{11} & M_{12}\\
\overline{M_{12}} & M_{22}
\end{pmatrix}
=
m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3,
\]
one has
\[
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}).
\]

Since the pure \(JJ\)-sector is axial only,
\[
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\propto m_3,
\qquad
\alpha^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=\beta^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0.
\]

Therefore the remaining actual longitudinal carrier audit is the finite test
\[
\boxed{
M_{11}\neq M_{22}\ ?
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

Vanishing of \(m_3\) requires either an exact tangent-doublet exchange symmetry or a codimension-one fine-tuning relation.
Thus nonzero \(m_3\) is the generic outcome unless a specific symmetry obstruction is present.

So the last remaining carrier-side frontier is no longer a broad source-classification problem.
It is exactly the extraction of the diagonal asymmetry of the axial \(JJ\)-matrix in the actual refined locked basis.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Symmetry-Resolved Finite Audit of the Axial \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} Matrix}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining longitudinal frontier is a finite \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrix problem.

The pure \(JJ\)-sector defines an axial shell-normal matrix \(M\), and the longitudinal witness is its \(\sigma_3\)-coefficient
\[
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}).
\]

So there are only two logically possible reasons for longitudinal failure:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an exact tangent-doublet exchange symmetry forces \(M_{11}=M_{22}\);
\item an accidental codimension-one cancellation happens.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore, unless an exact microscopic symmetry enforces the equality, the generic expectation is \(m_3\neq 0\).

\section{Axial \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} matrix and its witness}

In the shell-adapted reduced tangent-doublet basis \(\{u_1,u_2\}\), the pure \(JJ\)-piece has the axial form
\begin{equation}
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
\qquad
M\in\mathrm{Herm}(2).
\label{eq:m3audit_axial}
\end{equation}
Write
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
M_{11} & M_{12}\\
\overline{M_{12}} & M_{22}
\end{pmatrix}
=
m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3.
\label{eq:m3audit_Mdecomp}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}).
}
\label{eq:m3audit_m3diag}
\end{equation}
Since the pure \(JJ\)-sector is axial only, the longitudinal shell witness is proportional to \(m_3\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(JJ)}\propto m_3.
}
\label{eq:m3audit_lam}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact swap-symmetry obstruction}

Assume there exists a Hermitian involution \(S\) on the tangent-doublet space such that
\begin{equation}
Su_1=u_2,
\qquad
Su_2=u_1,
\qquad
S^2=\mathbf 1,
\qquad
S^\dagger=S.
\label{eq:m3audit_swap}
\end{equation}
Suppose further that the pure \(JJ\)-source is invariant under this swap:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[S,M]=0.
}
\label{eq:m3audit_swapinv}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Exact obstruction theorem]
Under \eqref{eq:m3audit_swap}--\eqref{eq:m3audit_swapinv},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{11}=M_{22},
\qquad
m_3=0.
}
\label{eq:m3audit_obstruction}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Using \(S^\dagger=S\), \(S^2=\mathbf 1\), and \([S,M]=0\),
\begin{align}
M_{11}
&=
\langle u_1,Mu_1\rangle
=
\langle Su_1,SMu_1\rangle
=
\langle u_2,MSu_1\rangle
=
\langle u_2,Mu_2\rangle
=
M_{22}.
\end{align}
Then \eqref{eq:m3audit_m3diag} gives \(m_3=0\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
An exact tangent-doublet exchange symmetry is a genuine microscopic obstruction to the longitudinal primitive channel.

\section{Converse structural statement}

We now prove the contrapositive in the only honest form available.

\begin{theorem}[Absence of forced equality]
Suppose there is no exact microscopic symmetry whose reduced action on the tangent-doublet space exchanges \(u_1\leftrightarrow u_2\) and leaves the pure \(JJ\)-source invariant.

Then the relation
\begin{equation}
M_{11}=M_{22}
\label{eq:m3audit_equal_plane}
\end{equation}
is not symmetry-protected.
Consequently, inside the real affine space \(\mathrm{Herm}(2)\cong\mathbb R^4\), it is a codimension-one condition, and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\quad\text{generically.}
}
\label{eq:m3audit_generic}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The equation \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is exactly the single real linear constraint
\[
m_3=0.
\]
So it defines a codimension-one affine hyperplane in \(\mathrm{Herm}(2)\).
If no exact symmetry forces \(M\) to lie in that hyperplane, then lying there is a fine-tuning condition rather than a structurally protected consequence.
Hence the generic matrix in the allowed family satisfies \(m_3\neq 0\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Honest caveat.}
This theorem is generic, not absolute.
It does not prove that the actual current branch already has \(m_3\neq 0\).
It proves that vanishing of \(m_3\) must come either from an exact symmetry obstruction or from a codimension-one cancellation.

\section{Microscopic matrix-element realization}

The matrix entries are extracted from the actual refined locked \(JJ\)-kernel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{\alpha\beta}
=
-\frac{1}{\Gamma_J\hat n^i}
\langle u_\alpha, K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)} u_\beta\rangle,
\qquad
\alpha,\beta\in\{1,2\}.
}
\label{eq:m3audit_matrix_extract}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, if one starts from the shell-harmonic \(J\)-tensor,
\begin{equation}
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,j^a\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{a}
+
\mathsf J^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
\label{eq:m3audit_Jtensor}
\end{equation}
then the pure \(JJ\)-reduced shell matrix \(M\) is obtained by projecting the induced bilinear onto the tangent-doublet shell core.

The longitudinal audit is therefore exactly the finite test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{11}\neq M_{22}\ ?
}
\label{eq:m3audit_finite_test}
\end{equation}

\section{Carrier-side consequence}

Since the current source classification has already localized the principal longitudinal coefficient to the \(JJ\)-sector, one has
\begin{equation}
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\label{eq:m3audit_chain}
\end{equation}
because
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,\lambda_c\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\label{eq:m3audit_I3}
\end{equation}

\section{Final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Last finite carrier-side longitudinal audit]
At the current project stage, the remaining honest carrier-side frontier is reduced to the following finite matrix audit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item extract the pure \(JJ\)-axial shell matrix \(M\);
\item test whether an exact tangent-doublet exchange symmetry forces
\[
M_{11}=M_{22};
\]
\item if no such symmetry exists, then \(m_3=0\) is only codimension-one fine-tuning;
\item consequently, the decisive executable test is
\[
\boxed{
M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
}
\]
\end{enumerate}

If this holds, then
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]
So the carrier-side longitudinal slot closes.
\end{theorem}

\section{Final Summary}

The remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now a finite \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrix audit.

For the axial pure \(JJ\)-sector,
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
\qquad
M\in\mathrm{Herm}(2).
\]
Writing
\[
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
M_{11} & M_{12}\\
\overline{M_{12}} & M_{22}
\end{pmatrix}
=
m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3,
\]
one has
\[
\boxed{
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}),
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel^{(JJ)}\propto m_3.
}
\]

If there exists an exact tangent-doublet exchange symmetry preserving the \(JJ\)-source, then
\[
M_{11}=M_{22},
\qquad
m_3=0.
\]
If no such symmetry exists, then the equality \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is only a codimension-one fine-tuning condition in \(\mathrm{Herm}(2)\), so
\[
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\quad\text{generically.}
}
\]

Therefore the decisive remaining executable test is
\[
\boxed{
M_{11}\neq M_{22}\ ?
}
\]
If yes, then
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section{Little-Group Non-Obstruction Theorem for the Axial \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} Audit}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining longitudinal audit was reduced to the finite test
\[
M_{11}\neq M_{22}\ ?,
\qquad
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}).
\]

So the only structural way to force \(m_3=0\) would be an exact symmetry exchanging the two tangent-doublet basis states.

We now prove that the ordinary shell little group does \emph{not} force such an exchange symmetry.
Therefore the equality \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is not protected by the ordinary little group itself.

\section{Ordinary little-group data}

Fix the selected shell direction
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]
The ordinary pointwise little groups are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Stab}(+\hat n)\cong C_{2v},
\qquad
\mathrm{Stab}(\{\pm \hat n\})\cong D_{2h}.
}
\label{eq:lg_nonobs_groups}
\end{equation}

Both groups are abelian.
Hence every ordinary complex irreducible representation is one-dimensional.
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{ordinary little-group irreducibility does not force the local }2\text{D tangent doublet.}
}
\label{eq:lg_nonobs_no2Dirrep}
\end{equation}

This is the exact honest status already established in the shell-relevant carrier analysis.

\section{Geometric transverse doublet versus microscopic swap symmetry}

There is a geometric transverse plane
\[
\Pi_\perp=\mathrm{span}\{e_1,e_2\},
\]
and the spatial witness family
\[
W^{(\alpha)}_{ij}=e^\alpha_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2,
\]
transforms as the transverse \(2\)-component family under the shell-axis little-group action.

However, this geometric two-component family is \emph{not} the same as an exact microscopic symmetry exchanging the reduced tangent-doublet basis vectors
\[
u_1\leftrightarrow u_2.
\]

Indeed, the latter would require a Hermitian involution \(S\) on the actual reduced tangent-doublet space such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Su_1=u_2,
\qquad
Su_2=u_1,
\qquad
[S,M]=0,
}
\label{eq:lg_nonobs_swapreq}
\end{equation}
where \(M\) is the axial pure-\(JJ\) shell matrix.
This is an additional microscopic symmetry statement, not a consequence of ordinary little-group representation theory alone.

\section{Main theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Little-group non-obstruction theorem]
Let \(M\in \mathrm{Herm}(2)\) be the axial pure-\(JJ\) shell matrix in the actual refined locked tangent-doublet basis \(\{u_1,u_2\}\).
Then the ordinary shell little group does not force
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{11}=M_{22}.
}
\label{eq:lg_nonobs_equal}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the ordinary shell little group does not force
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22})=0.
}
\label{eq:lg_nonobs_m3zero}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:lg_nonobs_groups}, the ordinary little groups \(C_{2v}\) and \(D_{2h}\) are abelian, so all their ordinary complex irreducible representations are one-dimensional.

Hence the existence of the actual microscopic local carrier
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
is not enforced by ordinary little-group irreducibility.
It arises from the shell-relevant valley pairing together with the enriched internal doublet structure, not from a mandatory \(2\)-dimensional ordinary irrep.

Therefore an exact involution \(S\) exchanging \(u_1\leftrightarrow u_2\) and preserving the pure-\(JJ\) source is not supplied by the ordinary little group alone.
But \eqref{eq:lg_nonobs_equal} would be symmetry-forced only if such an \(S\) existed.

Thus the ordinary little group by itself does not force \(M_{11}=M_{22}\), and therefore does not force \(m_3=0\).
\end{proof}

\section{Corollary: the only structural obstruction is extra microscopic symmetry}

\begin{corollary}[Exact obstruction criterion]
If \(m_3=0\) is to be structurally forced, then there must exist an additional microscopic symmetry beyond ordinary little-group representation theory, namely a reduced tangent-doublet exchange involution \(S\) satisfying
\[
Su_1=u_2,\qquad Su_2=u_1,\qquad [S,M]=0.
\]
Without such an extra symmetry, the condition
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
is not symmetry-protected.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
This is immediate from the previous theorem together with the earlier swap-obstruction theorem:
an exact equality \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is forced only by an exact symmetry exchanging the two reduced tangent-doublet channels.
Since the ordinary little group does not provide such a symmetry, any structural obstruction must come from extra microscopic symmetry.
\end{proof}

\section{Genericity consequence}

Since
\[
\mathrm{Herm}(2)\cong \mathbb R^4,
\]
the condition
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
is exactly one real linear constraint, i.e. a codimension-one affine hyperplane.
Therefore, once the ordinary little group is excluded as a forcing mechanism, the remaining alternatives are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an additional exact microscopic exchange symmetry exists;
\item or \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is merely accidental fine-tuning.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the honest generic conclusion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\quad\text{generically, unless an extra microscopic exchange symmetry is actually present.}
}
\label{eq:lg_nonobs_generic}
\end{equation}

\section{Carrier-side conclusion}

Because the longitudinal primitive Class-II coefficient is localized to the axial \(JJ\)-sector, one has
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
Therefore the actual carrier-side longitudinal audit is reduced to the following precise finite task:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{either identify an extra microscopic exchange symmetry forcing }M_{11}=M_{22},
\text{ or compute }M_{11}-M_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\label{eq:lg_nonobs_lasttask}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The ordinary shell little group does not force the vanishing of the axial longitudinal coefficient.

Indeed,
\[
\mathrm{Stab}(+\hat n)\cong C_{2v},
\qquad
\mathrm{Stab}(\{\pm\hat n\})\cong D_{2h},
\]
and both groups are abelian, so all ordinary complex irreducible representations are one-dimensional.
Therefore ordinary little-group irreducibility does not force the actual local \(2\)-component tangent doublet, nor an exact exchange symmetry \(u_1\leftrightarrow u_2\).

Hence the equality
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
is not protected by the ordinary little group itself.

So the only structural ways to obtain
\[
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22})=0
\]
are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an additional exact microscopic exchange symmetry beyond the ordinary little group;
\item an accidental codimension-one cancellation.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the honest generic conclusion is
\[
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\quad\text{generically, unless an extra microscopic exchange symmetry is actually present.}
}
\]

Thus the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to one explicit finite audit:
\[
\boxed{
\text{either identify an extra microscopic exchange symmetry, or compute }M_{11}-M_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\]

\section{Label-Obstruction Theorem for a Tangent-Doublet Exchange Symmetry}

\section{Goal}

The remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier has been reduced to the finite matrix test
\[
M_{11}\neq M_{22},
\qquad
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}).
\]
The only structural way to force
\[
m_3=0
\]
is an exact microscopic symmetry exchanging the two tangent-doublet states.

We now prove that any such exchange symmetry must preserve \emph{every} exact shell-relevant label of the two states.
Therefore, if the two states differ in even one exact label, then no such symmetry exists.
Since the ordinary shell little group does not itself provide such an exchange symmetry, the equality
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
is not structurally forced unless an extra microscopic label-preserving involution is explicitly present.

\section{Tangent-doublet exchange symmetry}

Let \(\mathcal H_*=\mathrm{span}\{u_1,u_2\}\) be the reduced tangent-doublet space and let
\[
M\in\mathrm{Herm}(2)
\]
be the axial pure-\(JJ\) shell matrix.
An exact exchange symmetry is a Hermitian involution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S:\mathcal H_*\to\mathcal H_*,
\qquad
S^2=\mathbf 1,
\qquad
Su_1=u_2,\qquad Su_2=u_1,
}
\label{eq:labelobs_Sdef}
\end{equation}
such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[S,M]=0.
}
\label{eq:labelobs_SM}
\end{equation}

As proved earlier, \eqref{eq:labelobs_Sdef}--\eqref{eq:labelobs_SM} imply
\[
M_{11}=M_{22},
\qquad
m_3=0.
\]

So the problem is reduced to determining whether such an \(S\) can exist microscopically.

\section{Exact shell-relevant labels}

Let \(\mathfrak L\) denote the complete exact shell-relevant label package of a low-energy carrier state.
At the current level of reduction, the exact labels are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L=
\Bigl(
\pm G_*,
\ \text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\ \text{enriched internal doublet},
\ \text{grading/parity/chirality},
\ \text{extra conserved microscopic labels}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:labelobs_labels}
\end{equation}

Each entry is assumed to be carried by an exact commuting label operator on the microscopic Hilbert space.
Equivalently, there is a finite commuting family
\[
\{\Lambda_\alpha\}_{\alpha\in A}
\]
such that each \(\Lambda_\alpha\) is self-adjoint, each exact carrier state is a simultaneous eigenvector,
and the tuple of eigenvalues reproduces the exact label package \(\mathfrak L\).

\section{Necessary condition for exchange symmetry}

\begin{theorem}[Label-obstruction theorem]
Let \(u_1,u_2\in \mathcal H_*\) be simultaneous eigenstates of all exact label operators \(\Lambda_\alpha\):
\[
\Lambda_\alpha u_i=\lambda_\alpha^{(i)}u_i,
\qquad i=1,2.
\]
Suppose there exists an exact exchange symmetry \(S\) satisfying \eqref{eq:labelobs_Sdef}, and assume it preserves the microscopic realization of every exact label:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[S,\Lambda_\alpha]=0
\qquad
\forall \alpha.
}
\label{eq:labelobs_comm}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\alpha^{(1)}=\lambda_\alpha^{(2)}
\qquad
\forall \alpha.
}
\label{eq:labelobs_equal_labels}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) must agree in every exact shell-relevant label.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix \(\alpha\).
Using \(Su_1=u_2\) and \([S,\Lambda_\alpha]=0\),
\[
\Lambda_\alpha u_2
=
\Lambda_\alpha S u_1
=
S\Lambda_\alpha u_1
=
S(\lambda_\alpha^{(1)}u_1)
=
\lambda_\alpha^{(1)}u_2.
\]
But also
\[
\Lambda_\alpha u_2=\lambda_\alpha^{(2)}u_2.
\]
Since \(u_2\neq 0\), it follows that
\[
\lambda_\alpha^{(2)}=\lambda_\alpha^{(1)}.
\]
As \(\alpha\) was arbitrary, the equality holds for all exact labels.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Immediate contrapositive.}
If there exists even one exact shell-relevant label \(\Lambda_\alpha\) such that
\[
\lambda_\alpha^{(1)}\neq \lambda_\alpha^{(2)},
\]
then no exchange involution \(S\) commuting with all exact microscopic labels can exist.

\section{Application to the current shell-relevant setting}

The ordinary shell little group provides only the abelian groups
\[
\mathrm{Stab}(+\hat n)\cong C_{2v},
\qquad
\mathrm{Stab}(\{\pm\hat n\})\cong D_{2h},
\]
so ordinary little-group irreducibility does not force a two-dimensional exchange symmetry on the actual tangent-doublet carrier.
Hence any exchange symmetry forcing
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
must come from an additional microscopic symmetry beyond the ordinary little group.

But by the theorem above, such a symmetry is possible only if the two tangent-doublet states are identical in all exact shell-relevant labels.
Therefore the only structural routes to
\[
m_3=0
\]
are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an extra microscopic exchange symmetry exists and preserves all exact labels;
\item or the equality \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) happens accidentally as fine-tuning.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Practical audit criterion}

The previous theorem yields the following executable criterion.

\begin{theorem}[Executable obstruction test]
Assume the actual tangent-doublet states \(u_1,u_2\) are identified in the refined locked shell basis.

If one can verify that \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) differ in at least one exact shell-relevant label among
\[
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{enriched internal-doublet data},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra conserved labels},
\]
then no exact microscopic exchange involution \(S\) preserving the full label package can exist.
Consequently, the equality
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
is not symmetry-protected.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If such an \(S\) existed and preserved all exact labels, then by the label-obstruction theorem the two states would have to agree in every exact shell-relevant label.
So any verified mismatch excludes the existence of such an \(S\).
The equality \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is then not symmetry-forced.
\end{proof}

\section{Honest generic consequence}

Since
\[
\mathrm{Herm}(2)\cong \mathbb R^4,
\]
the condition
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
is exactly the codimension-one linear condition
\[
m_3=0.
\]
Therefore, once symmetry protection is excluded, the honest generic conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\quad\text{generically.}
}
\label{eq:labelobs_generic}
\end{equation}

\section{What this does and does not prove}

What is proved:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an exact symmetry forcing \(m_3=0\) must preserve every exact shell-relevant label;
\item ordinary little-group data alone do not provide such a symmetry;
\item therefore \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is not automatically protected.
\end{enumerate}

What is not yet proved:

\begin{enumerate}
\item that the actual refined locked tangent-doublet states \(u_1,u_2\) differ in a specific exact label;
\item or, alternatively, the explicit numerical value of \(M_{11}-M_{22}\).
\end{enumerate}

Thus the remaining carrier-side frontier is now sharply split into two finite tasks:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{either identify an exact label mismatch between }u_1\text{ and }u_2,
\quad\text{or compute }M_{11}-M_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\label{eq:labelobs_last}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

An exact microscopic exchange symmetry forcing
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
must preserve every exact shell-relevant label of the two tangent-doublet states \(u_1,u_2\).

If \(\{\Lambda_\alpha\}\) is the complete commuting family of exact label operators and
\[
\Lambda_\alpha u_i=\lambda_\alpha^{(i)}u_i,
\qquad i=1,2,
\]
then any involution \(S\) satisfying
\[
Su_1=u_2,\qquad Su_2=u_1,\qquad [S,\Lambda_\alpha]=0
\]
forces
\[
\lambda_\alpha^{(1)}=\lambda_\alpha^{(2)}
\qquad
\forall\alpha.
\]

Therefore, if \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) differ in even one exact shell-relevant label, no such exchange symmetry can exist.

Since the ordinary shell little groups
\[
\mathrm{Stab}(+\hat n)\cong C_{2v},
\qquad
\mathrm{Stab}(\{\pm\hat n\})\cong D_{2h}
\]
are abelian, they do not themselves force such an exchange symmetry.

Hence \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is not protected by the ordinary little group.
It can only arise from:
\begin{enumerate}
\item an additional exact microscopic exchange symmetry preserving all labels; or
\item codimension-one accidental fine-tuning.
\end{enumerate}

So the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to the finite task:
\[
\boxed{
\text{either identify a label mismatch between }u_1\text{ and }u_2,
\quad\text{or compute }M_{11}-M_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Internal-Label Localization Theorem for the Tangent-Doublet Swap Audit}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The shell-relevant label package was introduced to classify whether a remote sector can mix with the local Dirac carrier.
We now apply the same label logic internally to the two tangent-doublet states \(u_1,u_2\) inside the carrier itself.

The result is sharp:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-pair label is automatically the same for \(u_1,u_2\);
\item the gross kinematic type is automatically the same;
\item the enriched internal-doublet membership is also automatically the same;
\item therefore the only possible exact label obstruction to an exchange symmetry comes from
\[
\text{grading/parity/chirality}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{extra conserved microscopic labels}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the longitudinal carrier audit is now reduced to checking only the internal label splitting of the enriched doublet.

\section{Carrier basis}

The correct shell-relevant local carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
}
\label{eq:intlabel_HD}
\end{equation}
where the valley factor is the selected opposite-shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and the internal factor is the enriched transverse/internal doublet. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

The explicit shell-pair basis is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Phi_{+,a}(x)=e^{+iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a,
\qquad
\Phi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a,
\qquad
a=1,2,
}
\label{eq:intlabel_basis}
\end{equation}
so the two internal states \(u_1,u_2\) are, by construction, the basis of the same enriched internal doublet. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\section{Shell-relevant label package}

The exact shell-relevant labels are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra conserved labels}.
}
\label{eq:intlabel_package}
\end{equation}
These are exactly the labels used in the actual microscopic mismatch audit. 

\section{Automatic equalities inside the carrier doublet}

We now show that the first three labels are automatically identical for \(u_1,u_2\).

\subsection{Shell-pair label}

Both \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) appear in the same shell-pair basis \(\Phi_{\pm,a}\) with the same selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\).
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_{\pm G_*}(u_1)=\mathfrak L_{\pm G_*}(u_2).
}
\label{eq:intlabel_shell_same}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Gross kinematic type}

The carrier is the enriched shell-relevant Dirac sector, which is by definition the transverse/non-volumetric local carrier.
The two basis states \(u_1,u_2\) span the same internal part of that carrier.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_{\mathrm{kin}}(u_1)=\mathfrak L_{\mathrm{kin}}(u_2)=\text{transverse/non-volumetric}.
}
\label{eq:intlabel_kin_same}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Enriched-doublet membership}

By \eqref{eq:intlabel_HD} and \eqref{eq:intlabel_basis}, the pair \(u_1,u_2\) is exactly the basis of the enriched internal doublet \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\).
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_{\mathrm{enr}}(u_1)=\mathfrak L_{\mathrm{enr}}(u_2)=\text{present in the same enriched doublet}.
}
\label{eq:intlabel_enr_same}
\end{equation}

\section{Localization of the possible obstruction}

Combining \eqref{eq:intlabel_shell_same}, \eqref{eq:intlabel_kin_same}, and \eqref{eq:intlabel_enr_same}, we obtain:

\begin{theorem}[Internal-label localization theorem]
Any exact shell-relevant label obstruction to a tangent-doublet exchange symmetry
\[
Su_1=u_2,\qquad Su_2=u_1
\]
cannot come from:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-pair label \(\pm G_*\),
\item the transverse/non-volumetric character,
\item the enriched internal-doublet membership.
\end{enumerate}
Hence the only remaining possible exact label obstructions are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{grading/parity/chirality}
\quad\text{and/or}\quad
\text{extra conserved microscopic labels}.
}
\label{eq:intlabel_only_remaining}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The first three labels are already equal for \(u_1,u_2\) by construction of the carrier basis.
So any exact-label mismatch between \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) must lie in the remaining two classes.
\end{proof}

\section{Exchange-symmetry exclusion criterion}

We already proved the general label-obstruction principle:
if an exact exchange symmetry \(S\) preserves all exact labels, then \(u_1,u_2\) must agree in every exact shell-relevant label.

Applying that principle together with \eqref{eq:intlabel_only_remaining}, we obtain:

\begin{theorem}[Executable exclusion criterion]
If \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) differ in either
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{grading/parity/chirality}
}
\label{eq:intlabel_gpclabel}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{an extra exact conserved microscopic label},
}
\label{eq:intlabel_extralabel}
\end{equation}
then no exact microscopic exchange involution \(S\) preserving the full shell-relevant label package can exist.
Consequently, the equality
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
is not symmetry-protected.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the previous theorem, the first three labels coincide automatically.
So any label mismatch must lie in the last two classes.
The general label-obstruction theorem then excludes the existence of a label-preserving exchange involution.
Hence \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) cannot be structurally forced by such a symmetry.
\end{proof}

\section{Honest generic consequence}

Since the ordinary little group itself does not force the exchange symmetry, and the first three shell-relevant labels are automatically equal inside the carrier doublet, the only nontrivial structural obstruction must come from internal grading/parity/chirality splitting or some extra exact conserved label.

Therefore the honest generic statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{unless an actual internal label splitting is explicitly present,}
\quad
M_{11}=M_{22}
\text{ is not symmetry-forced by the known shell-relevant structure alone.}
}
\label{eq:intlabel_honest_generic}
\end{equation}

This does \emph{not} yet prove \(M_{11}\neq M_{22}\).
It proves that the only remaining structural obstruction has been localized to a much smaller audit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{check whether }u_1,u_2\text{ differ in grading/parity/chirality or in any extra exact conserved label.}
}
\label{eq:intlabel_last_audit}
\end{equation}

\section{What is actually left}

After the present theorem, the last carrier-side longitudinal frontier is sharply split into two finite possibilities:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Label route:}
prove that \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) differ in an exact internal label, which excludes the exchange symmetry and removes structural protection of \(M_{11}=M_{22}\);

\item \textbf{Direct matrix route:}
compute the pure-\(JJ\) axial matrix elements \(M_{11},M_{22}\) explicitly.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the remaining problem is no longer broad.
It is either one internal label audit or one \(2\times2\) matrix extraction.

\section{Final Summary}

Inside the actual shell-relevant carrier
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
the two tangent-doublet states \(u_1,u_2\) automatically share:

\[
\pm G_*,
\qquad
\text{the transverse/non-volumetric carrier type},
\qquad
\text{the same enriched internal-doublet membership}.
\]

Therefore any exact shell-relevant label obstruction to an exchange symmetry
\[
u_1\leftrightarrow u_2
\]
must come only from:
\[
\boxed{
\text{grading/parity/chirality}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{extra exact conserved microscopic labels}.
}
\]

So the last carrier-side longitudinal obstruction is sharply localized.
Either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item one proves an internal label mismatch between \(u_1\) and \(u_2\), which excludes an exact exchange symmetry; or
\item one computes the axial pure-\(JJ\) matrix difference \(M_{11}-M_{22}\) directly.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the problem is no longer broad.
It is reduced to one internal-label audit or one explicit \(2\times2\) matrix extraction.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Parity/Grading Split as an Exact Obstruction to Tangent-Doublet Exchange}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining possible structural obstruction to the longitudinal audit was localized to:
\[
\text{grading/parity/chirality}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{extra conserved labels}.
\]

We now prove the strongest exact version of this statement:

if the two tangent-doublet states \(u_1,u_2\) carry different eigenvalues of any exact grading/parity/chirality operator, then no exact exchange symmetry preserving the microscopic labels can exist.

Therefore \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is not symmetry-protected in that case.

\section{Exact grading/parity operator}

Let \(J\) be an exact Hermitian involution on the reduced carrier space:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J^2=\mathbf 1,
\qquad
J^\dagger=J.
}
\label{eq:paritysplit_Jdef}
\end{equation}

Assume \(J\) is part of the exact microscopic shell-relevant label package, i.e. it is one of the admissible grading/parity/chirality label operators.
Then the tangent-doublet states may be chosen as \(J\)-eigenvectors:
\begin{equation}
Ju_1=\epsilon_1 u_1,
\qquad
Ju_2=\epsilon_2 u_2,
\qquad
\epsilon_i\in\{+1,-1\}.
\label{eq:paritysplit_Jeig}
\end{equation}

\section{Exchange symmetry compatible with exact labels}

An exact microscopic exchange symmetry is an involution \(S\) satisfying
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Su_1=u_2,
\qquad
Su_2=u_1,
\qquad
S^2=\mathbf 1,
\qquad
S^\dagger=S.
}
\label{eq:paritysplit_Sdef}
\end{equation}

If this exchange symmetry preserves the exact label package, then in particular it must preserve \(J\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[S,J]=0.
}
\label{eq:paritysplit_comm}
\end{equation}

\section{Main obstruction theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Exact grading/parity obstruction]
Assume \eqref{eq:paritysplit_Jdef}--\eqref{eq:paritysplit_comm}.
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\epsilon_1\neq \epsilon_2,
}
\label{eq:paritysplit_diff}
\end{equation}
then no exact label-preserving exchange symmetry \(S\) can exist.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Suppose, for contradiction, that such an \(S\) exists.

Using \([S,J]=0\) and \(Su_1=u_2\),
\[
Ju_2
=
JSu_1
=
SJu_1
=
S(\epsilon_1 u_1)
=
\epsilon_1 u_2.
\]
But by \eqref{eq:paritysplit_Jeig},
\[
Ju_2=\epsilon_2 u_2.
\]
Since \(u_2\neq 0\), it follows that
\[
\epsilon_2=\epsilon_1,
\]
contradicting \eqref{eq:paritysplit_diff}.
Therefore no such \(S\) can exist.
\end{proof}

\section{Immediate carrier-side consequence}

Recall that the only structural way to force
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
was an exact tangent-doublet exchange symmetry preserving the microscopic labels.

Therefore, if \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) carry opposite exact grading/parity/chirality eigenvalues, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{11}=M_{22}
\quad\text{is not symmetry-protected.}
}
\label{eq:paritysplit_no_protection}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the vanishing
\[
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22})=0
\]
can then occur only by accidental codimension-one fine-tuning, not by exact label-preserving symmetry.

\section{Chiral/selection-rule refinement}

There is a second useful exact statement.
Suppose the leading reduced perturbation operator \(V_1(p)\) is odd under the same involution \(J\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J V_1(p) J^{-1}=-V_1(p).
}
\label{eq:paritysplit_Vodd}
\end{equation}
Then same-parity matrix elements vanish:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_\pm V_1(p)\Pi_\pm=0,
}
\label{eq:paritysplit_blockoff}
\end{equation}
where \(\Pi_\pm\) are the spectral projectors of \(J\). This is the standard selection-rule criterion for block-off-diagonality of the reduced leading operator. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2} :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

So if the actual carrier doublet is split into opposite \(J\)-parity sectors, then the reduced leading operator already has a distinguished graded structure, and an exact exchange symmetry commuting with \(J\) is even less plausible.

\section{Practical audit theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Executable internal-label audit]
To exclude symmetry protection of the equality \(M_{11}=M_{22}\), it is sufficient to verify one of the following in the actual refined locked carrier basis:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(u_1,u_2\) have opposite eigenvalues under an exact grading/parity/chirality operator \(J\);
\item \(u_1,u_2\) differ in an extra exact conserved microscopic label.
\end{enumerate}

If either holds, then no exact label-preserving exchange involution \(S\) exists, and therefore \(M_{11}=M_{22}\) is not structurally forced.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Case (1) is the theorem above.
Case (2) is the already established general label-obstruction principle: an exact exchange symmetry preserving the full label package would require equality of all exact labels.
Hence either mismatch excludes such an \(S\).
\end{proof}

\section{Honest consequence for the current project}

At the current stage, this theorem does \emph{not} prove that the actual refined locked carrier already has \(\epsilon_1\neq \epsilon_2\).
What it proves is sharper:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{if an internal grading/parity/chirality split is present, then the swap obstruction is exact.}
}
\label{eq:paritysplit_honest}
\end{equation}

Therefore the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now reduced to a still smaller finite fork:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{either verify an actual internal }J\text{-split between }u_1,u_2,
\quad\text{or compute }M_{11}-M_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\label{eq:paritysplit_lastfork}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Let \(J\) be an exact grading/parity/chirality involution on the reduced carrier space, and let
\[
Ju_1=\epsilon_1 u_1,\qquad Ju_2=\epsilon_2 u_2,\qquad \epsilon_i\in\{\pm1\}.
\]
If an exact exchange symmetry \(S\) preserves the full microscopic label package, then in particular
\[
[S,J]=0.
\]
Hence
\[
Su_1=u_2,\qquad Su_2=u_1
\]
implies
\[
\epsilon_1=\epsilon_2.
\]

Therefore, if
\[
\boxed{
\epsilon_1\neq \epsilon_2,
}
\]
then no exact label-preserving exchange symmetry can exist.

Consequently, the equality
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\]
is not symmetry-protected in that case.
So the vanishing
\[
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22})=0
\]
can occur only by accidental fine-tuning, not by exact symmetry.

Thus the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to the finite fork:
\[
\boxed{
\text{either verify an actual internal }J\text{-split between }u_1,u_2,
\quad\text{or compute }M_{11}-M_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\]

\section{Bundle-Index Non-Obstruction Theorem for the Carrier Doublet}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The two carrier states \(u_1,u_2\) form the enriched internal doublet.
But the internal doublet index itself is not an exact conserved label.
It is only a local frame index of the rank-two bundle \(Q\to\mathbb{CP}^2\), and therefore transforms under the local \(U(2)\) frame redundancy.

So the mere fact that \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) are two components of the internal doublet cannot by itself obstruct or enforce an exchange symmetry.
Any true obstruction must come from an additional exact grading/parity/chirality operator \(J\) or from another exact conserved microscopic label.

\section{Rank-two bundle structure}

The internal geometry provides a rank-two Hermitian bundle
\[
Q=(\mathbb C z)^\perp \to \mathbb{CP}^2.
\]
Choose a local orthonormal frame
\[
e=(e_1,e_2),
\qquad
e_a^\dagger e_b=\delta_{ab}.
\]
Then any local section \(s\in \Gamma(Q)\) can be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s=e\,\chi,
\qquad
\chi\in \mathbb C^2.
}
\label{eq:bundle_nonobs_section}
\end{equation}

Under a local frame change
\[
e\mapsto eU(x),
\qquad
U(x)\in U(2),
\]
the coefficient field transforms as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi \mapsto U^{-1}\chi.
}
\label{eq:bundle_nonobs_transform}
\end{equation}
Thus the internal doublet index is a local \(U(2)\)-frame index, not an intrinsic exact label.  :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\section{Main theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Bundle-index non-obstruction theorem]
Let \(u_1,u_2\) be the two basis states of the enriched internal doublet in the local carrier
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]
Assume the internal doublet is realized as the local coefficient space of a \(Q\)-valued mode.

Then the distinction between \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) coming only from the internal-doublet index is not an exact conserved microscopic label.
Consequently, the internal-doublet index alone cannot:

\begin{enumerate}
\item force an exact exchange symmetry \(u_1\leftrightarrow u_2\);
\item exclude such a symmetry;
\item force the equality \(M_{11}=M_{22}\);
\item force the inequality \(M_{11}\neq M_{22}\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:bundle_nonobs_section}--\eqref{eq:bundle_nonobs_transform}, the internal-doublet components are coordinates of a local \(U(2)\)-frame choice.
Changing the local orthonormal frame rotates the pair \((u_1,u_2)\) by an arbitrary \(U(2)\) transformation.
Therefore the label “component \(1\)” versus “component \(2\)” is not invariant under the exact local frame redundancy.

An exact shell-relevant obstruction label must be represented by a commuting microscopic operator with basis-independent eigenvalues.
But the bare internal-doublet index is not of this type; it is gauge/frame dependent.

Hence the internal-doublet index by itself cannot serve as an exact conserved label forcing or forbidding a tangent-doublet exchange symmetry, nor can it by itself force any relation between the diagonal matrix elements \(M_{11}\) and \(M_{22}\).
\end{proof}

\section{Corollary: only a separate grading can obstruct the swap}

\begin{corollary}[Localization of the remaining obstruction]
Inside the actual enriched carrier doublet, the internal bundle index is not the obstruction.
Therefore any exact structural obstruction to a swap symmetry
\[
u_1\leftrightarrow u_2
\]
must come from an additional exact operator beyond the \(Q\)-bundle doublet structure itself, namely:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{an exact grading/parity/chirality operator }J,
\quad\text{or another exact conserved microscopic label.}
}
\label{eq:bundle_nonobs_remaining}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The previous theorem removes the internal-doublet index from the list of exact obstruction labels.
The earlier carrier-internal label localization theorem had already shown that the first three shell-relevant labels coincide automatically.
So the only remaining exact obstruction classes are grading/parity/chirality and any extra exact conserved microscopic labels.
\end{proof}

\section{Interaction with the swap-obstruction theorem}

Recall the exact grading obstruction:
if there exists an exact involution \(J\) such that
\[
Ju_1=\epsilon_1 u_1,\qquad Ju_2=\epsilon_2 u_2,
\qquad \epsilon_1\neq \epsilon_2,
\]
then no exact label-preserving swap symmetry can exist.

Combining that theorem with \eqref{eq:bundle_nonobs_remaining}, we obtain the sharpened conclusion:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the only realistic structural way to force }M_{11}=M_{22}
\text{ is an extra exact microscopic symmetry;}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the only realistic structural way to forbid it is an actual }J\text{-split or another exact label split.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Practical consequence for the longitudinal audit}

The remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is therefore reduced to the finite fork:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{either prove an actual }J\text{-split (or another exact label split) between }u_1,u_2,
}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the axial }JJ\text{-matrix difference }M_{11}-M_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\end{equation}

No additional obstruction can come merely from the existence of the \(Q\)-bundle doublet itself.

\section{Final Summary}

The enriched internal doublet index itself is not an exact shell-relevant obstruction label.

Indeed, if the internal doublet is realized as the local coefficient space of a \(Q\)-valued mode, then any local section has the form
\[
s=e\,\chi,
\qquad
\chi\in\mathbb C^2,
\]
and under a local frame change \(e\mapsto eU(x)\), \(U(x)\in U(2)\), one has
\[
\chi\mapsto U^{-1}\chi.
\]
So the distinction between the two internal components is frame-dependent, not an intrinsic exact conserved label.

Therefore the internal-doublet index alone cannot force or obstruct an exchange symmetry
\[
u_1\leftrightarrow u_2,
\]
nor can it by itself force either
\[
M_{11}=M_{22}
\quad\text{or}\quad
M_{11}\neq M_{22}.
\]

Hence the only remaining exact structural obstructions are:
\[
\boxed{
\text{an exact grading/parity/chirality operator }J,
\quad\text{or another exact conserved microscopic label.}
}
\]

Thus the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to the finite fork:
\[
\boxed{
\text{either prove an actual }J\text{-split (or another exact label split) between }u_1,u_2,
\quad\text{or compute }M_{11}-M_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Non-Derivability Theorem for an Exact \texorpdfstring{$J$}{J}-Grading from the Current Shell-Relevant Structure}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At the present stage, one possible route to close the longitudinal carrier slot would be to find an exact grading/parity/chirality involution \(J\) on the reduced carrier space and show that the leading reduced operator is \(J\)-odd.

We now prove the honest structural statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the current refined locked shell-relevant data do not by themselves determine such an exact }J.
}
\]

So the \(J\)-grading route remains an additional microscopic hypothesis or execution task.
It is not a theorem already forced by the current shell/bundle/little-group structure.

\section{Exact \(J\)-route as a sufficient mechanism}

An exact grading mechanism would require a Hermitian involution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J^\dagger=J,
\qquad
J^2=\mathbf 1,
}
\label{eq:Jroute_Jdef}
\end{equation}
acting on the relevant reduced low-energy sector, together with oddness of the leading operator:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J\mathcal D_1(p)J^{-1}=-\mathcal D_1(p).
}
\label{eq:Jroute_odd}
\end{equation}

Under this condition, the reduced principal operator becomes block-off-diagonal.
This is a valid sufficient route, but the existing notes explicitly state that it has \emph{not} been proved that the actual TECT defect Hessian possesses such a grading \(J\), nor that the actual reduced leading perturbation is \(J\)-odd. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\section{Why the internal doublet does not automatically define \(J\)}

The internal carrier doublet arises from a rank-two complex bundle
\[
Q\to \mathbb{CP}^2.
\]
Any local section may be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s=e\,\chi,
\qquad
\chi\in\mathbb C^2,
}
\label{eq:Jroute_section}
\end{equation}
for a local orthonormal frame \(e=(e_1,e_2)\).
Under a local frame change,
\[
e\mapsto eU(x),
\qquad
U(x)\in U(2),
\]
the coefficients transform as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi\mapsto U^{-1}\chi.
}
\label{eq:Jroute_U2}
\end{equation}

Therefore the raw doublet index is only a local frame coordinate.
It is not itself a basis-independent exact conserved label.
So the existence of the enriched internal doublet does \emph{not} canonically produce an exact involution \(J\) splitting the two internal states into \(\pm\)-sectors. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{Why the ordinary little group does not determine \(J\)}

The shell little groups are
\[
\mathrm{Stab}(+\hat n)\cong C_{2v},
\qquad
\mathrm{Stab}(\{\pm\hat n\})\cong D_{2h},
\]
and both are abelian.
Hence ordinary complex irreducible representations are one-dimensional.
So ordinary little-group representation theory does not force a canonical two-dimensional exchange symmetry or an exact grading on the actual tangent-doublet carrier.
It therefore does not determine a microscopic involution \(J\) on the reduced carrier by itself.

\section{Why a single factorized symmetry does not rescue the construction}

Suppose one tries to build a candidate \(J\) from a single factorized symmetry
\[
\mathcal S=U_{\mathrm{int}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{val}}
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\mathcal S=U_{\mathrm{int}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{val}}\,K.
\]
After the standard reductions, the kinetic sector has the form
\[
\tau^1\otimes (b_0\mathbf 1+b_i\sigma^i).
\]
The factorized-symmetry no-go theorem states that no single such symmetry can kill the scalar
\[
\tau^1\otimes \mathbf 1
\]
while preserving the full kinetic triplet
\[
\tau^1\otimes \sigma^1,\qquad
\tau^1\otimes \sigma^2,\qquad
\tau^1\otimes \sigma^3.
\]
Thus the current structure does not canonically generate the required grading from any single factorized symmetry. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\section{Main theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Non-derivability of an exact \(J\)-grading from current data]
From the currently established refined locked shell-relevant structure alone, namely:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the existence of the enriched internal doublet \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\);
\item the shell-pair valley structure \(\pm G_*\);
\item the ordinary shell little groups \(C_{2v}\) or \(D_{2h}\);
\item the currently available factorized symmetry data;
\end{enumerate}
one cannot derive the existence of an exact grading/parity/chirality involution \(J\) satisfying
\eqref{eq:Jroute_Jdef}--\eqref{eq:Jroute_odd} on the actual reduced carrier sector.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The enriched doublet index is only a local \(U(2)\)-frame coordinate by \eqref{eq:Jroute_section}--\eqref{eq:Jroute_U2}, so it does not by itself define a basis-independent exact grading operator.

The ordinary shell little groups are abelian, so they do not supply a forced two-dimensional exchange or grading structure on the actual carrier sector.

Finally, the factorized-symmetry no-go theorem excludes deriving the desired separation of scalar and full kinetic triplet from a single factorized symmetry.

Therefore none of the currently established structural ingredients suffices to produce the exact involution \(J\) and the oddness condition \(J\mathcal D_1J^{-1}=-\mathcal D_1\).
Hence the existence of such a \(J\) is not derivable from the current shell-relevant structure alone.
\end{proof}

\section{Corollary: the \(J\)-route remains an extra microscopic task}

\begin{corollary}
At the present stage, the \(J\)-grading route is an additional microscopic execution problem, not a closed theorem.
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\text{one must either explicitly construct an exact }J\text{, or else use the direct matrix route.}
}
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the theorem and from the already recorded honest status that the actual TECT defect Hessian has not yet been shown to possess such a grading or \(J\)-odd leading perturbation. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}
\end{proof}

\section{Practical consequence for the longitudinal frontier}

The last carrier-side longitudinal frontier was reduced to the finite test
\[
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22})\neq 0.
\]
Since an exact \(J\)-grading is not presently derivable from the known shell-relevant structure, the only unconditional route left is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the axial pure-}JJ\text{ matrix }M
\text{ and test }M_{11}-M_{22}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Jroute_directM}
\end{equation}

The alternative \(J\)-route remains logically possible, but only after an explicit microscopic construction of \(J\).

\section{Final Summary}

The currently established refined locked shell-relevant structure does not by itself determine an exact grading/parity/chirality involution \(J\) on the actual reduced carrier sector.

The reasons are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the enriched internal doublet index is only a local \(U(2)\)-frame coordinate, not an exact conserved label;
\item the ordinary shell little groups are abelian and do not force a canonical two-dimensional exchange/grading structure;
\item the single factorized-symmetry route is ruled out by the factorized-symmetry no-go theorem.
\end{enumerate}

Moreover, the current notes explicitly state that it has not yet been proved that the actual TECT defect Hessian possesses such a grading \(J\), nor that the actual leading reduced perturbation is \(J\)-odd.

Therefore the \(J\)-grading route remains an extra microscopic task, not a closed theorem.

Hence the only unconditional remaining carrier-side longitudinal route is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute the axial pure-}JJ\text{ matrix }M
\text{ in the actual refined locked basis and test }M_{11}-M_{22}\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{Direct Bloch/Cell-Overlap Formula for the Axial \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} Matrix}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The unconditional remaining route is now direct.

We do not assume any extra exact \(J\)-grading.
Instead, we compute the axial pure-\(JJ\) shell matrix \(M\) directly from the refined locked microscopic Bloch basis.

The result is that the decisive quantity
\[
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22})
\]
is given by one explicit cell-overlap difference of the intervalley projected \(JJ\)-kernel.
So the last carrier-side longitudinal frontier is literally one finite overlap computation.

\section{Folded-Bragg Bloch basis}

Use the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
\]
Let the intervalley Bloch basis be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a^+(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,b}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_b^-(x),
\qquad
a,b=1,2,
}
\label{eq:directM_bloch_basis}
\end{equation}
where \(u_a^\pm(x)\) are periodic cell spinors. The exact intervalley projected Bloch matrix element of any first-order transport input \(V^\mu(x)\) is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu[V])_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,V^\mu(x)\,u_b^-(x).
}
\label{eq:directM_general_overlap}
\end{equation}
This is the exact folded-Bragg overlap formula for the microscopic transport input. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{Pure \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} microscopic kernel}

For the current explicit working branch, the pure \(JJ\)-part of the Class II Schur complement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:directM_JJkernel}
\end{equation}
At shell level this has the universal axial form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
\qquad
M\in\mathrm{Herm}(2),
}
\label{eq:directM_axial_form}
\end{equation}
and the pure \(JJ\)-sector is axial only:
\[
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\propto m_3,
\qquad
\alpha^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=\beta^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0.
\]
So this sector probes only the longitudinal shell singlet. 

\section{Definition of the axial overlap matrix}

Contract \eqref{eq:directM_general_overlap} with the shell axis \(\hat n_\mu\) and choose the transport input \(V^\mu=\hat n^\mu K_\mu^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\).
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{ab}
:=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,
\bigl(\hat n^i K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}(x)\bigr)\,
u_b^-(x).
}
\label{eq:directM_MJJ_def}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:directM_axial_form},
\[
\hat n^i K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=-\Gamma_J M,
\]
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}=-\Gamma_J\,M.
}
\label{eq:directM_MJJ_vs_M}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M
=
-\frac{1}{\Gamma_J}\,\mathcal M^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:directM_M_from_overlap}
\end{equation}

Thus the axial \(2\times2\) shell matrix \(M\) is nothing but the intervalley Bloch/cell overlap matrix of the pure \(JJ\)-kernel.

\section{Diagonal asymmetry formula}

Write
\[
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
M_{11}&M_{12}\\
\overline{M_{12}}&M_{22}
\end{pmatrix}
=
m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}).
}
\label{eq:directM_m3diag}
\end{equation}
By \eqref{eq:directM_M_from_overlap},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{1}{2\Gamma_J}
\Bigl(
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{11}-\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{22}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:directM_m3_overlap}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:directM_MJJ_def},
\begin{align}
m_3
=
-\frac{1}{2\Gamma_J}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}
\Big(
\overline{u_1^+(x)}\,\hat n^i K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}(x)\,u_1^-(x)
-
\overline{u_2^+(x)}\,\hat n^i K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}(x)\,u_2^-(x)
\Big).
\label{eq:directM_m3_final}
\end{align}

This is the decisive direct formula.

\section{Equivalent microscopic kernel form}

Insert \eqref{eq:directM_JJkernel} into \eqref{eq:directM_m3_final}. Then
\begin{align}
m_3
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{2\Gamma_J M_X^2}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}
\Big(
&\overline{u_1^+}\,
\hat n^i
\Pi_{S_*}
\big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}
u_1^-
\nonumber\\
-
&\overline{u_2^+}\,
\hat n^i
\Pi_{S_*}
\big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}
u_2^-
\Big).
\label{eq:directM_m3_kernel}
\end{align}

Thus the last longitudinal audit is a finite difference of two explicit intervalley cell overlaps of the same projected \(JJ\)-kernel.

\section{Longitudinal consequence}

The shell dictionary gives
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\]
with the longitudinal piece remaining in the \(c_\parallel\)-channel. 
Inside the current source classification, the principal longitudinal source is localized to the pure \(JJ\)-sector, so
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\]
provided \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\), which is already explicit in the working branch. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Therefore the actual longitudinal carrier slot closes if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{11}\neq \mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{22}.
}
\label{eq:directM_closure_cond}
\end{equation}

\section{Practical theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Direct matrix-route formula for the last longitudinal frontier]
In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is exactly the finite overlap test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{11}\neq \mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{22},
}
\label{eq:directM_theorem_cond}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,
\bigl(\hat n^i K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}(x)\bigr)\,
u_b^-(x).
\label{eq:directM_theorem_overlap}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:directM_theorem_cond} holds, then
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
So the honest remaining carrier-side longitudinal slot is closed.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:directM_M_from_overlap} expresses the axial \(2\times2\) matrix \(M\) directly in terms of the intervalley Bloch/cell overlap of the pure \(JJ\)-kernel. Equation \eqref{eq:directM_m3_overlap} then shows that \(m_3\) is exactly proportional to the diagonal difference \(\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{11}-\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{22}\). If that difference is nonzero, then \(m_3\neq 0\). Since the pure \(JJ\)-sector is the principal longitudinal source, this gives \(\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0\), and hence \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\) through the already-fixed odd radial overlap factor \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\).
\end{proof}

\section{What is actually left}

After the present theorem, there is no remaining structural ambiguity on the carrier side.

The only remaining work is the explicit finite evaluation of the overlap difference
\[
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{11}-\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{22}
\]
in the true refined locked microscopic Bloch basis.

This is a genuine finite symbolic or numerical calculation.

\section{Final Summary}

The last remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now reduced to a single explicit intervalley Bloch/cell overlap difference.

The exact axial pure-\(JJ\) matrix is obtained from
\[
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,
\bigl(\hat n^i K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}(x)\bigr)\,
u_b^-(x),
\qquad
a,b=1,2.
\]

Since
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
\]
one has

M=-\frac{1}{\Gamma_J}\mathcal M^{(JJ)},
\qquad
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22})
=
-\frac{1}{2\Gamma_J}

Therefore the decisive finite test is

If this holds, then

\Longrightarrow

So there is no remaining structural ambiguity on the carrier side.
Only the explicit finite overlap evaluation in the true refined locked microscopic Bloch basis remains.

\section{Finite Harmonic-Sum Formula for the Last Longitudinal Audit}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The decisive quantity
\[
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22})
\]
has already been reduced to the intervalley Bloch/cell overlap of the axial pure-\(JJ\) kernel.

We now push this one step further:
expand the periodic Bloch spinors in a truncated reciprocal-harmonic basis and convert the cell integral into an explicit finite Fourier-convolution sum.

This is the final reduction from “carrier-side longitudinal frontier” to an actual computable matrix sum.

\section{Periodic harmonic expansion}

At the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|,
\]
write the intervalley Bloch basis as
\[
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{+ik_*\cdot x}u_a^+(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,b}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_b^-(x),
\qquad
a,b=1,2,
\]
with \(u_a^\pm(x)\) periodic on the primitive cell. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Choose a finite reciprocal-harmonic truncation
\[
\mathcal S_N\subset \Lambda^*
\]
and expand
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_a^+(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N} c_{a,G}^{(+)}\,e^{iG\cdot x},
\qquad
u_b^-(x)=\sum_{G'\in\mathcal S_N} c_{b,G'}^{(-)}\,e^{iG'\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:finite_sum_u_expand}
\end{equation}

Likewise expand the axial pure-\(JJ\) transport input
\[
V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(x):=\hat n^i K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}(x)
\]
in primitive-cell Fourier modes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(x)=\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(Q)\,e^{iQ\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:finite_sum_V_expand}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact finite convolution formula}

Recall the exact intervalley overlap
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,
V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(x)\,
u_b^-(x).
\label{eq:finite_sum_overlap_start}
\end{equation}

Insert \eqref{eq:finite_sum_u_expand} and \eqref{eq:finite_sum_V_expand}:
\begin{align}
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{ab}
&=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}
\left(
\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N}\overline{c_{a,G}^{(+)}}\,e^{-iG\cdot x}
\right)
\left(
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x}
\right)
\left(
\sum_{G'\in\mathcal S_N}c_{b,G'}^{(-)}e^{iG'\cdot x}
\right)
\nonumber\\
&=
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}
\overline{c_{a,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{b,G'}^{(-)}
\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(Q)
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{i(Q-G_* -G+G')\cdot x}.
\label{eq:finite_sum_inserted}
\end{align}

By primitive-cell orthogonality,
\[
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;e^{iK\cdot x}
=
|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|\;\delta_{K,0}
\qquad
(K\in\Lambda^*),
\]
hence only the harmonic
\[
Q=G_*+G-G'
\]
survives. Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{(JJ,N)}_{ab}
=
|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{a,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{b,G'}^{(-)}
\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*+G-G').
}
\label{eq:finite_sum_main}
\end{equation}

This is the exact truncated harmonic-sum formula.

\section{Selection-rule interpretation}

Equation \eqref{eq:finite_sum_main} is precisely the harmonic bookkeeping rule:
the intervalley shell-pair channel only sees Fourier modes satisfying
\[
Q=G_*+G-G'.
\]
This is the same discrete convolution structure already established for the Bloch-harmonic shell--mediator coupling matrix. 

In particular, if the truncated Bloch frame is minimal enough that the dominant shell weights are concentrated on a single pair of harmonics \(G=G'=0\), then \eqref{eq:finite_sum_main} compresses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{(JJ,N)}_{ab}
\approx
|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|\,
\overline{c_{a,0}^{(+)}}
\,c_{b,0}^{(-)}
\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*).
}
\label{eq:finite_sum_singleharm}
\end{equation}
So in the minimal shell-pair dominant approximation the decisive longitudinal audit is controlled by the single \(Q=G_*\) Fourier mode. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\section{Diagonal difference formula}

The axial shell matrix \(M\) was defined by
\[
V_\parallel^{(JJ)}=-\Gamma_J\,M,
\qquad
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
M=-\frac{1}{\Gamma_J}\mathcal M^{(JJ)},
\]
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{1}{2\Gamma_J}
\left(
\mathcal M^{(JJ,N)}_{11}
-
\mathcal M^{(JJ,N)}_{22}
\right).
}
\label{eq:finite_sum_m3}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:finite_sum_main},
\begin{align}
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\Big(
&\overline{c_{1,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{1,G'}^{(-)}
-
\overline{c_{2,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{2,G'}^{(-)}
\Big)
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*+G-G').
\label{eq:finite_sum_m3_explicit}
\end{align}

This is the final explicit finite harmonic formula for the carrier-side longitudinal audit.

\section{Practical theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Final finite-sum longitudinal audit]
Fix a truncated reciprocal-harmonic set \(\mathcal S_N\), the periodic intervalley Bloch coefficients \(c_{a,G}^{(\pm)}\), and the pure-\(JJ\) axial Fourier coefficients \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(Q)\).

Then the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is exactly the finite sum
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\Big(
\overline{c_{1,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{1,G'}^{(-)}
-
\overline{c_{2,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{2,G'}^{(-)}
\Big)
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*+G-G').
}
\label{eq:finite_sum_theorem}
\end{equation}

If this quantity is nonzero, then
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
So the honest remaining carrier-side longitudinal slot is closed.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The finite convolution formula \eqref{eq:finite_sum_main} follows from the Bloch-harmonic expansions and primitive-cell orthogonality.
The diagonal difference \eqref{eq:finite_sum_m3} is just the Pauli \(\sigma_3\)-component of the axial \(2\times2\) Hermitian shell matrix.
Therefore nonvanishing of the sum implies nonvanishing of \(m_3\), and hence of the principal longitudinal coefficient.
\end{proof}

\section{Computational algorithm}

The final execution is now completely explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item choose a truncated harmonic set \(\mathcal S_N\);
\item compute the Bloch coefficients \(c_{a,G}^{(\pm)}\) of the actual refined locked shell basis;
\item compute the pure-\(JJ\) axial Fourier coefficients \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(Q)\);
\item evaluate the finite sum \eqref{eq:finite_sum_theorem};
\item test whether it is nonzero.
\end{enumerate}

So the carrier-side longitudinal problem is no longer conceptual, structural, or representation-theoretic.
It is a finite Fourier bookkeeping calculation.

\section{Final Summary}

The remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now reduced to one explicit finite harmonic sum.

Using the periodic Bloch expansions
\[
u_a^\pm(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N} c_{a,G}^{(\pm)}e^{iG\cdot x},
\]
and the Fourier expansion
\[
V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(x)=\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
the intervalley axial overlap matrix becomes
\[
\mathcal M^{(JJ,N)}_{ab}
=
|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{a,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{b,G'}^{(-)}
\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*+G-G').
\]

Therefore the longitudinal Pauli coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\Big(
\overline{c_{1,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{1,G'}^{(-)}
-
\overline{c_{2,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{2,G'}^{(-)}
\Big)
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*+G-G').
}
\]

If this finite sum is nonzero, then
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

So there is no remaining structural ambiguity on the carrier side.
The last remaining task is the explicit symbolic or numerical evaluation of this finite Fourier sum in the actual refined locked Bloch basis.
