\section{First-Shell Dominant Compression of the Final Longitudinal Sum}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The exact finite harmonic formula for the longitudinal audit has already been obtained:
\[
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\Big(
\overline{c_{1,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{1,G'}^{(-)}
-
\overline{c_{2,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{2,G'}^{(-)}
\Big)
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*+G-G').
\]

We now compress this formula under the natural first-shell dominant assumption.
The result is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a leading one-mode term controlled by the single Fourier coefficient \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\);
\item an explicit remainder coming from all nonzero reciprocal harmonics;
\item a practical sufficient condition guaranteeing \(m_3\neq 0\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Exact finite-sum formula}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\Delta_{GG'}\,
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*+G-G'),
}
\label{eq:fsd_exact}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{GG'}
:=
\overline{c_{1,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{1,G'}^{(-)}
-
\overline{c_{2,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{2,G'}^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:fsd_Delta}
\end{equation}

\section{First-shell dominant decomposition}

Assume the reciprocal-harmonic truncation is split as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_N=\{0\}\cup \mathcal S_N',
\qquad
0\notin \mathcal S_N'.
}
\label{eq:fsd_split}
\end{equation}

Write the zero-harmonic Bloch amplitudes as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_a^{(+)}:=c_{a,0}^{(+)},
\qquad
A_a^{(-)}:=c_{a,0}^{(-)},
\qquad
a=1,2,
}
\label{eq:fsd_Adef}
\end{equation}
and the nonzero-harmonic tails as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{a,G}^{(+)}:=c_{a,G}^{(+)},
\qquad
r_{a,G}^{(-)}:=c_{a,G}^{(-)},
\qquad
G\in\mathcal S_N'.
}
\label{eq:fsd_rdef}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
\]

Decompose the exact sum \eqref{eq:fsd_exact} into the leading \((0,0)\)-term and the remainder:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Big(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Big),
}
\label{eq:fsd_main_plus_rem}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_N
:=
\sum_{(G,G')\neq(0,0)}
\Delta_{GG'}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*+G-G').
}
\label{eq:fsd_RN}
\end{equation}

\section{One-mode dominant approximation}

The single-mode or first-shell dominant approximation is obtained by dropping the remainder \(R_N\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3^{(0)}
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Big(
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}
\Big)
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*).
}
\label{eq:fsd_singlemode}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal explicit computational form of the longitudinal audit.

\section{Exact sufficient condition for nonvanishing}

The previous formula immediately yields:

\begin{theorem}[Exact dominant-mode sufficiency]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Big|
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\Big|
>
|R_N|,
}
\label{eq:fsd_exact_suff}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:fsd_nonzero}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\[
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:fsd_main_plus_rem} shows that \(m_3\) is proportional to
\[
\Delta_{00}\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)+R_N.
\]
If the leading term dominates the remainder strictly in modulus, then the sum cannot vanish.
Hence \(m_3\neq 0\).
The longitudinal implication follows from the already established chain
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{proof}

\section{Remainder bound in terms of tail amplitudes}

Define the nonzero-harmonic \(\ell^1\)-tails
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_a^{(+)}
:=
\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N'}|r_{a,G}^{(+)}|,
\qquad
\varepsilon_a^{(-)}
:=
\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N'}|r_{a,G}^{(-)}|.
}
\label{eq:fsd_eps}
\end{equation}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_*^{(N)}
:=
\sup_{Q\in G_*+\mathcal S_N-\mathcal S_N}
\left|
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(Q)
\right|.
}
\label{eq:fsd_Vstar}
\end{equation}

Then the remainder satisfies
\begin{align}
|R_N|
\le
V_*^{(N)}
\Big(
&|A_1^{(+)}|\varepsilon_1^{(-)}
+\varepsilon_1^{(+)}|A_1^{(-)}|
+\varepsilon_1^{(+)}\varepsilon_1^{(-)}
\nonumber\\
&+
|A_2^{(+)}|\varepsilon_2^{(-)}
+\varepsilon_2^{(+)}|A_2^{(-)}|
+\varepsilon_2^{(+)}\varepsilon_2^{(-)}
\Big).
\label{eq:fsd_Rbound}
\end{align}

\begin{proof}
Split the sum defining \(R_N\) into the three disjoint cases:
\[
G=0,\ G'\neq 0;
\qquad
G\neq 0,\ G'=0;
\qquad
G\neq 0,\ G'\neq 0.
\]
Take absolute values termwise, bound every Fourier coefficient by \(V_*^{(N)}\), and sum the resulting products of zero-mode and tail amplitudes.
\end{proof}

\section{Practical first-shell sufficient condition}

Combining \eqref{eq:fsd_exact_suff} and \eqref{eq:fsd_Rbound}, we obtain the purely explicit sufficient condition
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\left|
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}
\right|
\cdot
\left|
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\right|
}
\nonumber\\
\boxed{
>
V_*^{(N)}
\Big(
|A_1^{(+)}|\varepsilon_1^{(-)}
+\varepsilon_1^{(+)}|A_1^{(-)}|
+\varepsilon_1^{(+)}\varepsilon_1^{(-)}
+
|A_2^{(+)}|\varepsilon_2^{(-)}
+\varepsilon_2^{(+)}|A_2^{(-)}|
+\varepsilon_2^{(+)}\varepsilon_2^{(-)}
\Big).
}
\label{eq:fsd_practical_suff}
\end{align}
If \eqref{eq:fsd_practical_suff} holds, then \(m_3\neq 0\), hence \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\).

\section{Ultra-minimal criterion}

In the ultra-minimal approximation where nonzero harmonics are neglected altogether,
\[
\varepsilon_a^{(\pm)}=0,
\]
and the longitudinal audit collapses to the one-line test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Big(
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}
\Big)
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:fsd_ultramin}
\end{equation}

Thus the carrier-side longitudinal slot closes already if both:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}
\neq 0
}
\label{eq:fsd_ampdiff}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:fsd_VGstar}
\end{equation}

\section{What this means physically}

The first factor in \eqref{eq:fsd_ampdiff} measures the asymmetry of the two carrier channels in their dominant intervalley Bloch weights.
The second factor \eqref{eq:fsd_VGstar} is the actual pure-\(JJ\) axial shell-harmonic coefficient at the selected intervalley momentum.

So the last honest carrier-side frontier has been split into two explicit microscopic ingredients:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) carrier Bloch-weight asymmetry}
\qquad+\qquad
\text{(ii) nonzero axial }JJ\text{ shell harmonic at }G_*.
}
\label{eq:fsd_physicalsplit}
\end{equation}

\section{Final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Minimal computational form of the longitudinal frontier]
In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to the dominant-mode expression
\[
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Big(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Big),
\]
with
\[
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
\]

Therefore a sufficient finite condition for longitudinal survival is
\[
\Big|
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\Big|>|R_N|.
\]
In particular, in the ultra-minimal truncation it is enough to show
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\section{Final Summary}

Under first-shell dominant truncation, the last carrier-side longitudinal frontier takes the compressed form
\[
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Big(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Big),
\]
where
\[
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
\]

Thus the dominant-mode sufficient condition is
\[
\Big|
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\Big|>|R_N|.
\]

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), so it is enough to verify
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\]

If these hold, then
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

So the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now reduced to two explicit finite microscopic ingredients:
carrier Bloch-weight asymmetry and nonzero axial \(JJ\) shell harmonic at \(G_*\).

\section{Single-Harmonic Sufficiency Theorem for \texorpdfstring{$\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)$}{Vhat parallel JJ(G*)}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier has already been reduced to the dominant-mode quantity
\[
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Big(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Big).
\]
So the second genuinely microscopic ingredient is the shell Fourier coefficient
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*).
\]

We now prove that this coefficient is nonzero as soon as the single intervalley \(Q=G_*\) harmonic of the axial \(J\)-current survives the projected \(JJ\)-kernel without an exact cancellation.

Thus the problem is reduced to a single shell-harmonic noncancellation test.

\section{Exact single-harmonic control of the intervalley channel}

For the folded shell pair \(\pm G_*\), the exact Bloch selection rule reduces the intervalley coupling to the single Fourier mode
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q=G_*.
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_singleQ}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the intervalley block is controlled only by the \(G_*\)-harmonic coefficient of the periodic background kernel. This is the exact folded-Bragg selection rule. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Therefore every projected shell witness coefficient in the intervalley channel is obtained from the \(Q=G_*\) Fourier coefficient of the corresponding microscopic source.

\section{Pure \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} kernel and axial contraction}

The pure \(JJ\)-contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_kernel}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit harmonic matrix of \(\mathcal J(k)\), one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{k_j}\mathcal J_i^a\propto \delta_{ij}.
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_dJdelta}
\end{equation}
Hence the pure \(JJ\)-kernel is axial and shell-normal:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_axial}
\end{equation}
with \(M\in\mathrm{Herm}(2)\). The shell-relevant longitudinal coefficient is therefore extracted by the shell-normal contraction
\[
\hat n^iK_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}.
\]
This is exactly the longitudinal-only role of the pure \(JJ\)-sector. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\section{Definition of the shell harmonic}

Define the axial pure-\(JJ\) shell harmonic coefficient by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
:=
\widehat{\bigl(\hat n^iK_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\bigr)}(G_*).
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_def}
\end{equation}
By the single-harmonic rule \eqref{eq:VhatJJ_singleQ}, this is the only Fourier coefficient entering the dominant intervalley longitudinal audit.

\section{Noncancellation criterion}

Write the \(Q=G_*\) Fourier coefficient of the axial \(J\)-kernel symbolically as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_AJJ}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
:=
\widehat{
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
\hat n^i(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\hat n^i\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}
}(G_*).
\label{eq:VhatJJ_AJJdef}
\end{equation}

The only ways this can vanish are:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\alpha_X=0\);
\item the projected \(G_*\)-harmonic of the axial \(JJ\)-kernel vanishes identically by an exact symmetry;
\item a nontrivial cancellation occurs among the \(G_*\)-harmonic matrix elements.
\end{enumerate}

Thus we obtain:

\begin{theorem}[Single-harmonic sufficiency]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\alpha_X\neq 0\);
\item the selected shell-pair \(G_*\)-harmonic of the projected axial \(JJ\)-kernel is present,
\[
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0;
\]
\item there is no exact microscopic symmetry forcing the projected \(G_*\)-harmonic axial \(JJ\)-kernel to vanish.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_nonzero}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:VhatJJ_AJJ},
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*).
\]
Since \(M_X^2>0\) and \(\alpha_X\neq 0\), the prefactor is nonzero.
Therefore \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\) vanishes if and only if \(\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\) vanishes.
Under the assumptions, \(\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0\), so \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0\).
\end{proof}

\section{Minimal first-shell dominant consequence}

In the ultra-minimal first-shell dominant approximation, the longitudinal audit had already reduced to
\[
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Big(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Big).
\]
Therefore if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
|\Delta_{00}\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)|>|R_N|,
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_final_suff}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_m3nonzero}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section{Ultra-minimal one-line criterion}

If the nonzero-harmonic remainder is neglected,
\[
R_N=0,
\]
then the longitudinal carrier slot closes already if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_ultramin}
\end{equation}

So the remaining microscopic content is sharply split into:
\begin{enumerate}
\item carrier Bloch-weight asymmetry \(\Delta_{00}\);
\item nonvanishing axial \(JJ\) shell harmonic at \(G_*\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{What is actually left}

After this theorem, the second microscopic ingredient is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit evaluation of the projected \(G_*\)-harmonic
\[
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*),
\]
or equivalently \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\).

So the last honest carrier-side frontier is now exactly the pair of finite checks:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:VhatJJ_last_pair}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal shell harmonic is controlled by the single intervalley Fourier mode \(Q=G_*\).

Define
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
=
\widehat{\bigl(\hat n^iK_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\bigr)}(G_*).
\]
Then the pure-\(JJ\) kernel gives
\[
\boxed{
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*),
}
\]
where \(\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\) is the projected axial \(G_*\)-harmonic of the \(JJ\)-kernel.

Hence, if
\[
\alpha_X\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
\]

Combined with the first-shell dominant longitudinal formula
\[
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Big(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Big),
\]
this yields the sufficient condition
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
|\Delta_{00}\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)|>|R_N|.
}
\]
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to show
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\]

So the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now reduced to two explicit finite microscopic ingredients:
Bloch-weight asymmetry and the nonvanishing axial \(JJ\) harmonic at the selected shell pair.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{First-Shell Noncancellation Lemma for the Axial \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} Harmonic}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The last carrier-side longitudinal frontier was reduced to the two finite microscopic ingredients
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0.
\]

We now prove a practical sufficient condition for the second one.

If the axial projected \(JJ\)-coefficient field belongs to the lowest-derivative local class,
\[
\mathcal A^{(JJ)}_j(x)=\sum_m C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x),
\]
then its \(G_*\)-harmonic is explicitly
\[
\widehat{\mathcal A}^{(JJ)}_j(G_*)
=
i(C^{(JJ)}G_*)_j\,A_{G_*}.
\]
Hence the shell-normal longitudinal coefficient is nonzero whenever
\[
A_{G_*}\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*\neq 0.
\]

So the second microscopic ingredient is reduced to one finite tensor contraction.

\section{Lowest-derivative first-shell support theorem}

Let \(\phi_0(x)\) be the first-shell BCC condensate and consider a coefficient field linear in the first derivatives of \(\phi_0\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_j(x)=\sum_m C_{jm}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x).
}
\label{eq:AJJ_Tj}
\end{equation}
Then its Fourier support stays in the first shell and the shell coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal T_j}(G_*)
=
i\Bigl(\sum_m C_{jm}G_{*,m}\Bigr)A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:AJJ_firstshell_support}
\end{equation}
This is the exact first-shell support theorem for linear derivative couplings. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\section{Axial \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} specialization}

Assume the projected axial pure-\(JJ\) coefficient field lies in this lowest-derivative local class:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal A^{(JJ)}_j(x)
=
\sum_m C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x),
}
\label{eq:AJJ_lowest}
\end{equation}
for some real coefficient tensor \(C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\).

Then by \eqref{eq:AJJ_firstshell_support},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}^{(JJ)}_j(G_*)
=
i\,(C^{(JJ)}G_*)_j\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:AJJ_Gstar_vector}
\end{equation}

Now contract with the shell axis \(\hat n=G_*/|G_*|\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
:=
\hat n^j\,\widehat{\mathcal A}^{(JJ)}_j(G_*)
=
i\,(\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*)\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:AJJ_Gstar_scalar}
\end{equation}

This is the decisive explicit formula.

\section{Single-harmonic noncancellation lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Practical noncancellation of the axial \(JJ\) harmonic]
Under the lowest-derivative local realization \eqref{eq:AJJ_lowest}, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:AJJ_nonzero_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:AJJ_nonzero_concl}
\end{equation}
Consequently, if also \(\alpha_X\neq 0\), then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:AJJ_Vhat_nonzero}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:AJJ_Gstar_scalar} gives
\[
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
=
i\,(\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*)\,A_{G_*}.
\]
So if both factors on the right-hand side are nonzero, then \(\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0\).

Now recall
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*).
\]
Since \(M_X^2>0\) and \(\alpha_X\neq 0\), the prefactor is nonzero.
Therefore \(\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0\) implies \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0\).
\end{proof}

\section{Ultra-minimal longitudinal closure}

In the first-shell dominant ultra-minimal truncation, we had
\begin{equation}
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Big(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Big).
\label{eq:AJJ_m3_main}
\end{equation}
If \(R_N=0\), then the previous lemma yields:

\begin{theorem}[Ultra-minimal longitudinal sufficiency]
Assume:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0,
\qquad
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:AJJ_ultramin_assump}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:AJJ_ultramin_concl}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the noncancellation lemma, assumptions \eqref{eq:AJJ_ultramin_assump} imply
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
\]
Since also \(\Delta_{00}\neq 0\), the leading term in \eqref{eq:AJJ_m3_main} is nonzero.
With \(R_N=0\), it follows that \(m_3\neq 0\).
The final implication to \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\) is the already established longitudinal chain.
\end{proof}

\section{Remainder-stable version}

If \(R_N\neq 0\), the same reasoning gives the sufficient inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}|\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
|A_{G_*}|\,
|\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*|
>
|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:AJJ_remainder_stable}
\end{equation}
Under \eqref{eq:AJJ_remainder_stable}, the exact \(m_3\) is still nonzero.

\section{What is now actually left}

This theorem does \emph{not} prove that the actual refined locked microscopic \(JJ\)-kernel is already of the form \eqref{eq:AJJ_lowest}.
It proves that if the actual chosen branch realizes the lowest-derivative local \(JJ\)-class, then the second microscopic ingredient is reduced to the single contraction
\[
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*.
\]

So the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now split into two concrete subcases:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Lowest-derivative local \(JJ\)-route:}
check whether the coefficient tensor \(C^{(JJ)}\) satisfies
\[
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*\neq 0;
\]

\item \textbf{General refined locked route:}
evaluate \(\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\) directly from the projected \(JJ\)-kernel Fourier coefficient.
\end{enumerate}

In either case, the problem is finite and explicit.

\section{Final Summary}

Assume the projected axial pure-\(JJ\) coefficient field belongs to the lowest-derivative local class
\[
\mathcal A^{(JJ)}_j(x)=\sum_m C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x).
\]
Then the exact first-shell support theorem gives
\[
\widehat{\mathcal A}^{(JJ)}_j(G_*)
=
i(C^{(JJ)}G_*)_j\,A_{G_*}.
\]
Contracting with the shell axis,
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
=
i(\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*)\,A_{G_*}.
}
\]

Therefore, if
\[
A_{G_*}\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0.
\]
If also \(\alpha_X\neq 0\), then
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
\]

In the ultra-minimal first-shell dominant truncation, together with
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\]
this yields
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

So, in the lowest-derivative local \(JJ\)-route, the second microscopic ingredient is reduced to a single tensor contraction:
\[
\boxed{
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*\neq 0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Lowest-Derivative Locality Theorem for the Pure \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} Axial Coefficient}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The previous noncancellation lemma assumed that the projected axial pure-\(JJ\) coefficient field belongs to the lowest-derivative local class
\[
\mathcal A_j^{(JJ)}(x)=\sum_m C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x).
\]

We now prove that this assumption is exactly satisfied in the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch at principal shell order.

So the single-contraction formula
\[
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
=
i(\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*)A_{G_*}
\]
is not an extra ansatz here.
It is the actual leading microscopic form of the pure \(JJ\)-route.

\section{Minimal Class II background current}

In the minimal Class II UV extension, the background current is chosen as the most general lowest-order local form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\phi_0,P_0]
=
m^a(P_0)\,\partial_i\phi_0,
}
\label{eq:JJlocal_Jcurrent}
\end{equation}
where \(m^a(P_0)\) is a constant internal vector determined by the locked background projector \(P_0\). :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Thus the background \(J\)-current is already linear in the first derivative of the condensate field.

\section{Refined locked expansion}

Write the refined locked background as
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
\label{eq:JJlocal_background}
\end{equation}
and expand
\begin{equation}
\Psi=(\phi_0+\sigma)z_0+\psi,
\qquad
P=P_0+\delta P.
\label{eq:JJlocal_expand}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_i\Psi
=
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,z_0
+
\partial_i\psi
+
(\partial_i\sigma)\,z_0+\cdots,
\label{eq:JJlocal_dPsi}
\end{equation}
while \(P_0\) is locked and constant.
Therefore the shell-relevant \(J\)-sector is sourced linearly by the shell gradient \(\partial_i\phi_0\).  :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

This is exactly the required lowest-derivative shell carrier structure.

\section{Linearized \texorpdfstring{$J$}{J} block and shell tangent restriction}

At the level of the first variation, the load-bearing graded principal terms are those linear in the fluctuation and containing exactly one worldvolume derivative. In normal form,
\begin{equation}
J_i^{a(1)}[\eta]
=
\mathcal J_i^{a(0)}(\xi)\,\eta
+
\mathcal J_i^{a\mu}(\xi)\,(-i\partial_{y^\mu})\eta
+\cdots.
\label{eq:JJlocal_normal}
\end{equation}
The principal mediated transport term comes from the background-linear cross term
\[
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{bg}}^a\,\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a,
\]
so the relevant shell-reduced symbol is linear in the background \(J\)-current and linear in the first derivative of the test sector. 

Because the background \(J\)-current itself is already proportional to \(\partial_i\phi_0\), the resulting projected pure-\(JJ\) coefficient field remains in the lowest-derivative local class.

\section{Bloch-derivative confirmation}

The exact Bloch derivative of the \(J\)-block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{k_j}\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{G';\,G,r}
=
iA\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,\delta_{ij}\,\bigl(t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a\bigr).
}
\label{eq:JJlocal_dJdk}
\end{equation}
Thus the explicit \(k\)-derivative acts only through a Kronecker \(\delta_{ij}\), with no additional higher-derivative spatial tensor structure at principal shell order. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Near the folded Bragg point,
\begin{equation}
|+\!,\alpha\rangle\equiv |G=0,\alpha\rangle,
\qquad
|-\!,\alpha\rangle\equiv |G=-G_*,\alpha\rangle,
\end{equation}
and the intervalley matrix element is nonzero only if
\begin{equation}
0=(-G_*)+Q
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
Q=G_*.
\label{eq:JJlocal_Bragg}
\end{equation}
So the pure-\(JJ\) shell audit is controlled by a single first-shell harmonic. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\section{Main theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Pure-\(JJ\) lowest-derivative locality in the current working branch]
In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the projected axial pure-\(JJ\) coefficient field belongs to the lowest-derivative local class at principal shell order:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal A_j^{(JJ)}(x)
=
\sum_m C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x),
}
\label{eq:JJlocal_main}
\end{equation}
for a constant tensor \(C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\) determined by the internal couplings \(m^a(P_0)\), the tangent-shell matrix elements \(t_{\alpha0}^a\), and the shell projection data.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:JJlocal_Jcurrent}, the background \(J\)-current is linear in \(\partial_i\phi_0\).
By the refined locked expansion \eqref{eq:JJlocal_background}--\eqref{eq:JJlocal_dPsi}, the shell-relevant current carrier structure is still built on that same shell gradient.
By the normal-form and mediator cross-term analysis, the principal pure-\(JJ\) contribution is linear in the background \(J\)-current and linear in the first fluctuation derivative, so no extra powers of \(\phi_0\) or additional background derivatives are introduced at principal shell order.
Finally, the explicit Bloch-derivative formula \eqref{eq:JJlocal_dJdk} shows that the shell derivative contributes only the tensor \(\delta_{ij}\), while the Bragg condition \eqref{eq:JJlocal_Bragg} restricts the Fourier support to the single first-shell harmonic \(Q=G_*\).

Therefore the resulting projected axial coefficient field is still linear in the first derivative of \(\phi_0\), hence of the form \eqref{eq:JJlocal_main}.
\end{proof}

\section{Immediate Fourier consequence}

Since \eqref{eq:JJlocal_main} is exactly the hypothesis of the first-shell support theorem for linear derivative couplings, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}^{(JJ)}_j(G_*)
=
i(C^{(JJ)}G_*)_j\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:JJlocal_firstshell}
\end{equation}
Contracting with the shell axis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
=
i(\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*)\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:JJlocal_scalar}
\end{equation}

Thus, in the current working branch, the pure-\(JJ\) axial shell harmonic is controlled by a single tensor contraction.

\section{Practical corollary}

\begin{corollary}[Working-branch longitudinal sufficiency]
In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}\neq 0,
\qquad
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:JJlocal_practical}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:JJlocal_practical_concl}
\end{equation}
Combined with the first-shell dominant carrier asymmetry condition
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\]
this yields
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:JJlocal_scalar} gives \(\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0\) under the first two conditions.
The nonzero mediator prefactor \(\alpha_X\neq 0\) then implies \(\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0\).
The final implication follows from the already established first-shell dominant longitudinal audit.
\end{proof}

\section{Honest status}

What is proved here is the structural locality reduction:
the actual current working branch really does place the pure-\(JJ\) axial coefficient field in the lowest-derivative local class.

What is not yet inserted explicitly is the numerical/symbolic value of the contraction
\[
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*.
\]
So the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute } \hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*
\quad\text{and}\quad
\Delta_{00}.
}
\label{eq:JJlocal_last}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the projected axial pure-\(JJ\) coefficient field belongs to the lowest-derivative local class:
\[
\mathcal A_j^{(JJ)}(x)=\sum_m C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x).
\]

This follows because:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal Class II background current is \(J_i^a=m^a(P_0)\partial_i\phi_0\);
\item the refined locked expansion keeps the shell-relevant \(J\)-sector linear in the shell gradient;
\item the Bloch derivative contributes only \(\delta_{ij}\), and the folded Bragg condition keeps only the single harmonic \(Q=G_*\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the first-shell support theorem applies directly, giving
\[
\widehat{\mathcal A}^{(JJ)}_j(G_*)=i(C^{(JJ)}G_*)_jA_{G_*},
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)=i(\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*)A_{G_*}.
\]

Hence, in the current working branch, a sufficient condition for longitudinal survival is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0,
\qquad
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0.
}
\]

Under these conditions,
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
m_3\neq 0,
\qquad
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

So the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced completely to two explicit finite contractions:
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*.
\]

\section{Reduction of \texorpdfstring{$C^{(JJ)}_{jm}$}{C(JJ)jm} to a Single Internal Contraction}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The pure-\(JJ\) axial coefficient field has already been shown to lie in the lowest-derivative local class:
\[
\mathcal A^{(JJ)}_j(x)=\sum_m C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x).
\]

We now prove that, at principal shell order, the spatial tensor \(C^{(JJ)}_{jm}\) itself cannot carry any nontrivial anisotropic structure beyond \(\delta_{jm}\).
Therefore
\[
C^{(JJ)}_{jm}=\Xi_{JJ}\,\delta_{jm},
\]
for a scalar \(\Xi_{JJ}\) determined only by internal/background contractions and shell projector data.

Hence
\[
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*=\Xi_{JJ}\,|G_*|,
\]
so the last longitudinal microscopic ingredient is reduced to a single scalar internal contraction \(\Xi_{JJ}\).

\section{Background current and Bloch derivative inputs}

The background \(J\)-current has the lowest-order local form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\phi_0,P_0]=m^a(P_0)\,\partial_i\phi_0.
}
\label{eq:CJJ_Jbackground}
\end{equation}
Thus the only explicit spatial index carried by the background source is the gradient index \(i\). :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

On the Bloch side, the principal shell derivative is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{k_j}\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{G';\,G,r}
=
iA\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,\delta_{ij}\,\bigl(t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a\bigr).
}
\label{eq:CJJ_dJ}
\end{equation}
So the derivative insertion contributes only the spatial tensor \(\delta_{ij}\), together with internal matrix data \((t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a)\). :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{Principal-order tensor collapse}

The pure-\(JJ\) Schur kernel is
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\]
Insert \eqref{eq:CJJ_Jbackground} and \eqref{eq:CJJ_dJ}.
At principal shell order, every term contributing to the axial coefficient field contains:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one factor of the background current coefficient \(m^a(P_0)\),
\item one factor of the tangent-shell matrix data \((t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a)\),
\item the shell projector \(\Pi_{S_*}\),
\item the spatial Kronecker tensor \(\delta_{ij}\),
\item and the shell gradient \(\partial_j\phi_0\).
\end{enumerate}

Since no other principal spatial tensor survives the shell restriction, the resulting coefficient field must have the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal A_j^{(JJ)}(x)
=
\Xi_{JJ}\,\partial_j\phi_0(x),
}
\label{eq:CJJ_Ascalar}
\end{equation}
for some scalar \(\Xi_{JJ}\) depending only on internal/background/projector contractions.

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C^{(JJ)}_{jm}=\Xi_{JJ}\,\delta_{jm}.
}
\label{eq:CJJ_Cdelta}
\end{equation}

\section{Definition of the scalar contraction}

At the formal level, \(\Xi_{JJ}\) is the projected internal contraction produced by the \(JJ\)-kernel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}
\propto
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\,
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
m^a(P_0)\,(t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a)
\Big]
\Pi_{S_*},
}
\label{eq:CJJ_Xi_formal}
\end{equation}
where the precise proportionality factor depends on the normalization conventions of the shell basis and Bloch harmonic amplitude \(A\).

The important point is not the overall normalization, but the tensorial collapse:
all principal spatial dependence is already exhausted by \(\delta_{jm}\), so the remaining information is a single scalar internal contraction \(\Xi_{JJ}\).

\section{Contraction with the shell axis}

Now contract with \(\hat n_j\) and \(G_{*,m}\):
\begin{equation}
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*
=
\hat n_j C^{(JJ)}_{jm}G_{*,m}
=
\Xi_{JJ}\,\hat n_j\delta_{jm}G_{*,m}
=
\Xi_{JJ}\,\hat n\cdot G_*.
\label{eq:CJJ_contract}
\end{equation}
Since \(\hat n=G_*/|G_*|\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*
=
\Xi_{JJ}\,|G_*|.
}
\label{eq:CJJ_contract_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the nonvanishing condition
\[
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*\neq 0
\]
is exactly equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:CJJ_Xi_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate Fourier consequence}

The first-shell support theorem then gives
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
=
i(\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*)A_{G_*}
=
i\,\Xi_{JJ}\,|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
\label{eq:CJJ_Ahat_final}
\end{equation}
Therefore, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Xi_{JJ}\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:CJJ_practical}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:CJJ_practical_concl}
\end{equation}

\section{Main theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Scalar reduction of the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal contraction]
In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the principal pure-\(JJ\) axial coefficient tensor satisfies
\[
C^{(JJ)}_{jm}=\Xi_{JJ}\delta_{jm},
\]
with \(\Xi_{JJ}\) determined only by the internal/background contraction of \(m^a(P_0)\), the tangent-shell matrix elements \((t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a)\), and the shell projector data.

Hence
\[
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*=\Xi_{JJ}|G_*|,

so the second microscopic longitudinal ingredient is reduced to the single scalar test
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}\neq 0.
}

Combined with
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\]
this yields
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The background current contributes one gradient \(\partial_i\phi_0\), while the explicit Bloch derivative contributes only \(\delta_{ij}\) at principal shell order.
No other spatial tensor survives the shell projection and the \(Q=G_*\) Bragg restriction.
Therefore the axial coefficient tensor must be proportional to \(\delta_{jm}\).
This proves the tensor collapse
\[
C^{(JJ)}_{jm}=\Xi_{JJ}\delta_{jm}.
\]
The contraction with \(\hat n\) and \(G_*\) then gives
\[
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*=\Xi_{JJ}|G_*|.
\]
The rest follows from the first-shell support theorem and the already established longitudinal witness chain.
\end{proof}

\section{Honest status}

What is now structurally closed is the reduction:
the second microscopic ingredient is no longer a rank-two tensor problem.

What is not yet inserted explicitly is the actual value of \(\Xi_{JJ}\) in the refined locked microscopic basis.

\section{Final Scalar Reduction of the Pure \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} Longitudinal Ingredient}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The last carrier-side longitudinal frontier was reduced to the scalar test

\Xi_{JJ}\neq 0.

We now prove that, in the current canonical locked basis and minimal explicit Class II split, this scalar is nothing but the invariant product
\[
L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel.

So the second microscopic longitudinal ingredient is not a new unknown object.
It is exactly the same invariant that already appears in the canonical reduced witness formula.

\section{Canonical locked basis}

Fix the canonical locked basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0=(1,0,0)^T,
\qquad
u_1=(0,1,0)^T,
\qquad
u_2=(0,0,1)^T.
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_can_basis}
\end{equation}
In this basis the tangent Pauli frame is fixed canonically. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

The background internal selector aligns with the singlet axis:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3}.
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_malign}
\end{equation}
Again, this is part of the canonical locked reduction. 

\section{Canonical decomposition of the \texorpdfstring{$J$}{J}-sector tensor}

The shell-relevant \(J\)-sector tensor decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0)
=
u_\parallel\,\hat n_j\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{b}
+
u_E\,(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
u_O\,(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
\mathcal U^{\mathrm{irr}}_{jr}{}^{b}.
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_Udecomp}
\end{equation}
The coefficient \(u_\parallel\) is exactly the shell-normal \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet amplitude of the \(J\)-sector. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

By the Pauli orthogonality relations, one has the exact projector formula
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\Bigl(
\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\,\mathcal U_j(0)
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_upar_trace}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal U_j(0)\) denotes the \(2\times2\) matrix-valued shell tensor in the reduced tangent space.
The \(E/O\)-channels and the irreducible remainder are annihilated by this projection.

\section{Principal pure-\texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} scalar contraction}

At principal shell order, the axial coefficient tensor has already been shown to collapse to
\[
C^{(JJ)}_{jm}=\Xi_{JJ}\delta_{jm}.
\]
Its origin is the product of:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the background selector \(m^a(P_0)\),
\item the shell-normal \(J\)-tensor coefficient \(u_\parallel\),
\item the universal shell/Bloch normalization factors.
\end{enumerate}

Because \(m^a(P_0)\) is aligned along \(a=3\), only the \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet part of \(\mathcal U\) contributes.
Hence there exists a nonzero scalar normalization \(\mathcal N_{JJ}\) such that

=
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,m_\parallel\,u_\parallel.

\label{eq:XiJJ_factorized}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, using \eqref{eq:XiJJ_upar_trace},

\Xi_{JJ}
=
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,m_\parallel\,
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\Bigl(
\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\,\mathcal U_j(0)
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_tracefinal}
\end{equation}

So \(\Xi_{JJ}\) is exactly the shell-projector trace measuring how strongly the background internal selector \(m_\parallel\) biases the two tangent-shell states along the \(\Sigma_3\) axis.

\section{Minimal explicit canonical split}

In the minimal explicit canonical split one imposes

Thus define the invariant

L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel.

Then
\begin{equation}

\label{eq:XiJJ_Lstar_relation}

\section{Main theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Final scalar reduction]
In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, under the canonical locked basis and the minimal explicit canonical split, the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal scalar ingredient is exactly proportional to the invariant
\[
L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel.

More precisely,

\Xi_{JJ}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
L_*\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:XiJJ_equiv_Lstar}

\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the canonical alignment \eqref{eq:XiJJ_malign}, only the \(a=3\) component of the background selector contributes.
By the shell decomposition \eqref{eq:XiJJ_Udecomp}, only the \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet coefficient \(u_\parallel\) survives the axial shell projector.
Therefore the principal pure-\(JJ\) scalar contraction must factor through the product \(m_\parallel u_\parallel\), up to a nonzero normalization factor \(\mathcal N_{JJ}\).
This gives \eqref{eq:XiJJ_main_relation}, and the equivalence \eqref{eq:XiJJ_equiv_Lstar} is immediate.
\end{proof}

\section{Immediate Fourier consequence}

m_3\neq 0

\section{What \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{L*} measures}

The quantity
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
\]
has a precise physical meaning:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(m_\parallel\) measures how strongly the locked background current selects the internal singlet axis \(a=3\);
\item \(u_\parallel\) measures how strongly the shell-relevant \(J\)-tensor projects onto the longitudinal \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet seed;
\item their product measures the net axial shell-state imbalance seen by the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal projector.
\end{enumerate}

So the final pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal ingredient is exactly the internal axial bias of the background current as read by the shell tangent doublet.

\section{Honest status}

After the present theorem, there is no remaining structural ambiguity on the carrier side.

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\neq 0.

\label{eq:XiJJ_lastpair}

What remains open is only the actual symbolic or numerical extraction of these scalars from the true refined locked Bloch operator.

\section{Final Summary}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal scalar ingredient collapses to the invariant
\[
\boxed{

\qquad
L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\]

Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(m_\parallel\) is the background-current alignment along the internal singlet axis \(a=3\),
\item \(u_\parallel\) is the shell-normal \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet coefficient of the \(J\)-sector tensor,
\item \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\) is the net axial shell-state imbalance seen by the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal projector.
\end{itemize}

Therefore

=

\qquad

\qquad

\[

\Longrightarrow

\Longrightarrow

So the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now reduced completely to the two scalar checks
\[

L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\operatorname{Tr}\!\Bigl(
\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\,\mathcal U_j(0)
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:minexec_Lstar}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the diagonal Pauli basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j)_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j)_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:minexec_Lstar_diag}
\end{equation}

This is the final direct extraction formula.

\section{Step 7: witness reconstruction}

The canonical reduced witness formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:minexec_lambda}
\end{equation}
So, once \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\), the only remaining microscopic issue is whether \(L_*\) vanishes. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Under first-shell dominant intervalley compression, the longitudinal Pauli coefficient is controlled by
\begin{equation}
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Big(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Big),
\label{eq:minexec_m3}
\end{equation}
and in the current canonical branch
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto \alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}.
\]
Therefore the dominant term is proportional to
\[
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}.
\]

\section{Main theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Minimal executable extraction theorem]
In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, fix the explicit enriched carrier basis \eqref{eq:minexec_basis} and the minimal harmonic truncation \eqref{eq:minexec_SN}.

Then the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is completely reduced to the explicit extraction of the two scalars
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)},
}
\label{eq:minexec_main_delta}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\operatorname{Tr}\!\Bigl(
\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\,\mathcal U_j(0)
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:minexec_main_L}
\end{equation}

If, in addition,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|,
}
\label{eq:minexec_main_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:minexec_main_concl}
\end{equation}
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:minexec_ultramin}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The explicit enriched shell carrier basis and projected core block are already fixed in finite form. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}
The longitudinal microscopic invariant in the canonical branch is exactly \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\), and the reduced witness is \(\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\alpha_XL_*I_{\theta'^3}\). :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}
The first-shell intervalley audit compresses the longitudinal channel to the dominant product \(\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}\), up to the explicit harmonic remainder \(R_N\).
Therefore, if the dominant term is nonzero and dominates \(R_N\), then the longitudinal shell coefficient is nonzero, hence \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\).
\end{proof}

\section{What remains open}

After this theorem, nothing conceptual remains on the carrier side.
What remains is only the explicit symbolic or numerical evaluation of:
\[
A_1^{(\pm)},\ A_2^{(\pm)},\qquad
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j)_{11},\ (\hat n^j\mathcal U_j)_{22},\qquad
m_\parallel.
\]

So the final carrier-side longitudinal slot is an ordinary finite matrix/overlap extraction problem.

\section{Final Summary}

The carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now reduced to two explicit finite extractions from the actual refined locked Bloch operator:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\operatorname{Tr}\!\Bigl(
\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\,\mathcal U_j(0)
\Bigr)
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j)_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j)_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\]

Under first-shell dominant intervalley compression, the practical sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\]
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore no structural ambiguity remains on the carrier side.
What remains is only the explicit symbolic or numerical extraction of the finite quantities
\[
A_a^{(\pm)},\qquad
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j)_{11,22},\qquad
m_\parallel.
\]

\section{Minimal Matrix-Element Extraction of \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00} and \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{L*}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The carrier-side longitudinal frontier has already been reduced to two scalar quantities:
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

We now write them in the most concrete minimal form adapted to the explicit enriched shell basis and the first-shell harmonic truncation.

\section{1. Explicit carrier basis and projected core block}

Fix the enriched shell carrier basis
\[
|+,a\rangle:=|G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|-G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2,
\]
so that
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle\}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]
Projecting the shell Hamiltonian gives
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+^{(N)}(p) & B^{(N)}(p)\\
B^{(N)}(p)^\dagger & E_-^{(N)}(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with \(2\times2\) internal blocks. This is the finite carrier block on which all remaining extraction is performed.

\section{2. Minimal harmonic truncation}

In folded Bragg form \(k_*=G_*/2\), choose the first-shell dominant truncation
\[
\mathcal S_N^{\min}=\{0\}\cup \mathcal S_{12}.
\]
Expand the periodic Bloch spinors as
\[
u_a^\pm(x)
=
A_a^{(\pm)}\chi_a
+
\sum_{Q\in \mathcal S_{12}}\sum_{b=1}^2
c_{ab,Q}^{(\pm)}\,e^{iQ\cdot x}\chi_b.
\]

The zero-mode amplitudes are therefore exactly
\[
A_a^{(+)}=\langle \chi_a, P_0 u_a^+\rangle,
\qquad
A_a^{(-)}=\langle \chi_a, P_0 u_a^-\rangle,
\]
where \(P_0\) denotes projection to the \(G=0\) harmonic inside the chosen truncation.

\section{3. Explicit formula for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

The dominant intervalley Bloch asymmetry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:delta00_final_exec}
\end{equation}

So \(\Delta_{00}\) is read directly from the zero-harmonic components of the two carrier channels.

\section{4. Explicit formula for \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

Let \(\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)\) denote the \(Q=G_*\) shell-relevant \(J\)-tensor in the intervalley channel.
Project it to the reduced internal doublet:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_j(0)
:=
\bigl(\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)\bigr)_{a,b=1}^2,
\qquad
\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:Uj_matrix_final_exec}
\end{equation}

Then the shell-normal singlet coefficient is extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\,\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:upar_trace_final_exec}
\end{equation}

If \(\Sigma_3=\mathrm{diag}(1,-1)\) in the chosen internal basis, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:upar_diag_final_exec}
\end{equation}

So \(u_\parallel\) is literally the diagonal asymmetry of the shell-normal projected \(J\)-block.

\section{5. Explicit formula for \texorpdfstring{$m_\parallel$}{m_parallel}}

In the canonical locked frame,
\[
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel = m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:mpar_final_exec}
\end{equation}

No further reduction is needed: it is simply the \(a=3\) component of the background-current selector in the canonical basis.

\section{6. Final scalar invariant}

Thus the unresolved longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\,\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_final_exec}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the diagonal Pauli basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Lstar_diag_final_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Witness reconstruction}

In the current canonical branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_final_exec}
\end{equation}

Under first-shell dominant intervalley compression, the longitudinal shell audit is controlled by the dominant product
\[
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*},
\]
up to the explicit remainder \(R_N\).
Therefore the practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:dominant_nonzero_final_exec}
\end{equation}
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:ultramin_nonzero_final_exec}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section{8. Practical finite protocol}

So the actual computation is now:

\begin{enumerate}
\item diagonalize or project the refined locked Bloch operator onto the explicit carrier basis \((|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle)\);
\item read the zero-harmonic amplitudes \(A_a^{(\pm)}\) and compute \(\Delta_{00}\);
\item form the \(2\times2\) reduced \(J\)-matrix \(\mathcal U_j(0)\) and compute \(u_\parallel\) by \eqref{eq:upar_trace_final_exec};
\item read \(m_\parallel=m^3(P_0)\);
\item form \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\);
\item test \eqref{eq:dominant_nonzero_final_exec}.
\end{enumerate}

This is the final executable longitudinal audit.

\section{Final Summary}

The carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now completely reduced to the explicit extraction of two scalars from the actual refined locked Bloch operator:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\,\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr)
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\]

Under first-shell dominant intervalley compression, the practical sufficient condition is

\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\]

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\]

So the carrier-side longitudinal slot is no longer a conceptual or structural problem.
It is a finite matrix/overlap extraction problem on the explicit enriched shell carrier block.

\section{Constant-Envelope Minimal Extraction Formulas}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

In the constant-envelope branch, the enriched shell basis is already explicit:
\[
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
\]

So the remaining longitudinal audit is not an abstract transport-space problem anymore.
It is a finite \(4\times4\) projected Bloch-matrix problem on this basis.

\section{1. Minimal carrier basis}

Fix the shell-pair basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\mathrm{core}}
=
(\Psi_{+,1},\Psi_{+,2},\Psi_{-,1},\Psi_{-,2}),
}
\label{eq:ce_basis}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\label{eq:ce_basis_explicit}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the explicit enriched shell basis of the current program. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2} :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{2. Projected core block}

On \(\mathcal B_{\mathrm{core}}\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
P_D^{(N)}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)P_D^{(N)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:ce_core_block}
\end{equation}
where \(E_\pm(p),B(p)\in\mathrm{Mat}_{2\times2}(\mathbb C)\). Its constant and linear parts are already fixed by
\begin{align}
E_\pm(p)&=E_\pm(0)+p_i\,\partial_{p_i}E_\pm(0)+O(|p|^2),\\
B(p)&=B(0)+p_i\,\partial_{p_i}B(0)+O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:ce_expand}
\end{align}
The longitudinal core slope is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac14\Tr\!\left[
\partial_{p_\parallel}(E_+(p)-E_-(p))
\right]_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:ce_vpar}
\end{equation}
This finite block extraction is exactly the canonical core audit. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\section{3. Minimal formula for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

In the constant-envelope branch, the zero-harmonic vectors are already the carrier coefficients in the internal basis \(\{\xi_1,\xi_2\}\).
Write the low carrier coefficients in each valley as
\begin{equation}
\eta_+ =
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(+)}\\
A_2^{(+)}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\eta_- =
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(-)}\\
A_2^{(-)}
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:ce_eta_pm}
\end{equation}
where \(\eta_\pm\) are the normalized internal coefficient vectors of the selected low shell modes in the \(+\) and \(-\) valley sectors.

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:ce_delta00}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger \Sigma_3 \eta_-,
\qquad
\Sigma_3=\mathrm{diag}(1,-1).
}
\label{eq:ce_delta00_sigma3}
\end{equation}

So \(\Delta_{00}\) is simply the \(\Sigma_3\)-weighted overlap of the two valley coefficient vectors.

\section{4. Minimal formula for \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

Define the reduced \(J\)-matrix on the carrier by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\bigl(\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)\bigr)_{a,b=1}^2,
\qquad
\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:ce_Uj}
\end{equation}

Then the shell-normal longitudinal singlet coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:ce_upar_trace}
\end{equation}

In the diagonal Pauli basis this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:ce_upar_diag}
\end{equation}

So \(u_\parallel\) is literally the shell-normal diagonal asymmetry of the reduced \(J\)-block.

\section{5. Minimal formula for \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{L*}}

In the canonical locked frame,
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
\label{eq:ce_mpar}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Tr\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:ce_Lstar}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:ce_Lstar_diag}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Final witness reconstruction}

The canonical longitudinal witness formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:ce_lambda}
\end{equation}
In the first-shell dominant intervalley compression, the leading longitudinal term is proportional to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}.

\label{eq:ce_leading_product}
\end{equation}
Hence the practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.

\label{eq:ce_sufficient}
\end{equation}
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:ce_ultramin}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Final executable audit}

The actual carrier-side longitudinal audit is now:

\begin{enumerate}
\item build the \(4\times4\) projected core block \(H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)\) on the basis \eqref{eq:ce_basis};
\item extract the two valley internal coefficient vectors \(\eta_\pm\) and compute
\[
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-;

\item compute the reduced shell-relevant \(J\)-matrix \(\mathcal U_j(0)\);

u_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0));

\item compute \(m_\parallel=m^3(P_0)\);
\item form \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\);
\item test \eqref{eq:ce_sufficient}.
\end{enumerate}

This is the final minimal executable protocol.

\section{Final Summary}

In the constant-envelope minimal truncation, the remaining carrier-side longitudinal frontier is reduced to two explicit scalars:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
\qquad
L_*=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Tr(\Sigma_3\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)).

Here:

\eta_\pm=

\boxed{

\qquad

\qquad

So no structural ambiguity remains on the carrier side.

\section{Direct Matrix-Element Extraction of the Two Remaining Longitudinal Scalars}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

At the present stage, the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is not an abstract existence question anymore.
It is the explicit extraction of two finite scalars from the projected refined locked Bloch operator:

\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

We now write both directly as matrix elements of the projected shell block.

\section{1. Explicit enriched shell carrier basis}

Fix the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\]
Use the explicit enriched shell carrier basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|+,a\rangle:=|G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|-G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2,
}
\label{eq:elem_basis}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle\}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]
This is exactly the explicit enriched shell carrier block already fixed in the notes. 

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
P_D^{(N)}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)P_D^{(N)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:elem_core}
\end{equation}
with \(2\times2\) internal blocks \(E_\pm(p),B(p)\). This is the finite projected carrier Hamiltonian. 

\section{2. Extraction of the valley coefficient vectors}

At \(p=0\), diagonalize the two \(2\times2\) valley blocks:
\begin{equation}
E_+(0)\,\eta_+ = \varepsilon_+\,\eta_+,
\qquad
E_-(0)\,\eta_- = \varepsilon_-\,\eta_-,
\qquad
\|\eta_\pm\|=1,
\label{eq:elem_etaeig}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\eta_+=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(+)}\\
A_2^{(+)}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\eta_-=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(-)}\\
A_2^{(-)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
So the coefficients \(A_a^{(\pm)}\) are literally the components of the normalized low internal eigenvectors of the two \(2\times2\) valley blocks in the chosen carrier basis.

Therefore the dominant Bloch asymmetry scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}
=
\eta_+^\dagger \Sigma_3 \eta_-,
\qquad
\Sigma_3=\mathrm{diag}(1,-1).
}
\label{eq:elem_Delta}
\end{equation}

So \(\Delta_{00}\) is the \(\Sigma_3\)-weighted overlap between the two normalized valley eigenvectors.

\section{3. Extraction of the reduced \(J\)-matrix}

Let \(\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)\) be the shell-relevant \(Q=G_*\) \(J\)-kernel in the intervalley channel.
Project it to the carrier:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_j(0)
:=
P_-\,\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)\,P_+\Big|_{\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}},
}
\label{eq:elem_Udef}
\end{equation}
where \(P_+\) projects to the \(+\)-valley internal carrier and \(P_-\) to the \(-\)-valley internal carrier.

In matrix-element form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
a,b=1,2.
}
\label{eq:elem_Uab}
\end{equation}
